Refuting the False Premise Against Takwin's Eternity
Nasafi identifies and refutes a false premise in the opponents' argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the false premise that eternal takwin implies an eternal world, and why this refutation targets the opponents' reasoning rather than the status of takwin itself.

Core Idea
A false premise can invalidate an argument even if its conclusion seems plausible.

Nasafi now engages with a specific objection from opponents (ahl al-batin) who argue that if takwin is eternal, then the world must also be eternal. Since the world is temporally originated, they conclude that takwin cannot be eternal. This passage exposes the false premise underlying this argument and shows why it fails.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the structure: Nasafi first states a premise, then applies evidence, then draws a conclusion.
2
Identify the false premise
Locate the statement that Nasafi calls a false premise. It is the claim that 'the statement that takwin is eternal leads to the statement that the world is eternal'.
This premise is the key link that the opponents rely on.
3
Reflect on the refutation
Understand that Nasafi does not here prove that takwin is or is not eternal. He only shows that the opponents' argument is invalid because their premise is false. The evidence for the world's temporality does not directly relate to takwin's eternity; it only shows that the premise leads to a false conclusion.
This is a logical refutation, not a positive proof about takwin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة كاذبة للخصوم فنقول : أطبق أهل الباطن على مقدمة كاذبة وهي أن القول بقدم التكوين يؤدي إلى القول بقدم العالم، وقد قامت الدلالة على حدوثه، فكان القول بما يؤدي إلى قدمه باطلا، فكان القول بقدم التكوين باطلا.
A false premise of the opponents: We say: The adherents of esoteric interpretation (ahl al-batin) have unanimously agreed upon a false premise, namely that the statement that takwin is eternal leads to the statement that the world is eternal, while the evidence for its temporal origination has been established. So the statement that leads to its eternity is false, and thus the statement that takwin is eternal is false.
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes a false premise held by the opponents (ahl al-batin). The premise is that if takwin is eternal, then the world must also be eternal. Since the world is proven to be temporally originated (hadith), the premise that leads to its eternity is false, and therefore the claim that takwin is eternal is false. This is a proof by contradiction.

Key Terms
مقدمة كاذبة
أهل الباطن
التكوين
العالم
القدم
الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage proves that takwin is not eternal.
Correction: Nasafi only refutes the opponents' argument that takwin's eternity implies the world's eternity. He does not here make a positive claim about takwin's status.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the false premise that leads to the conclusion that takwin's eternity implies the world's eternity?
A) The world is eternal.
B) Takwin is the same as the world.
C) The statement that takwin is eternal leads to the statement that the world is eternal.
D) The world is temporally originated.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the opponents' argument by exposing their false premise that takwin's eternity necessitates the world's eternity, but this does not settle the actual status of takwin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about Allah that was built on a false premise—something you assumed without checking the evidence? What would it take for you to expose and abandon that premise today?
?
This lesson shows that even a logical argument can crumble if its foundation is false. Are you willing to question the foundations of your own understanding of Allah's attributes, even if it feels uncomfortable? What step can you take this week to dig deeper into a belief you hold?
?
The opponents clung to a false premise. Is there any belief about Allah you cling to simply because it feels ancient or common, rather than because it is true? Could you be using a false premise to protect a comfortable position?

Sectarian Views on Takwin and Mukawwan
Nasafi catalogues the positions of various sects on takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main positions of various Islamic theological schools regarding the relationship between the divine attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) and the created thing (mukawwan).

Core Idea
Takwin's identity or distinction from creation divides Islamic sects.

Nasafi presents a fascinating map of sectarian opinions on whether God's act of creating is identical to the created thing or distinct from it. This seemingly technical distinction has profound implications for how we understand divine attributes and their relation to creation. Let's explore the spectrum of views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the different groups named.
Focus on the flow: common ground, then divergence.
2
Identify the two main camps
Find the first group (majority Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, Kullabiyya, Ash'ariyya, Qalanisiyya) who say takwin is identical to mukawwan. Then find the second group (Abu al-Hudhayl, Bishr, Mu'ammar, Ibn al-Rawandi, Karramiyya) who say takwin is a distinct meaning.
3
Spot the unique position
Notice Hisham ibn al-Hakam's view: he says takwin is neither the mukawwan nor other than it. Why? Because takwin is an attribute, and attributes for him are not describable.
Hisham's view is nuanced—he refuses both descriptions.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why would theologians care about this distinction? How does it relate to the denial of eternal attributes by Mu'tazila and Najjariyya?
This classification shows how different schools conceptualize divine action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن المعتزلة بأسرهم ، والنجارية بأجمعهم ، يرون قيام صفة ما أي صفة كانت بذات القديم محالا فقالوا بامتناع قيام التكوين بذات الله تعالى ثم إنهم تفرقوا فيما بينهم، واختلفوا اختلافا فاحشا، فذهب عامة المعتزلة والنجارية ومتكلمو أهل الحديث كالكلابية والأشعرية و القلانسية أن التكوين ليس بمعنى غير المكون بل هو عين المكون أي شيء كان المكون. وذهب أبو الهذيل العلاف وبشر بن المعتمر ومعمر من رؤساء المعتزلة وابن الراوندي وهشام بن الحكم والكرامية بأجمعهم، أن التكوين معنى وراء المكون. غير أن هؤلاء كلهم ، يقولون: هو غير المكون، وهشام بن الحكم يقول: لا هو المكون ولا غيره. وإنما نشأ الاختلاف بينهم لأن هشاما يقول: التكوين صفة والصفة عنده لا توصف فلم يصف التكوين بأنه غير المكون.
Then indeed the Mu'tazila entirely and the Najjariyya altogether consider the subsistence of any attribute whatsoever in the essence of the Eternal impossible, so they said that it is impossible for takwin to subsist in the essence of Allah the Exalted. Then they diverged among themselves and differed excessively. The majority of the Mu'tazila, the Najjariyya, and the speculative theologians of the People of Hadith such as the Kullabiyya, Ash'ariyya, and Qalanisiyya held that takwin does not mean something other than the mukawwan (the thing brought into existence), rather it is identical to the mukawwan, whatever the mukawwan may be. And Abu al-Hudhayl al-'Allaf, Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir, and Mu'ammar among the leaders of the Mu'tazila, and Ibn al-Rawandi, Hisham ibn al-Hakam, and the Karramiyya in their entirety held that takwin is a meaning beyond the mukawwan. However, all of these say it is other than the mukawwan, while Hisham ibn al-Hakam says: it is neither the mukawwan nor other than it. The dispute among them arose only because Hisham says: takwin is an attribute, and an attribute according to him is not describable, so he did not describe takwin as being other than the mukawwan.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage classifies the positions of various sects on the relationship between takwin and mukawwan. It begins by noting that the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya consider it impossible for any attribute to subsist in God's essence, hence they deny that takwin is an attribute subsisting in God. Then it details their disagreement: the majority of Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, Kullabiyya, Ash'ariyya, and Qalanisiyya hold that takwin is identical to the mukawwan. Another group including Abu al-Hudhayl, Bishr, Mu'ammar, Ibn al-Rawandi, Hisham ibn al-Hakam, and the Karramiyya hold that takwin is a meaning distinct from the mukawwan. However, Hisham has a unique view that it is neither the same nor different, because he considers it an attribute and attributes for him are not themselves described.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Hisham's view is just a third distinct position between identity and difference.
Correction: Hisham does not assert a third relationship; rather, he refuses to describe takwin as either identical or distinct because for him attributes are not themselves describable. He denies both descriptions.

Checkpoint
How does Hisham ibn al-Hakam's view on the relationship between takwin and mukawwan differ from the other groups?
A) He says takwin is identical to mukawwan.
B) He says takwin is a distinct meaning.
C) He says it is neither the same nor different.
D) He denies takwin altogether.

Key Takeaway
Islamic theologians disagreed on whether God's act of creating (takwin) is identical to the created thing (mukawwan), with most asserting identity while a minority argued for distinction, and Hisham ibn al-Hakam uniquely refusing to describe it as either.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see the diversity of opinions among early Muslim scholars on something as fundamental as how God creates, does your heart feel a restless desire to know the truth? Or are you content to follow without understanding? Will you take steps to study these matters deeper?
?
The passage shows that even within the same school, scholars disagreed. Do you ever cling to your own theological views as if they are beyond question? How might this lesson's reminder of scholarly disagreement humble you before God?
?
Hisham ibn al-Hakam refused to describe takwin as 'other than' the mukawwan because of his theory of attributes. Have you ever avoided making a claim about God because you felt it was beyond your knowledge? Is that reluctance a sign of piety or negligence? What will you do?

Refuting the Batiniyya's False Premise on Takwin
Refutation of the Batiniyya's false premise linking takwin's eternity to the world's eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Batiniyya's argument linking takwin's eternity to the world's eternity is based on a false premise and how it is refuted.

Core Idea
A false premise invalidates any conclusion, even if the conclusion seems plausible.

The Batiniyya (esotericists) claimed that affirming the eternity of the divine attribute takwin (bringing into existence) necessarily implies the eternity of the world. They thought that since the world is temporally originated, takwin cannot be eternal. However, their reasoning rests on an unproven causal link. This lesson examines the author's concise refutation of that false premise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a concise, logical style.
2
Identify the false premise
Find the premise that the Batiniyya hold. Note how the author describes it as 'false' (kadhiba).
The premise is the conditional: if takwin is eternal, then the world is eternal.
3
Understand why it is false
The author points out that the world's temporality is already proven. Therefore, any premise that leads to eternity must be false. But why is the premise itself false? Because it assumes an unwarranted link between the attribute and its effect.
This step requires seeing the logical flaw beyond the author's explicit words.
4
Trace the logical flow
The argument goes: premise (false) → proof (world is temporal) → conclusion (statement leading to eternity is false). Follow the chain.
Use the guided breakdown and learning flow to visualise.
5
Reflect on the importance
Consider why it matters to identify false premises in theological arguments. How does this strengthen the doctrine of divine attributes?
This connects to the broader kalam method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنقول : أطبق أهل الباطن على مقدمة كاذبة وهي أن القول بقدم التكوين يؤدي إلى القول بقدم العالم، وقد قامت الدلالة على حدوثه، فكان القول بما يؤدي إلى قدمه باطلا، فكان القول بقدم التكوين باطلا.
We say: The batiniyya have unanimously agreed upon a false premise, namely that the statement that takwin is eternal leads to the statement that the world is eternal, while the proof has been established for its temporality, so the statement that leads to its eternity is false, so the statement that takwin is eternal is false.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of the batiniyya (esotericists) who argue that holding takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) to be eternal implies the eternity of the world. The author points out that they rely on a false premise (muqaddima kadhiba). The proof (dalala) has already been established that the world is temporally originated (hadith). Therefore, any line of thought that leads to the world being eternal is invalid. Consequently, the claim that takwin is eternal is also invalid. The argument is straightforward: the premise is false, so the conclusion is rejected.

Key Terms
أهل الباطن
مقدمة كاذبة
التكوين
قدم
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Batiniyya's argument is sound because if takwin is eternal, what it produces (the world) would also be eternal.
Correction: But the argument fails because it assumes a necessary causal link between the attribute and its effect, whereas in kalam, the attribute of takwin is eternal but its effect (the world) is brought into existence in time.

Checkpoint
What is the false premise used by the batiniyya?
A) The world is eternal.
B) Saying takwin is eternal leads to saying the world is eternal.
C) The world is created.
D) Takwin is not an attribute.

Key Takeaway
The Batiniyya's refutation hinges on exposing a false premise; the eternity of takwin does not necessitate the eternity of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you accepted a conclusion about your faith because it seemed logically necessary, without questioning whether the premise was actually true? What is one belief you hold that might be based on an unexamined premise?
?
The Batiniyya's error was assuming that an eternal attribute must produce an eternal effect. Are there areas in your life where you assume that because God is eternal, His actions or decrees must fit your expectations of how eternity works? How might this assumption lead you to a false conclusion about Him?
?
If you discovered that a deeply held belief about Allah was built on a false premise, would you have the courage to abandon it, even if it felt comfortable? What specific step can you take this week to test one of your theological assumptions against the Quran and Sunnah?

Mu'tazila and Najjariyya on Takwin: Identity or Distinct Meaning?
Reports sectarian agreement and disagreement on takwin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key disagreement among Mu'tazila and Najjariyya about whether takwin (bringing into existence) is identical to the created thing or a distinct meaning, including Hisham b. al-Hakam's unique position.

Core Idea
Even those who deny attributes in God split on what takwin actually is.

This passage reveals that the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya, despite sharing the principle that no attribute can subsist in God, fell into serious disagreement over the nature of takwin. The author reports two main camps and a nuanced third position, showing that the debate over divine attributes is far from monolithic.

Guided Path
1
Understand the shared principle
Both Mu'tazila and Najjariyya agree that no attribute can subsist in God's essence; thus they deny that takwin subsists in God.
This is the common ground before the split.
2
Identify the first group: takwin identical to mukawwan
The majority of Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Ahl al-Hadith mutakallimun hold that takwin is not a separate meaning but identical to the created thing (mukawwan).
3
Identify the second group: takwin as a distinct meaning
Abu Hudhayl, Bishr, Ma'mar, Ibn al-Rawandi, Hisham b. al-Hakam, and the Karramiyya hold that takwin is a meaning beyond the mukawwan.
4
Examine Hisham b. al-Hakam's nuance
Hisham says takwin is neither the mukawwan nor other than it, because he refrains from describing the attribute itself.
This highlights a deeper disagreement about whether attributes can be described.
5
Reflect on the source of difference
The split ultimately stems from whether one can describe an attribute (sifa) as 'other than' something; Hisham does not allow describing attributes, so he takes a middle position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن المعتزلة بأسرهم ، والنجارية بأجمعهم ، يرون قيام صفة ما أي صفة كانت بذات القديم محالا فقالوا بامتناع قيام التكوين بذات الله تعالى ثم إنهم تفرقوا فيما بينهم، واختلفوا اختلافا فاحشا، فذهب عامة المعتزلة والنجارية ومتكلمو أهل الحديث كالكلابية والأشعرية و القلانسية أن التكوين ليس بمعنى غير المكون بل هو عين المكوَّن أي شيء كان المكون. وذهب أبو الهذيل العلاف وبشر بن المعتمر ومعمر من رؤساء المعتزلة وابن الراوندي وهشام بن الحكم والكرامية بأجمعهم، أن التكوين معنى وراء المكون. غير أن هؤلاء كلهم ، يقولون: هو غير المكون، وهشام بن الحكم يقول: لا هو المكون ولا غيره. وإنما نشأ الاختلاف بينهم لأن هشاما يقول: التكوين صفة والصفة عنده لا توصف فلم يصف التكوين بأنه غير المكون. وغيره من المتكلمين يجوزون وصف الصفة، فوصفوا التكوين بأنه غير المكون.
Then indeed the Mu'tazila entirely, and the Najjariyya completely, hold that the subsistence of any attribute whatsoever in the essence of the Eternal is impossible, so they said: the subsistence of takwin in the essence of God is impossible. Then they diverged among themselves and differed greatly. The majority of the Mu'tazila, the Najjariyya, and the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith such as the Kullabiyya, Ash'ariyya, and Qalanisiyya held that takwin is not a meaning other than the mukawwan, but rather it is identical to the mukawwan whatever the mukawwan may be. And Abu Hudhayl al-'Allaf, Bishr b. al-Mu'tamir, Ma'mar from among the leaders of the Mu'tazila, Ibn al-Rawandi, Hisham b. al-Hakam, and the Karramiyya entirely held that takwin is a meaning beyond the mukawwan. However, all of these say it is other than the mukawwan, while Hisham b. al-Hakam says: it is neither the mukawwan nor other than it. The difference arose among them because Hisham says: takwin is an attribute, and according to him the attribute is not described, so he did not describe takwin as other than the mukawwan. And others among the mutakallimun allow describing the attribute, so they described takwin as other than the mukawwan.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage begins by stating a common principle held by the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya: that no attribute can subsist in the essence of God (qiyam sifat bi-dhat al-Qadim muhal). Therefore, they deny that takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) subsists in God. However, they disagree among themselves about what takwin actually is. The author then lists two main groups. The first group, comprising the majority of Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith (like Kullabiyya, Ash'ariyya, Qalanisiyya), hold that takwin is not a separate meaning (ma'na) from the thing created (mukawwan), but rather it is identical to it. The second group, including Abu Hudhayl, Bishr, Ma'mar, Ibn al-Rawandi, Hisham b. al-Hakam, and the Karramiyya, hold that takwin is a meaning distinct from the mukawwan. Within this group, Hisham b. al-Hakam has a nuanced position: he says takwin is neither the mukawwan nor other than it, because he does not describe the attribute itself. The author explains that Hisham's principle is that an attribute (sifa) is not described (as being 'other than' something), so he refrains from describing takwin as 'other than the mukawwan'. Other mutakallimun allow describing attributes, so they describe takwin as 'other than'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all who deny attributes subsisting in God agree on the nature of takwin.
Correction: The passage shows that despite agreeing on the impossibility of attribute subsistence, the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya split into multiple positions on takwin: some say it is identical to the created thing, others say it is distinct, and Hisham b. al-Hakam says it is neither.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group holds that takwin is identical to the mukawwan?
A) The Karramiyya
B) Abu Hudhayl and his followers
C) The majority of Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Ahl al-Hadith mutakallimun
D) Hisham b. al-Hakam

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila and Najjariyya agreed on denying attribute subsistence in God but disagreed on the nature of takwin, with some equating it to creation and others seeing it as distinct, while Hisham b. al-Hakam refused to describe the attribute at all.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn that scholars—even those who agree on a fundamental principle like the denial of attributes—differ radically on its implications, how does that challenge your own tendency to be dogmatic about theological details? Can you identify an area where you might be holding a position without fully understanding the underlying principles?
?
The second camp described takwin as 'other than' the mukawwan, but Hisham refused to describe the attribute at all. Is there an area of your faith where you have added descriptions that Allah has not given for Himself? How can you ensure that your statements about Allah's attributes are precisely what He revealed?
?
If even the Mu'tazila, who are often seen as a unified group, split into camps on a core issue like takwin, what does that say about the humility needed when studying aqeedah? Are you willing to revise your own views when confronted with evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, even if it means leaving a position you were taught?

Disagreements on the Locus of Takwin
Survey of opinions on the locus of takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various opinions among early theologians regarding where the attribute of takwin subsists, and why each position was held.

Core Idea
Takwin's locus is disputed: some say it is self-subsistent, others in the created, others in God's essence.

In the previous lesson, it was established that some theologians consider takwin a distinct attribute from the mukawwan. Now, the author surveys the different positions on where this attribute subsists—whether it has a locus (mahall) or not, and if so, what that locus is. This passage presents five distinct views, each with its own reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a very concise style here, listing each opinion with its rationale.
2
Identify the five opinions
List each theologian or group mentioned and their specific view on the locus of takwin. The passage covers Ibn al-Rawandi, Bishr b. al-Mu'tamir, Abu Hudhayl, some authors of articles, and the Karramiyya. Also note Hisham's position is left unknown.
3
Understand each argument
For each opinion, find the reasoning given. For example, Bishr argues by analogy with capacity before the act. Abu Hudhayl argues from the impossibility of self-subsistence. The ‘authors of articles’ distinguish between ordinary speech and the command 'Be'. The Karramiyya hold that God's essence can be a locus.
Pay attention to how each argument connects to other theological principles.
4
Note the author's stance
Observe the author's exclamation 'Exalted is God above what the wrongdoers say' in response to the Karramiyya view. This shows the author's rejection of that position.
The author does not explicitly reject the other views, but his silence may indicate acceptance or lack of strong objection.
5
Reflect on the diversity
Consider why such disagreements arise in theology. What underlying assumptions about God's attributes and their relationship to creation lead to these different positions?
This connects to broader themes in kalam about divine simplicity and temporality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلفوا فيما بينهم في محل التكوين. فزعم ابن الراوندي أنه قائم لا في محل، وما روي عن بشر بن المعتمر أنه كان يقول: أن التكوين قبل المكون إذ لو لم يكن قبله لبطل كون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل فوجب أن يكون التكوين قائما لا في محل عنده أيضا كما هو مذهب ابن الراوندي. وما روي عن أبي الهذيل أن التكوين يوجد مع المكون لاستحالة قيامه بنفسه يوجب أن يقوم بالمكون. وقد روي عن بعض أهل المقالات أنه كان يقول : إن جميع كلام الله حادث في محل، إلا خطاب كن، فإنه حادث لا في محل. يوجب أن يكون التكوين عنده أيضا حادثا لا في محل، إذ التكوين عنده ليس إلا خطاب "كن". وزعمت الكرامية بأسرهم أن التكوين حادث قائم بذات الله تعالى وأن ذاته محل الحوادث. تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرا - ولم أقف على مذهب هشام في هذا أنه حادث لا في محل أم في ذات الله تعالى.
Then they disagreed among themselves about the locus of takwin. Ibn al-Rawandi claimed that it subsists without a locus. And it was reported from Bishr b. al-Mu'tamir that he used to say: takwin is before the mukawwan, for if it were not before it, the validity of capacity before the act would be nullified, so it is necessary that takwin subsist without a locus according to him as well, as is the doctrine of Ibn al-Rawandi. And it was reported from Abu Hudhayl that takwin exists with the mukawwan, because it is impossible for it to subsist by itself, so it must subsist in the mukawwan. And it was reported from some of the authors of articles (ahl al-maqalat) that he used to say: all speech of God is created in a locus, except the address 'Be', for it is created without a locus. This necessitates that takwin according to him is also created without a locus, since takwin in his view is nothing but the address 'Be'. And the Karramiyya entirely claimed that takwin is created and subsists in the essence of God, and that His essence is the locus of temporal events. Exalted is God above what the wrongdoers say, with great exaltation. And I have not come across the doctrine of Hisham in this regard: whether it is created without a locus or in the essence of God.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage surveys the various opinions among those who hold takwin to be a distinct meaning from the mukawwan, regarding its locus (mahall). Ibn al-Rawandi claimed takwin subsists without a locus (qa'im la fi mahall). Bishr b. al-Mu'tamir also held that takwin is prior to the mukawwan, arguing by analogy with the capacity (istita'a) before the act; if takwin were not prior, the principle of capacity before the act would be invalid. Therefore, takwin must be self-subsistent without a locus. Abu Hudhayl, on the other hand, held that takwin exists simultaneously with the mukawwan, because it cannot subsist by itself, so it must inhere in the mukawwan. A different view, attributed to some authors of theological articles, distinguishes between ordinary divine speech (which is created in a locus) and the command 'Be' (kun), which is created without a locus. Since takwin is identified with 'Be', it too is created without a locus. Finally, the Karramiyya held that takwin is created (hadith) and subsists in God's essence, meaning that God's essence itself becomes the locus of temporal events (mahall al-hawadith). The author exclaims 'Exalted is God above what the wrongdoers say' in refutation of this view. He also notes that he has not found the position of Hisham b. al-Hakam on this particular issue.

Key Terms
محل التكوين
قائم لا في محل
قبل المكون
مع المكون
خطاب كن
الكرامية
ذات الله محل الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all who affirm takwin as a distinct attribute agree on its locus.
Correction: This passage shows sharp disagreement: some say it is self-subsistent, others that it inheres in the created, and others that it inheres in God's essence.

Checkpoint
Which group held that takwin is created and subsists in God's essence?
A) Ibn al-Rawandi
B) Abu Hudhayl
C) The Karramiyya
D) The author of 'all speech of God is created in a locus'

Key Takeaway
The locus of takwin was a point of disagreement among early theologians, with views ranging from self-subsistence to inherence in God's essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read five different theological opinions on where takwin resides. Each scholar claimed to base his view on reason and revelation. How do you approach theological disagreements? Are you genuinely seeking the truth, or do you follow a scholar or school out of habit? What would it take for you to change your position if evidence pointed elsewhere? Commit today to studying the proofs, not just the labels.
?
The Karamiyya claimed that God's essence is a locus of temporal events, which the author strongly rejects as 'what the wrongdoers say' (ta'ala Allah 'amma yaqulu al-zalimun). Have you ever held a belief about God that later turned out to be inconsistent with His transcendence? How did you respond? Are you truly open to correction, even when it challenges a view you have held for a long time? Make a specific intention to re-examine one of your current beliefs about God in light of the Qur'an and Sunnah.
?
The author notes that he has not come across Hisham's position, leaving it unknown. Are you comfortable with theological uncertainty? When you encounter a question for which you have no clear answer, do you search diligently, or do you simply adopt the view of your community? Reflect on one area of 'aqidah where you are uncertain—commit to learning the evidence before forming a firm conclusion.

The Claim: Takwin Is Originated but Not Created by God
Reports a sectarian view that takwin is hadith without being muhdath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction some theologians made between 'originated' (hadith) and 'brought into existence' (muhdath) regarding the attribute of takwin.

Core Idea
They claimed takwin is temporal yet not caused by God—a paradoxical self-origination.

This lesson examines a controversial theological position that attempts to separate temporal origination from divine causation. The passage presents the view that takwin occurs without being brought into existence by Allah, challenging the usual link between temporality and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the key terms: حادث and محدث.
2
Identify the distinction
The passage distinguishes between 'originated' (hadith) and 'brought into existence' (muhdath). Find how they define muhdath.
They define muhdath as something whose occurrence is connected to bringing-into-existence (ihdath).
3
Understand the claim
They claim takwin is originated but its origination is not connected to any act of bringing-into-existence. Ask yourself: what does this imply about takwin's cause?
This seems to make takwin self-originating.
4
Recognize the problem
Consider why this position is problematic from a Sunni perspective. The commentary hints at the absurdity.
This sets up the next lesson on Ma'mar's alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن هؤلاء الذين يقولون بحدوث التكوين الذي هو معنى وراء المكون يقولون: حدث هو لا بإحداث الله تعالى ويقولون : إنه حادث وليس بمحدث إذ المحدث ما تعلق وجوه بالإحداث، وهو لم يتعلق حدوثه بالإحداث، وقال معمر : إن التكوين حدث بتكوين ثان، والثاني بتكوين ثالث، والثالث برابع كذا إلى ما لا يتناهى.
Then indeed those who say that takwin is originated, which is a meaning beyond the mukawwan, say: it occurred not by the bringing-into-existence of God, and they say: it is originated (hadith) and not brought-into-existence (muhdath), because that which is brought-into-existence is what is connected to bringing-into-existence, and its origination is not connected to bringing-into-existence. And Ma'mar said: takwin occurred by a second takwin, and the second by a third takwin, and the third by a fourth, and so on ad infinitum.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage addresses the paradoxical position of those who affirm that takwin is temporally originated (hadith) but deny that it is brought into existence by God (muhdath). They distinguish between 'hadith' (temporal) and 'muhdath' (created/effected by an agent). For them, something is muhdath only if its coming into existence is connected to an act of bringing-into-existence (ihdath). But they claim that takwin's own origination is not connected to any such act. This seems to make takwin a self-originating temporal entity, which is problematic. The author then reports Ma'mar's view, which attempts to avoid this by positing an infinite regress: takwin is brought about by a second takwin, that by a third, and so on without end. This, of course, leads to an infinite chain, which is also problematic from a theological standpoint. The passage ends without explicit refutation, but the absurdity of infinite regress is implied.

Key Terms
حادث
محدث
إحداث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if something is temporal, it must be created by God; but this group denies that link specifically for takwin.
Correction: The passage shows a group that separates 'temporal' from 'created by God' for takwin, arguing it is hadith but not muhdath.

Checkpoint
According to the view reported, what distinguishes a muhdath from a mere hadith?
A) A muhdath is eternal
B) A muhdath is connected to bringing-into-existence
C) A muhdath is not temporal
D) A muhdath is self-caused

Key Takeaway
Some theologians claimed takwin is temporal but not caused by God, thereby distinguishing 'originated' from 'brought into existence'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's act of creation, do you ever unconsciously assume that some things can 'just happen' without God's direct causing? How does this passage's claim challenge your reliance on God as the sole originator of all that occurs? What would it take for you to truly affirm that nothing comes into existence except by His bringing-into-existence?
?
Have you ever caught yourself attributing a 'self-originating' quality to something in your life—an event, a habit, a feeling—as if it emerged without God's bringing it into existence? What would it mean to consciously return that area to God's ihdath and recognize it as muhdath?
?
This passage reveals a theological attempt to limit God's direct involvement in certain originated things. In your own heart, do you ever try to carve out a space where you are the self-originating cause—where you say 'I just did it' without reference to God's bringing into existence? What would it look like to repent of that independence and see every hadith in your life as muhdath by God?

Ma'mar's Infinite Regress of Takwins
Reports Ma'mar's view that takwin occurs through an infinite series of takwins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ma'mar's proposal of an infinite chain of takwins and why it is considered problematic in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Ma'mar solved the origination of takwin by positing an endless series of takwins.

This lesson explores Ma'mar's attempt to explain the coming into existence of takwin without direct divine causation. By positing a second takwin that brings about the first, and a third that brings about the second, and so on ad infinitum, he hoped to avoid the claim of self-origination. However, this leads to an infinite regress, which theologians reject.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Ma'mar
Read the Arabic sentence about Ma'mar and its translation. Note the phrase 'كذا إلى ما لا يتناهى'.
2
Trace the infinite chain
Ma'mar says: takwin came about by a second takwin, that by a third, and so on. Visualize this as an endless sequence.
Each takwin is produced by another takwin.
3
Understand the problem of infinite regress
Why is an infinite regress problematic? It never reaches a first cause, so explanation is postponed forever. In theology, this conflicts with the need for a first cause (God).
This is a classic objection to infinite causal regress.
4
Connect to the broader discussion
Realize that Ma'mar's view is presented as a response to those who said takwin is hadith but not muhdath. He tries to give a cause, but the cause is endless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And Ma'mar said: takwin occurred by a second takwin, and the second by a third takwin, and the third by a fourth, and so on ad infinitum.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage addresses the paradoxical position of those who affirm that takwin is temporally originated (hadith) but deny that it is brought into existence by God (muhdath). They distinguish between 'hadith' (temporal) and 'muhdath' (created/effected by an agent). For them, something is muhdath only if its coming into existence is connected to an act of bringing-into-existence (ihdath). But they claim that takwin's own origination is not connected to any such act. This seems to make takwin a self-originating temporal entity, which is problematic. The author then reports Ma'mar's view, which attempts to avoid this by positing an infinite regress: takwin is brought about by a second takwin, that by a third, and so on without end. This, of course, leads to an infinite chain, which is also problematic from a theological standpoint. The passage ends without explicit refutation, but the absurdity of infinite regress is implied.

?
The lesson shows the absurdity of infinite regress. Are there beliefs or habits in your life that rely on 'and so on ad infinitum' to avoid accountability? What would it mean for you to accept that there is a First Cause who holds you to account?

Takwin without a Locus: Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr
Presents Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr's views on takwin's locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the view that takwin subsists without a locus, as held by Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir.

Core Idea
Some theologians argued that takwin exists without a locus, independent of the object it brings into existence.

This lesson introduces the first major opinion on the locus of takwin: that it subsists without a locus. Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir both argued for this position, though with slightly different reasoning. The passage below presents their views as part of a broader survey of early kalam disputes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to grasp the core claim: takwin is distinct from the mukawwan and subsists without a locus.
Notice how Ibn al-Rawandi's view is stated simply, while Bishr's is linked to the ability (istita'a) before the act.
2
Compare the two arguments
Ibn al-Rawandi asserts takwin is not in a locus. Bishr argues that takwin must precede the mukawwan, otherwise the ability would be simultaneous with the act, which is invalid. Both conclude takwin is without a locus.
Bishr's reasoning invokes a principle about ability preceding action.
3
Reflect on the implications
If takwin is without a locus, it is not an accident in a substrate. This raises questions about how an attribute can exist without inherence.
This view challenges the standard Ash'ari framework where attributes inhere in a substrate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغيره من المتكلمين يجوزون وصف الصفة، فوصفوا التكوين بأنه غير المكون. ثم اختلفوا فيما بينهم في محل التكوين. فزعم ابن الراوندي أنه قائم لا في محل، وما روي عن بشر بن المعتمر أنه كان يقول: أن التكوين قبل المكون إذ لو لم يكن قبله لبطل كون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل فوجب أن يكون التكوين قائما لا في محل عنده أيضا كما هو مذهب ابن الراوندي. وما روي عن أبي الهذيل أن التكوين يوجد مع المكون لاستحالة قيامه بنفسه يوجب أن يقوم بالمكون. وقد روي عن بعض أهل المقالات أنه كان يقول: إن جميع كلام الله حادث في محل، إلا خطاب كن، فإنه حادث لا في محل. يوجب أن يكون التكوين عنده أيضا حادثا لا في محل، إذ التكوين عنده ليس إلا خطاب "كن". وزعمت الكرامية بأسرهم أن التكوين حادث قائم بذات الله تعالى وأن ذاته محل الحوادث. تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرا - ولم أقف على مذهب هشام في هذا أنه حادث لا في محل أم في ذات الله تعالى. ثم إن هؤلاء الذين يقولون بحدوث التكوين الذي هو معنى وراء المكون يقولون: حدث هو لا بإحداث الله تعالى ويقولون: إنه حادث وليس بمحدث إذ المحدث ما تعلق وجوه بالإحداث، وهو لم يتعلق حدوثه بالإحداث، وقال معمر: إن التكوين حدث بتكوين ثان، والثاني بتكوين ثالث، والثالث برابع كذا إلى ما لا يتناهى.
And others among the theologians permit describing the attribute, so they described takwin as distinct from the mukawwan. Then they differed among themselves concerning the locus of takwin. Ibn al-Rawandi claimed that it subsists without a locus. And it is related from Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir that he used to say: takwin precedes the mukawwan, for if it were not before it, the existence of ability before the act would be invalid, so it is necessary that takwin subsists without a locus according to him as well, as is the doctrine of Ibn al-Rawandi. And it is related from Abu al-Hudhayl that takwin exists with the mukawwan because it is impossible for it to subsist by itself, necessitating that it inhere in the mukawwan. And it is related from some of the adherents of doctrinal systems that he used to say: all of God's speech is created in a locus, except the address 'Be', for it is created without a locus. This necessitates that takwin according to him is also created without a locus, since takwin according to him is nothing but the address 'Be'. And the Karramiyya entirely claimed that takwin is created, subsisting in the essence of God Almighty, and that His essence is the locus of temporal events. Exalted is God above what the wrongdoers say, greatly exalted. And I did not come across Hisham's doctrine on this—whether it is created without a locus or in the essence of God Almighty. Then those who affirm the temporality of takwin, which is a meaning beyond the mukawwan, say: it occurred without God's bringing it into existence, and they say: it is temporal (hadith) and not made temporal (muhdath), since the muhdath is that to which the face of bringing into existence is attached, whereas its temporality is not attached to bringing into existence. And Muammar said: takwin occurs by a second takwin, the second by a third, the third by a fourth, and so on ad infinitum.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage is a survey of differing opinions on the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The author begins by noting that some theologians permit describing the attribute itself, so they described takwin as distinct from the thing brought into existence (al-mukawwan). Then they disagreed on the locus of takwin. Ibn al-Rawandi claimed it subsists without a locus. A report from Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir states that takwin precedes the mukawwan, because if it did not, the ability (istita'a) before the act would be invalid, so takwin must subsist without a locus, like Ibn al-Rawandi's view. A report from Abu al-Hudhayl says takwin exists with the mukawwan because it cannot subsist by itself, so it must inhere in the mukawwan. A report from some adherents of theological doctrines says all of God's speech is created in a locus, except the command 'Be' (kun), which is created without a locus. This implies that takwin is also created without a locus, since takwin for them is none other than the command 'Be'. The Karramiyya entirely held that takwin is created and inheres in God's essence, and that His essence is the locus of temporal events. The author comments, 'Exalted is Allah above what the wrongdoers say, greatly exalted.' He says he did not find Hisham's view on whether it is created without a locus or in God's essence. Then, those who hold that takwin is created and is a meaning distinct from the mukawwan say it occurs without God's bringing it into existence (ihdath), and it is temporal (hadith) but not made temporal (muhdath), because the muhdath is that which is connected to ihdath, whereas its occurrence is not connected to ihdath. Muammar said takwin occurs by a second takwin, the second by a third, the third by a fourth, ad infinitum.

Key Terms
تكوين
مكون
محل
استطاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That takwin must always inhere in a substrate like other accidents.
Correction: Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr argued takwin can subsist without a locus, based on the need for it to precede the mukawwan.

Checkpoint
What is the key similarity between Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr's views on takwin?
A) Both said takwin inheres in the mukawwan
B) Both said takwin is created in God's essence
C) Both said takwin subsists without a locus
D) Both said takwin is the command 'Be'

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr argued that takwin is an attribute that exists without inhering in any substrate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's attributes like 'bringing into existence', do you instinctively imagine them as dependent on creation? What does it mean for your concept of God that an attribute like takwin could exist independently, with no need for anything else—even the object it creates—to 'hold' it? How does this challenge your view of God's self-sufficiency?
?
Bishr argued that takwin must precede the object to preserve the principle that ability comes before action. In your own daily choices, do you act as if your intentions and abilities precede your actions, or do you often act impulsively? If you truly believed that intention must come before every act, what one habit would you need to change starting today?
?
Ibn al-Rawandi and Bishr concluded that an attribute of God can subsist without a locus. Yet you might assume that God's attributes must be 'attached' to something or appear only when creation exists. Where does that assumption come from in your own heart—a desire to limit God to what you can imagine, or a fear of affirming something you don't fully grasp? Will you accept this teaching from revelation and reason, even if your mind resists?

Takwin Inhering in the Mukawwan or as the Command 'Be'
Presents Abu al-Hudhayl's and the 'kun' view on takwin's locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the views that takwin inheres in the mukawwan (Abu al-Hudhayl) or is identified with the command 'Be' created without a locus.

Core Idea
Some theologians located takwin in the mukawwan itself, while others equated it with God's creative command.

This lesson covers two more views on takwin's locus. Abu al-Hudhayl argued that takwin cannot subsist by itself, so it must inhere in the mukawwan. Another group identified takwin with God's address 'Be' (kun), which they held is created without a locus. Both positions attempt to resolve the theological paradox of how an attribute relates to its effect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand each view and its reasoning.
Note the different starting points: one denies self-subsistence, the other identifies takwin with a specific divine speech act.
2
Analyze Abu al-Hudhayl's reasoning
He argues takwin cannot subsist by itself, so it must inhere in the mukawwan. This treats takwin as an accident inhering in the object it brings into existence.
This view suggests takwin is simultaneous with the mukawwan.
3
Analyze the 'kun' view
Some held that all of God's speech is created in a locus except the command 'Be', which is created without a locus. Since takwin is identified with 'Be', it too is created without a locus.
This view avoids takwin inhering in the mukawwan or in God, but raises questions about the nature of divine speech.
4
Compare the two views
Both try to explain the relationship between takwin and the mukawwan: one makes it an accident of the effect, the other makes it a separate creative command.
They represent different theological commitments about attributes and creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغيره من المتكلمين يجوزون وصف الصفة، فوصفوا التكوين بأنه غير المكون. ثم اختلفوا فيما بينهم في محل التكوين. فزعم ابن الراوندي أنه قائم لا في محل، وما روي عن بشر بن المعتمر أنه كان يقول: أن التكوين قبل المكون إذ لو لم يكن قبله لبطل كون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل فوجب أن يكون التكوين قائما لا في محل عنده أيضا كما هو مذهب ابن الراوندي. وما روي عن أبي الهذيل أن التكوين يوجد مع المكون لاستحالة قيامه بنفسه يوجب أن يقوم بالمكون. وقد روي عن بعض أهل المقالات أنه كان يقول: إن جميع كلام الله حادث في محل، إلا خطاب كن، فإنه حادث لا في محل. يوجب أن يكون التكوين عنده أيضا حادثا لا في محل، إذ التكوين عنده ليس إلا خطاب "كن". وزعمت الكرامية بأسرهم أن التكوين حادث قائم بذات الله تعالى وأن ذاته محل الحوادث. تعالى الله عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرا - ولم أقف على مذهب هشام في هذا أنه حادث لا في محل أم في ذات الله تعالى. ثم إن هؤلاء الذين يقولون بحدوث التكوين الذي هو معنى وراء المكون يقولون: حدث هو لا بإحداث الله تعالى ويقولون: إنه حادث وليس بمحدث إذ المحدث ما تعلق وجوه بالإحداث، وهو لم يتعلق حدوثه بالإحداث، وقال معمر: إن التكوين حدث بتكوين ثان، والثاني بتكوين ثالث، والثالث برابع كذا إلى ما لا يتناهى.
And others among the theologians permit describing the attribute, so they described takwin as distinct from the mukawwan. Then they differed among themselves concerning the locus of takwin. Ibn al-Rawandi claimed that it subsists without a locus. And it is related from Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir that he used to say: takwin precedes the mukawwan, for if it were not before it, the existence of ability before the act would be invalid, so it is necessary that takwin subsists without a locus according to him as well, as is the doctrine of Ibn al-Rawandi. And it is related from Abu al-Hudhayl that takwin exists with the mukawwan because it is impossible for it to subsist by itself, necessitating that it inhere in the mukawwan. And it is related from some of the adherents of doctrinal systems that he used to say: all of God's speech is created in a locus, except the address 'Be', for it is created without a locus. This necessitates that takwin according to him is also created without a locus, since takwin according to him is nothing but the address 'Be'. And the Karramiyya entirely claimed that takwin is created, subsisting in the essence of God Almighty, and that His essence is the locus of temporal events. Exalted is God above what the wrongdoers say, greatly exalted. And I did not come across Hisham's doctrine on this—whether it is created without a locus or in the essence of God Almighty. Then those who affirm the temporality of takwin, which is a meaning beyond the mukawwan, say: it occurred without God's bringing it into existence, and they say: it is temporal (hadith) and not made temporal (muhdath), since the muhdath is that to which the face of bringing into existence is attached, whereas its temporality is not attached to bringing into existence. And Muammar said: takwin occurs by a second takwin, the second by a third, the third by a fourth, and so on ad infinitum.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage is a survey of differing opinions on the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The author begins by noting that some theologians permit describing the attribute itself, so they described takwin as distinct from the thing brought into existence (al-mukawwan). Then they disagreed on the locus of takwin. Ibn al-Rawandi claimed it subsists without a locus. A report from Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir states that takwin precedes the mukawwan, because if it did not, the ability (istita'a) before the act would be invalid, so takwin must subsist without a locus, like Ibn al-Rawandi's view. A report from Abu al-Hudhayl says takwin exists with the mukawwan because it cannot subsist by itself, so it must inhere in the mukawwan. A report from some adherents of theological doctrines says all of God's speech is created in a locus, except the command 'Be' (kun), which is created without a locus. This implies that takwin is also created without a locus, since takwin for them is none other than the command 'Be'. The Karramiyya entirely held that takwin is created and inheres in God's essence, and that His essence is the locus of temporal events. The author comments, 'Exalted is Allah above what the wrongdoers say, greatly exalted.' He says he did not find Hisham's view on whether it is created without a locus or in God's essence. Then, those who hold that takwin is created and is a meaning distinct from the mukawwan say it occurs without God's bringing it into existence (ihdath), and it is temporal (hadith) but not made temporal (muhdath), because the muhdath is that which is connected to ihdath, whereas its occurrence is not connected to ihdath. Muammar said takwin occurs by a second takwin, the second by a third, the third by a fourth, ad infinitum.

Key Terms
تكوين
مكون
محل
كن
كلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu al-Hudhayl, why must takwin inhere in the mukawwan?
A) Because takwin is eternal
B) Because it is impossible for takwin to subsist by itself
C) Because takwin is identical to God's essence
D) Because takwin precedes the mukawwan

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Hudhayl located takwin in the mukawwan, while others identified it with the created command 'Be' existing without a locus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu al-Hudhayl argued that takwin cannot exist independently and must inhere in the creation. Do you live as if God's creative power is present in every moment of your existence, or do you sometimes feel disconnected from that immediacy? What would change if you truly believed that His act of bringing you into being is constantly with you?
?
The view that 'Be' is created without a locus suggests that God's command acts directly without any intermediate. When you face a situation that seems hopeless, do you truly expect God's 'Be' to work without needing a physical means? How does your reliance on material causes reveal the strength or weakness of your faith in His absolute creative power?
?
If takwin is debated as either an accident or a separate command, does this intellectual discussion move you to awe or distance you from the reality of creation? Which perspective makes you more conscious of your total dependence on God's act, and why?

The Karramiyya: Takwin Created in God's Essence
Presents the Karramiyya view and the author's rejection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Karramiyya position that takwin is a created attribute subsisting in God's essence, and the author's rejection of this view.

Core Idea
The Karramiyya held that takwin is a temporal accident inhering in God's essence, making Him a locus of temporal events.

This lesson presents the Karramiyya's radical claim that takwin is created (hādith) and subsists in God's essence itself. The author strongly rejects this, considering it a form of anthropomorphism. The passage also mentions that the author did not find Hisham's precise view. This view represents the extreme opposite of takwin without a locus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the Karramiyya's claim and the author's response.
Notice the author's interjection: 'Exalted is God above what the wrongdoers say.'
2
Understand the Karramiyya's position
They claimed takwin is created (hādith) and subsists in God's essence, meaning God's essence becomes a locus for temporal events.
This implies change in God, which orthodox theology rejects.
3
Note the author's stance
The author dismisses this view as the saying of wrongdoers, indicating it is beyond the pale of acceptable doctrine.
The author also notes uncertainty about Hisham's view, possibly to distance himself from it.
4
Reflect on the theological problem
If takwin is in God's essence, then God is subject to temporal events, challenging His immutability.
This is why the author rejects it so strongly.

The Paradox of Takwin: Occurring Without Divine Activation
Discusses the hadith-but-not-muhdath claim and Muammar's infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the paradoxical claim that takwin is temporal (hadith) yet not made temporal (muhdath) by God, and Muammar's infinite regress argument.

Core Idea
Some theologians claimed takwin occurs without God directly bringing it into existence, leading to logical puzzles like infinite regress.

This lesson examines a further twist: those who affirm takwin as a temporal entity distinct from the mukawwan also claim it occurs without God's bringing it into existence (ihdath). They distinguish between 'hadith' (temporal) and 'muhdath' (made temporal). Muammar went further, positing an infinite chain of takwins. These ideas represent the extreme logical implications of treating takwin as a separate entity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to grasp the distinction between hadith and muhdath, and Muammar's infinite regress.
This is a dense passage; take time to parse the logic.
2
Understand the paradox
They say takwin is hadith (temporal) but not muhdath (made temporal), because 'muhdath' is defined as that which is connected to ihdath, while takwin's temporality is not so connected.
This seems to make takwin self-caused or uncaused, which is theologically problematic.
3
Analyze Muammar's view
Muammar says takwin occurs by a second takwin, that by a third, ad infinitum. This is an infinite regress to avoid the first takwin being uncaused.
But an infinite regress is also problematic for kalam.
4
Reflect on the theological stakes
Both views try to preserve God's transcendence by not attributing the act of bringing into existence directly to God, but they lead to logical difficulties.
This shows the complexity of early kalam discussions on attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
According to the view presented, why is takwin considered hadith but not muhdath?
A) Because it is created by a second takwin
B) Because its temporality is not attached to any bringing into existence (ihdath)
C) Because it is eternal
D) Because it inheres in God's essence

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever act as if certain changes in your life can happen without God's direct involvement—as if they are 'hadith but not muhdath'? What is one area where you relying on your own power to produce a change, forgetting that only God's creative act (ihdath) brings things into being?
?
This passage shows that trying to separate God's action from the effect leads to infinite regress or paradox. In your spiritual life, are you trying to produce a result (like sincerity or repentance) without humbly acknowledging that even the ability to seek is granted by God? How does this divine dependence challenge your pride?
?
Muammar's infinite regress was an attempt to avoid saying takwin is uncaused. Are there areas in your belief where you create 'infinite regresses'—making up middle steps to avoid directly attributing everything to God? What would it look like to simply accept that every good thing comes directly from His ihdath?

Takwin as an Eternal Attribute
Presents the Maturidi view that takwin is an eternal attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi doctrine that takwin is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, and how it relates to other eternal attributes like power and will.

Core Idea
Takwin is eternal; the things it brings into existence are temporal.

The Maturidi school of kalam emphasizes that God's attribute of bringing into existence (takwin) is eternal, just like His knowledge and power. This passage from Imam Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla articulates this position clearly. It draws an analogy with power and will to show that the attribute is eternal while its effects are temporal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the core claim about takwin.
Pay attention to the analogy drawn with qudra and irada.
2
Identify the analogy
Notice how takwin is compared to power (qudra) and will (irada). Each attribute is eternal, but its effect is temporal.
The pattern is: attribute (eternal) → effect (temporal).
3
Understand the distinction
The passage emphasizes that the attribute itself is eternal, not the act of creating. The mukawwan (created thing) occurs in time.
This preserves God's timelessness while affirming His creative action.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters in kalam: it defends God's unity and timelessness against objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التكوين صفة أزلية قائمة بذات الله تعالى. وقال أهل الحق: إن التكوين صفة أزلية قائمة بذات الله تعالى كصفة العلم والقدرة والسمع والبصر، فكان التكوين أزليا والمكون حادثا، كالقدرة كانت أزلية والمقدور حادثا، وكذا الإرادة والمراد فيكون التكوين لكل مكون (تكوينا له) لوقت وجوده كإرادة وجود كل موجود يكون إرادة لوجوده لوقت وجوده.
Takwin is an eternal attribute subsisting in the essence of Allah Almighty. And Ahl al-Haqq said: Indeed, takwin is an eternal attribute subsisting in the essence of Allah Almighty, like the attribute of knowledge, power, hearing, and sight. So takwin is eternal while the mukawwan is temporal, just as power is eternal while the maqdur is temporal, and similarly will (irada) and the object of will (murad). So takwin is a bringing into existence for every mukawwan at the time of its existence, just as the will for the existence of every existent is a willing of its existence at the time of its existence.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage presents the doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq (the Maturidis) on the attribute of takwin. It begins with the heading that takwin is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence. Then it explains that just like knowledge, power, hearing, and sight are eternal attributes, takwin is also eternal. The thing brought into existence (mukawwan) is temporal. The analogy is drawn: power is eternal but its object (maqdur) comes into existence temporally; similarly, will (irada) is eternal but its object (murad) is temporal. Likewise, takwin is eternal, but the mukawwan is temporal. The author further clarifies that takwin is a bringing into existence for each mukawwan at the time of its existence, just as the will for each existent is a willing of its existence for the time of its existence (i.e., the eternal will determines the time of occurrence).

Key Terms
تكوين
صفة أزلية
مكون
قدرة
مقدور
إرادة
مراد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That by 'eternal' the Maturidis mean takwin has always been actively creating.
Correction: They only mean the attribute itself is eternal, not the act of creating; the creation occurs in time.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi view, how is takwin similar to power (qudra)?
A) Both are created in time
B) Both are eternal, but their effects are temporal
C) Both subsist without a locus
D) Both are identical to God's essence

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute of God, just like power and will, but its effects (created beings) come into existence in time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If takwin is an eternal attribute, what does that imply about God's relationship to time and your own life? Does this reality reshape how you view your moments of waiting for something to happen?
?
The passage teaches that takwin brings each thing into existence at its specific time. Are you truly content with God's timing, or do you sometimes wish He would create your desires sooner? What does your impatience reveal about your trust in His eternal attribute?
?
You now know that takwin is eternal, like power and will. How does this knowledge affect your prayer? Are you asking the Eternal One to act in time, or are you acknowledging that His eternal attribute of bringing into existence already encompasses your need?

Was Allah Creator in Pre-Eternity? Views of the Theologians
Enumerates four positions on Allah being Creator in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different theological positions on whether Allah was described as Creator in pre-eternity, focusing on the Maturidi distinction between the eternal attribute of takwin and the temporal act of creation.

Core Idea
The Maturidis affirm Allah was Creator in pre-eternity through the eternal attribute of takwin, not a pre-eternal creation.

The question of whether Allah was 'Creator' in pre-eternity touches on how we understand God's attributes and their relationship to time. Different schools answered differently, and the Maturidi position offers a nuanced resolution. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the views of the Mu'tazila, Abu al-Hudhayl, the Karramiyya, and finally the Maturidis, clarifying what it means to say Allah was Creator in pre-eternity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four positions
Read the passage and list the four groups whose views are presented. Notice how each group answers the question: Was Allah Creator in pre-eternity?
The groups are: Mu'tazila/Najjariyya/Ahl al-Hadith, Abu al-Hudhayl, Karramiyya, and Maturidis.
2
Understand the common ground
All groups agree that takwin (the act of bringing into existence) is created (hadith). Their disagreement is about whether Allah can be called 'Creator' in pre-eternity.
3
Focus on the Maturidi answer
The Maturidis say Allah was Creator because the attribute of takwin subsists in His essence eternally, just like knowledge and power. This is distinct from saying the act of creation is eternal.
Key term: takwin (تكوين)
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by stating that all divine attributes are eternal and Allah was described by them in pre-eternity. Consider how this preserves God's perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف القائلون بحدوث التكوين أن الله تعالى هل كان في الأزل خالقا رازقا مصورا محيبا ومميتا أم لا؟ فذهب جمهور المعتزلة والنجارية وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث أنه ما كان خالقا حتى حدث المخلوق، وكذا في سائر الصفات. وقال أبو الهذيل العلاف: إنه كان في الأزل خالقا بمعنى أنه سيخلق. وقالت الكرامية: إنه كان في الأزل خالقا بالخالقية رازقا بالرازقية، وكذا في سائر الصفات ويفسرون الخالقية بالقدرة على التخليق. وقال أصحابنا: إنه كان خالقا لقيام صفة الخلق وهو التكوين بذاته في الأزل، كما كان عالما قادرا سميعا بصيرا وصار الحاصل أن جميع ما هو صفة الله تعالى كان أزليا، وهو تعالى كان موصوفا به في الأزل.
Then those who affirm the temporality of takwin differed as to whether Allah was in pre-eternity a creator, a provider, a form-giver, a giver of life, and a giver of death, or not. The majority of the Mu'tazila, the Najjariyya, and all theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith held that He was not a creator until the creature happened, and similarly for the other attributes. Abu al-Hudhayl al-Allaf said: He was in pre-eternity a creator in the sense that He will create. The Karramiyya said: He was in pre-eternity a creator with creatorhood (al-khaliqiyya), a provider with providerhood (al-raziqiyya), and similarly for the other attributes, and they interpret creatorhood as the power to create (al-qudra 'ala al-takhliq). Our companions (Ashabuna) said: He was a creator due to the subsistence of the attribute of creating (khalq), which is takwin, in His essence in pre-eternity, just as He was knowing, powerful, hearing, and seeing. And the result is that all that is an attribute of Allah was eternal, and He was described by it in pre-eternity.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage addresses the theological question of whether Allah was described as Creator in pre-eternity. After mentioning that those who hold takwin is created differ, the author lists their positions. The majority of Mu'tazila, Najjariyya, and Ahl al-Hadith said He was not Creator until the creature existed. Abu al-Hudhayl said He was Creator in the sense of 'will create' (future tense). The Karramiyya said He was Creator in pre-eternity with an attribute of creatorhood, which they interpret as the power to create. Then the author presents the position of 'our companions' (the Maturidis): He was Creator because the attribute of creating (khalq), i.e., takwin, subsists in His essence in pre-eternity, just as He is knowing, powerful, hearing, seeing – these attributes are eternal and He is described by them eternally. The conclusion is that all attributes of Allah are eternal and He was described by them in pre-eternity.

Key Terms
خالق
خالقية
رازقية
تخليق
تكوين
أزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That saying 'Allah was Creator in pre-eternity' means the creation itself is eternal.
Correction: The Maturidis affirm the eternal attribute of takwin, not an eternal creation. The act of creating occurs in time.

Checkpoint
How do the Maturidis explain that Allah was Creator in pre-eternity?
A) He had the power to create from pre-eternity
B) The attribute of takwin subsists in His essence eternally
C) He created in pre-eternity
D) He will create in the future

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis affirm Allah's eternal attribute of takwin, allowing Him to be called 'Creator' in pre-eternity without implying an eternal creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah as 'the Creator,' do you instinctively limit that title to what He has already made? How does knowing that the attribute of takwin is eternal shape your view of His continuous creative power in your life right now?
?
If Allah was always described by all His eternal attributes, including being the Creator, what does that mean for your reliance on His ability to create new beginnings, even when your situation seems impossible?
?
The Maturidis distinguished between the eternal attribute of creation and the temporal act of creating. Is there an area of your life where you have confused God's timeless perfection with His timing in your circumstances? How can you trust both His eternal nature and His specific plan for you?

Consensus on Eternal and Act-Attributes and the Dispute over Kalam
Consensus on attributes and dispute over kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus among theologians on classifying attributes as eternal or originated, and the specific dispute over whether speech (kalam) is an attribute of the essence or of action.

Core Idea
While most attributes are clearly eternal or temporal, speech divides theologians.

Before exploring the finer criteria, Nasafi presents the broad agreement between the Mu'tazila and the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith on most attributes. Both groups affirm that attributes like life, power, and knowledge are eternal, while acts like creating are temporal. However, when it comes to speech (kalam), they part ways. This lesson covers that consensus and the key disagreement over kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on consensus
Read the Arabic passage that describes the agreement on eternal attributes and the disagreement on kalam.
2
Identify the two categories
Notice which attributes are considered eternal (sifat al-dhat) and which are temporal (sifat al-fi'l) by both groups.
3
Focus on the dispute over kalam
See how Ahl al-Hadith and Mu'tazila differ: one says it is eternal, the other says it is created.
This will lead to the need for a criterion in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت الخصوم: إن ما كان من صفات الذات فهو أزلي وما كان من صفات الفعل فهو حادث فعلى هذا انعقد الإجماع بين المعتزلة وبين متكلمي أهل الحديث، أنه تعالى كان في الأزل حيا باقيا قادرا عالما سميعا بصيرا وأنه لم يكن خالقا ولا رازقا ولا مصورا ولا محيبا ولا مميتا، لأن القسم الأول من صفات الذات والقسم الثاني من صفات الفعل، واختلفوا أنه تعالى هل كان في الأزل متكلما؟ فقال أهل الحديث : كان متكلماً في الأزل؛ لأن الكلام من قبيل صفات الذات. وقالت المعتزلة : لم يكن في الأزل متكلما ، لأن الكلام من صفات الفعل. وتفرع من هذا اختلاف فيما بينهم في الحد الفاصل بين صفات الذات وصفات الفعل ففرقت المعتزلة بينهما فرقا يبقى الكلام في جملة صفات الفعل فقالت: الفرق بينهما أن ما يثبت ولا يجوز نفيه فهو من صفات الذات، فإنه يقال: يعلم كذا، ولا يقال لا يعلم كذا وكذا يقال يقدر على كذا، ولا يقال لا يقدر على كذا ، ويقال : يبصر فلانا، ولا يقال لا يبصر فلانا، وكذا يقال : يسمع صوت فلان، ولا يقال لا يسمع صوت فلان.
And the opponents said: What is of the attributes of the essence (sifat al-dhat) is eternal, and what is of the attributes of action (sifat al-fi'l) is originated. On this basis consensus was reached between the Mu'tazila and the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith that He Most High was in pre-eternity Living, Everlasting, Powerful, Knowing, Hearing, Seeing, and that He was not a Creator, nor a Provider, nor a Shaper, nor a Giver of life, nor a Giver of death, because the first group are attributes of the essence and the second group are attributes of action. And they differed over whether He Most High was in pre-eternity a Speaker (mutakallim). Ahl al-Hadith said: He was a Speaker in pre-eternity because speech (kalam) is of the class of attributes of the essence. The Mu'tazila said: He was not a Speaker in pre-eternity because speech is of the attributes of action. From this branched out a difference among them concerning the distinguishing boundary (al-hadd al-fasil) between attributes of essence and attributes of action. So the Mu'tazila distinguished between them with a distinction by which speech remains among the attributes of action. They said: The difference between them is that what is affirmed and whose negation is not permissible is of the attributes of the essence. For example, it is said: He knows such-and-such, and it is not said: He does not know such-and-such. Similarly, it is said: He is able to do such-and-such, and it is not said: He is not able to do such-and-such. And it is said: He sees so-and-so, and it is not said: He does not see so-and-so. And similarly, it is said: He hears the voice of so-and-so, and it is not said: He does not hear the voice of so-and-so.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage discusses the distinction between eternal attributes (sifat al-dhat) and originated act-attributes (sifat al-fi'l). It begins by stating the consensus view: attributes of the essence (like life, power, knowledge) are eternal, while attributes of action (like creating, providing) are originated. Both Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Hadith agree on this classification for the basic attributes. However, they differ on speech (kalam). Ahl al-Hadith consider speech an attribute of the essence, so Allah is eternally speaking. Mu'tazila consider it an attribute of action, so He only speaks when He creates speech. This disagreement leads to a search for a clear criterion (al-hadd al-fasil) to distinguish the two types. The Mu'tazila propose a criterion: if an attribute is always affirmed and cannot be negated without contradiction, it is of the essence. They give examples: we can always say 'He knows' but never 'He does not know'; similarly for power, sight, hearing. This criterion would place kalam among act-attributes because we can say 'He does not speak' in some contexts, according to them.

Key Terms
صفات الذات
صفات الفعل
الكلام
متكلما

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All theologians consider speech an eternal attribute of Allah.
Correction: The Mu'tazila consider speech an originated act-attribute, leading to the dispute described.

Checkpoint
According to the consensus mentioned, which of the following attributes is considered an attribute of action (sifat al-fi'l)?
A) Life
B) Power
C) Creating
D) Hearing

Key Takeaway
Both Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Hadith agree that most attributes are either eternal or temporal, but they disagree on the status of speech (kalam).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you consider God's speech, as revealed in the Qur'an, to be an expression of His eternal nature or a temporal event? How does your answer shape how you approach His words in your daily life?
?
When you read that both groups agreed that God was not a 'Creator' in pre-eternity, does that change how you understand His relationship with time? Does it make you more patient in waiting for His actions in your life?
?
If you had to choose between viewing God's attributes as purely eternal or purely temporal, which would you lean toward — and does this lesson reveal a blind spot in your trust in God's unchanging essence?
