The Inseparability of Creation and Created: Rational and Linguistic Proofs
Nasafi presents a divisional argument and a linguistic proof to refute the Ash'ari view of creation as separate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses both a rational divisional argument and a linguistic analysis from Sibawayh to prove that creation (khalq) is not an additional entity over the created (makhluq).

Core Idea
Creation is not separate; it is identical to the created act.

In this passage, Nasafi deploys two powerful arguments against the Ash'ari claim that creation is an additional attribute. First, he rationally divides all possible loci for a separate creation and shows each is impossible. Then, he turns to Arabic grammar, citing Sibawayh's definition of the verb and object, to demonstrate linguistic inseparability. This lesson guides you through both proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the divisional argument carefully
The passage begins with a division: if creation is separate from the created, where does it subsist? Identify the four possibilities and how each is refuted.
Note that the division covers: in the created, in no locus, in the Creator (eternal or originated).
2
Understand the conclusion from the division
See how the refutation of all possibilities leads to the conclusion that creation is not an additional meaning.
3
Examine the linguistic proof from Sibawayh
Read how Sibawayh's definition of the verb (fi'l) and the real object (masdar) supports the inseparability of action and object.
The key quote: 'the real object (maf'ul) is the infinitive (masdar)'.
4
Reflect on the author's method
Note that the author quotes the opponent's own words to avoid accusations of misrepresentation.
This shows scholarly integrity in dialectical theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : لو كان الخلق غير المخلوق، إما أن كان قائما بالمخلوق أو لا في محل وأبطل القسمين ثم قال : أو بالباري جل وعلا وهو لا يخلو إما أن كان قديما أو كان محدثا وإبطال وأبطل أن يكون محدثا لاستحالة كون الباري محلا للحوادث وعاد في إبطاله أن يكون قديما إلى ما قال بدءً، أن الاختراع إن حصل به فهو في معنى القدرة فيكون له قدرتان وإن لم يحصل فلا فائدة في إثباته. ثم قال: ظهر بطلان هذه الأقسام، أن الخلق ليس معنى زائدا على المخلوق . قال : والذي يدل عليه قول أهل اللسان في حد الفعل، قال سيبويه : في حد الفعل أمثلة أحدث من لفظ إحداث الأسماء مثل قول: ضرب يضرب وأضرب وقالوا: الأفعال على ثلاثة أقسام ماض ومستقبل وفعل هو أمر وقال إن الفعل على ضربين لازم ومتعدي ثم عندهم المفعول على الحقيقة هو المصدر ثم يقولون: مفعول به و مفعول له ومفعول فيه ومفعول معه، ولا يزيدون على ذلك وما أخذ منهم الفصل في الفعل والمفعول فدل ذلك على ما قلناه. وتكلم بهذا كله بعض الأشعرية حكيته بلفظه لئلا يظن بي التقصير في حكاية شبه الخصوم.
Then he said: If creation (khalq) is other than the created (makhluq), either it subsists in the created or in no locus. And he invalidated both divisions. Then he said: Or in the Almighty Creator, and it is not free: either it is eternal or originated. And he invalidated and declared that it being originated is impossible due to the impossibility of the Creator being a locus for originated things. And he returned in invalidating that it is eternal to what he said at the beginning: that if invention (ikhtira') is obtained through it, then it is in the sense of power, so He would have two powers; and if not obtained, then there is no benefit in establishing it. Then he said: The invalidity of these divisions has become apparent, that creation is not an additional meaning over the created. He said: And what indicates that is the statement of the people of language in defining the verb (fi'l). Sibawayh said: In defining the verb, examples are derived from the pronunciation of the derivation of nouns, like saying: daraba, yadribu, and adrib. And they said: Verbs are three types: past, future, and a verb which is a command. And he said: The verb is of two types: transitive and intransitive. Then according to them, the real object (maf'ul) is the infinitive (masdar). Then they say: object with (maf'ul bihi), object for (maf'ul lahu), object in (maf'ul fihi), object with (maf'ul ma'ahu), and they do not add to that. And what they took regarding the distinction between verb and object indicates what we have said. And all of this was spoken by some Ash'ari; I narrated it in his wording, lest I be thought to have slacked in narrating the doubts of the opponents.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the Ash'ari argument. It begins with a division: if creation (khalq) is distinct from the created (makhluq), where does it subsist? It cannot subsist in the created (since that would make it accident), nor without a locus, nor in the Creator (since that would make the Creator a locus for originated events). The author then shows that if khalq is eternal, it is redundant with qudra, and if originated, it cannot be in the Creator. Thus, khalq is not an additional meaning. The passage then provides a linguistic proof from the grammarian Sibawayh. The definition of 'verb' (fi'l) in Arabic is such that the object (maf'ul) is inherently tied to it, and the term 'creation' (khalq) is linguistically a verbal noun that implies the created. This supports the conclusion that khalq is not a separate entity. The author emphasizes that he narrated this in the opponent's own words to avoid accusations of misrepresentation.

Key Terms
خلق (khalq)
مخلوق (makhluq)
اختراع (ikhtira')
فعل (fi'l)
مصدر (masdar)
مفعول (maf'ul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Linguistic analysis is irrelevant to theological issues.
Correction: Language reflects conceptual realities; the grammatical inseparability of verb and object mirrors the theological inseparability of action and effect.

Checkpoint
According to the divisional argument, if creation (khalq) were an additional meaning over the created, which of the following is NOT a possibility for its locus?
A) In the created
B) In no locus
C) In the Creator
D) In another separate entity

Key Takeaway
Both rational division and linguistic analysis show that creation is not a separate entity but is identical to the created act.

Confess a specific area where you have ignored this reality and commit to remembering it daily.

Rational Proof That Khalq Is Not Additional to Makhluq
Rational argument invalidating all ways khalq could be additional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument proving that 'creation' (khalq) cannot be a separate attribute beyond the 'created' (makhluq).

Core Idea
Khalq cannot be additional to makhluq; any attempt leads to absurdities.

The author now presents a rigorous rational argument to demonstrate that creation is not a distinct attribute. He begins by laying out the general principle for affirming divine attributes, then considers all possible ways creation could be separate, systematically invalidating each. This lesson walks through that logical elimination.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle for affirming attributes
Read the opening lines where the author states that attributes are affirmed either as implications of an act or to negate a deficiency. This sets the framework.
If an act has no relation to its object, it cannot be affirmed unless it negates a deficiency.
2
Follow the division of possibilities
The author considers where 'khalq' could subsist: in the makhluq, not in a locus, or in the Creator. Note each branch and its sub-branches (eternal vs. originated).
This is a classic kalam method of exhaustive division (taqsim).
3
See how each branch is invalidated
Go through the invalidation of each possibility. Pay attention to why the originated option makes the Creator a locus for events and the eternal option duplicates power or is useless.
The conclusion is that all divisions fail, so khalq cannot be additional.
4
Confirm the conclusion
The passage ends with the clear statement: 'creation is not an extra meaning beyond the created.' Ensure you see how it follows from the refutations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثباتها كنفيها، يدل عليه أن الصفات التي يمكن إثباتها الله تعالى عقلا، أن تكون من مدلولات الفعل كالحياة، أو لنفي نقص عن الذات لا ينتفي إلا بإثباته كالسمع والبصر والكلام، ثم الفعل إذا لم يكن له تعلق بالمفعول، إذ جميع المفعولات حاصلة بالقدرة ولم يكن إثباته لنفي نقص لا ينتفي إلا به لم يجز إثباته. ثم قال: لو كان الخلق غير المخلوق، إما أن كان قائما بالمخلوق أو لا في محل وأبطل القسمين ثم قال: أو بالباري جل وعلا وهو لا يخلو إما أن كان قديما أو كان محدثا وإبطال وأبطل أن يكون محدثا لاستحالة كون الباري محلا للحوادث وعاد في إبطاله أن يكون قديما إلى ما قال بدءً، أن الاختراع إن حصل به فهو في معنى القدرة فيكون له قدرتان وإن لم يحصل فلا فائدة في إثباته. ثم قال: ظهر بطلان هذه الأقسام، أن الخلق ليس معنى زائدا على المخلوق. قال: والذي يدل عليه قول أهل اللسان في حد الفعل، قال سيبويه: في حد الفعل أمثلة أحدث من لفظ إحداث الأسماء مثل قول: ضرب يضرب وأضرب وقالوا: الأفعال على ثلاثة أقسام ماض ومستقبل وفعل هو أمر وقال إن الفعل على ضربين لازم ومتعدي ثم عندهم المفعول على الحقيقة هو المصدر ثم يقولون: مفعول به و مفعول له ومفعول فيه ومفعول معه، ولا يزيدون على ذلك وما أخذ منهم الفصل في الفعل والمفعول فدل ذلك على ما قلناه.
Its affirmation is like its negation, indicated by the fact that the attributes which can be affirmed of God by reason are either from the implications of the act like life, or to negate a deficiency from the essence that is not negated except by affirming it, like hearing, sight, and speech. Then the act, if it has no relation to the object, since all objects are produced by power, and its affirmation is not to negate a deficiency that is not negated except by it, its affirmation is not permissible. Then he said: If creation were other than the created, either it subsists in the created or not in a locus, and he invalidated both divisions. Then he said: Or in the Creator, may He be exalted, and it is not free from being either eternal or originated. And he invalidated, and he invalidated its being originated due to the impossibility of the Creator being a locus for originated things. And he returned in invalidating its being eternal to what he said at first: that invention, if it is obtained by it, then it is in the meaning of power, so He would have two powers; and if it is not obtained, then there is no benefit in affirming it. Then he said: The invalidation of these divisions has become clear: that creation is not an extra meaning beyond the created. He said: And what indicates that is the statement of the linguists concerning the definition of the verb. Sibawayh said: In the definition of the verb are paradigms originated from the wording of originating nouns, like saying: daraba, yadribu, and adrib. And they said: Verbs are of three types: past, future, and a verb that is a command. And he said: The verb is of two types: transitive and intransitive. Then, according to them, the true object is the verbal noun. Then they say: object with, object for, object in, object with, and they do not add to that. And what is taken from them of the distinction between verb and object indicates what we have said.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument proving that 'creation' (khalq) is not a separate attribute or entity over and above the 'created' (makhluq). The author begins by presenting a general principle for affirming divine attributes: an attribute is either an implication of an act (like life, which is necessary for action) or it negates a deficiency from the essence that cannot be negated without affirming it (like hearing and sight). If an act has no relation to its object (maf'ul), and its affirmation is not for negating a deficiency, it cannot be affirmed. Next, the author reports an opponent's hypothetical division: if khalq were other than makhluq, it would have to subsist either in the makhluq or not in a locus, or in the Creator (al-Bari). Each option is invalidated: if in the makhluq, it is not independent; if not in a locus, it is impossible; if in the Creator, it must be either eternal or originated. If originated, the Creator would become a locus for originate things, which is impossible. If eternal, then it would be like power, implying two powers, or else useless. Thus, all divisions fail, proving khalq is not extra. Finally, the author adduces a linguistic proof from Sibawayh, who defines the verb (fi'l) as paradigms derived from nouns, and classifies verbs by tense and transitivity. The true object (maf'ul) is the verbal noun (masdar). According to grammarians, the object is always related to the verb, with no separate entity. This supports the conclusion that khalq and makhluq are identical, not two distinct realities.

Key Terms
خلق (khalq)
مخلوق (makhluq)
صفات (sifat)
فعل (fi'l)
مفعول (maf'ul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think khalq is a separate attribute like qudra, existing alongside makhluq.
Correction: The argument shows that if khalq were separate, it would lead to contradictions: either two powers or the Creator being a locus of events, both impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason for rejecting the idea that khalq is a separate attribute (sifa) beyond the makhluq?
A) It would imply two powers for God.
B) It has no basis in linguistic usage.
C) It leads to the Creator being a locus for events.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Khalq cannot be an additional attribute; every possible way it could be separate leads to an impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God creating the universe, do you unconsciously imagine 'creating' as a separate action or attribute? How does this passage challenge you to rethink that mental picture?
?
If God's attributes are not separate from His essence, how does that affect the way you perceive His involvement in your daily life—especially in moments when you feel distant from Him?
?
The argument here leaves no room for an eternal 'creative power' apart from creation. Does this make you feel more dependent on God's constant act of creation? How will you remind yourself of this dependency today?

Linguistic Proof from Sibawayh’s Definition of Verb and Object
Linguistic proof from Sibawayh on verb and object categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sibawayh's linguistic analysis of verbs and objects supports the identity of khalq and makhluq.

Core Idea
Language itself shows that 'creation' and 'created' are not separate realities.

Having refuted the rational possibility of khalq being separate, the author now turns to linguistic proof. He cites the grammarian Sibawayh's definition of the verb and the classification of objects. The grammatical relationship between verb and object mirrors the theological relationship: the act (khalq) is not an extra entity over the object (makhluq).

Guided Path
1
Read Sibawayh's definition of the verb
Sibawayh defines the verb as paradigms derived from nouns, e.g., daraba, yadribu, adrib. Notice he does not separate a distinct 'act' entity.
The verb is described as originating from the wording of nouns, not as a separate attribute.
2
Note the classification of verbs
Verbs are divided into past, future, and command. Also divided into transitive and intransitive. This shows the verb always relates to an object when transitive.
The classification emphasizes relationship, not separation.
3
Understand the true object (maf'ul haqiqi)
According to grammarians, the true object is the verbal noun (masdar). 'Object with', 'object for', etc. are extensions. This shows the object is inherent to the verb.
The masdar is the event itself, not a separate thing.
4
Connect to theology
The author concludes that the linguistic distinction between verb and object without an extra entity supports that khalq and makhluq are not separate. They are like verb and object: related but not additional.
Just as 'writing' and 'written' are not two separate things, creation and created are one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثباتها كنفيها، يدل عليه أن الصفات التي يمكن إثباتها الله تعالى عقلا، أن تكون من مدلولات الفعل كالحياة، أو لنفي نقص عن الذات لا ينتفي إلا بإثباته كالسمع والبصر والكلام، ثم الفعل إذا لم يكن له تعلق بالمفعول، إذ جميع المفعولات حاصلة بالقدرة ولم يكن إثباته لنفي نقص لا ينتفي إلا به لم يجز إثباته. ثم قال: لو كان الخلق غير المخلوق، إما أن كان قائما بالمخلوق أو لا في محل وأبطل القسمين ثم قال: أو بالباري جل وعلا وهو لا يخلو إما أن كان قديما أو كان محدثا وإبطال وأبطل أن يكون محدثا لاستحالة كون الباري محلا للحوادث وعاد في إبطاله أن يكون قديما إلى ما قال بدءً، أن الاختراع إن حصل به فهو في معنى القدرة فيكون له قدرتان وإن لم يحصل فلا فائدة في إثباته. ثم قال: ظهر بطلان هذه الأقسام، أن الخلق ليس معنى زائدا على المخلوق. قال: والذي يدل عليه قول أهل اللسان في حد الفعل، قال سيبويه: في حد الفعل أمثلة أحدث من لفظ إحداث الأسماء مثل قول: ضرب يضرب وأضرب وقالوا: الأفعال على ثلاثة أقسام ماض ومستقبل وفعل هو أمر وقال إن الفعل على ضربين لازم ومتعدي ثم عندهم المفعول على الحقيقة هو المصدر ثم يقولون: مفعول به و مفعول له ومفعول فيه ومفعول معه، ولا يزيدون على ذلك وما أخذ منهم الفصل في الفعل والمفعول فدل ذلك على ما قلناه.
Its affirmation is like its negation, indicated by the fact that the attributes which can be affirmed of God by reason are either from the implications of the act like life, or to negate a deficiency from the essence that is not negated except by affirming it, like hearing, sight, and speech. Then the act, if it has no relation to the object, since all objects are produced by power, and its affirmation is not to negate a deficiency that is not negated except by it, its affirmation is not permissible. Then he said: If creation were other than the created, either it subsists in the created or not in a locus, and he invalidated both divisions. Then he said: Or in the Creator, may He be exalted, and it is not free from being either eternal or originated. And he invalidated, and he invalidated its being originated due to the impossibility of the Creator being a locus for originated things. And he returned in invalidating its being eternal to what he said at first: that invention, if it is obtained by it, then it is in the meaning of power, so He would have two powers; and if it is not obtained, then there is no benefit in affirming it. Then he said: The invalidation of these divisions has become clear: that creation is not an extra meaning beyond the created. He said: And what indicates that is the statement of the linguists concerning the definition of the verb. Sibawayh said: In the definition of the verb are paradigms originated from the wording of originating nouns, like saying: daraba, yadribu, and adrib. And they said: Verbs are of three types: past, future, and a verb that is a command. And he said: The verb is of two types: transitive and intransitive. Then, according to them, the true object is the verbal noun. Then they say: object with, object for, object in, object with, and they do not add to that. And what is taken from them of the distinction between verb and object indicates what we have said.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument proving that 'creation' (khalq) is not a separate attribute or entity over and above the 'created' (makhluq). The author begins by presenting a general principle for affirming divine attributes: an attribute is either an implication of an act (like life, which is necessary for action) or it negates a deficiency from the essence that cannot be negated without affirming it (like hearing and sight). If an act has no relation to its object (maf'ul), and its affirmation is not for negating a deficiency, it cannot be affirmed. Next, the author reports an opponent's hypothetical division: if khalq were other than makhluq, it would have to subsist either in the makhluq or not in a locus, or in the Creator (al-Bari). Each option is invalidated: if in the makhluq, it is not independent; if not in a locus, it is impossible; if in the Creator, it must be either eternal or originated. If originated, the Creator would become a locus for originate things, which is impossible. If eternal, then it would be like power, implying two powers, or else useless. Thus, all divisions fail, proving khalq is not extra. Finally, the author adduces a linguistic proof from Sibawayh, who defines the verb (fi'l) as paradigms derived from nouns, and classifies verbs by tense and transitivity. The true object (maf'ul) is the verbal noun (masdar). According to grammarians, the object is always related to the verb, with no separate entity. This supports the conclusion that khalq and makhluq are identical, not two distinct realities.

Key Terms
فعل (fi'l)
مفعول (maf'ul)
مصدر (masdar)
سيبويه (Sibawayh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the linguistic argument, what is the 'true object' (al-maf'ul 'ala al-haqiqa) according to the grammarians?
A) The direct object (maf'ul bihi)
B) The verbal noun (masdar)
C) The object of purpose (maf'ul lahu)
D) The object of accompaniment (maf'ul ma'ahu)

Key Takeaway
Sibawayh's grammar shows that verb and object are inherently linked without an extra entity, mirroring the identity of khalq and makhluq.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your every action is a verb that originates from a noun—your essence. If the 'true object' of your deeds is the inner reality (masdar), what does that reveal about the sincerity of your worship? Have you been concerned more with the outward form than the substance?
?
Sibawayh's grammar shows a direct, unmediated relationship between verb and object. In your relationship with Allah, are you aware of the direct link between your actions and their ultimate meaning, or do you insert excuses and intermediaries to avoid accountability?
?
If creation and the created are one in reality, then every moment of your existence is directly sustained by Allah's creative act. How would your daily life change if you truly believed that you are constantly being created anew?

Takwin and the Ash'ari Contradiction
Definition of takwin and exposure of Ash'ari contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi definition of takwin and the Ash'ari contradiction that arises from their denial of takwin as an attribute while affirming its effect.

Core Idea
The Ash'aris deny takwin as an attribute but their own proof affirms it.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla tackles a key dispute between Maturidis and Ash'aris over the divine attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The author defines takwin and then exposes a logical contradiction in the Ash'ari position: they claim 'Kun' is speech, not an attribute of takwin, yet they admit the world came into existence through it. This contradiction, the author argues, undermines all Ash'ari objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the technical terms: takwin, ijad, kun, mukawwan.
2
Identify the Maturidi and Ash'ari views
Locate the sentence that gives the Maturidi view: that 'Kun' is an expression of speed of bringing into existence. Then find the Ash'ari view: that 'Kun' is speech and the world is created by it.
The contrast is between takwin as an attribute versus speech.
3
Trace the contradiction
Follow the author's reasoning: if the Ash'aris admit that the world's existence occurred through 'Kun', then they are affirming takwin in reality, even though they deny the name. That is a contradiction.
The author calls this 'a worse contradiction'.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author states that if this is not a contradiction, then nothing is. This shows how foundational the issue is. Reflect on why the Ash'ari denial of takwin matters for the overall theological system.
This argument is one of the famous 'contradictions of al-Ash'ari'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التكون، والإيجاد ما يتعلق به الوجود، وقد تعلق وجود العالم بخطاب "كن" فكان هو إيجادا وتكوينا وخلقا وهو غير المكون الموجود المخلوق غير أن أصحابنا يقولون : إن قوله "كن" عبارة عن سرعة الإيجاد من غير تعذر، والأشعري ومن تابعه من متكلمي أهل الحديث يقولون : إنه كلام وإن العالم خلق به. فإذا سلموا أن وجود العالم وتكونه حصل به فكان تكوينا وتخليقا، فمن أعطى الحقيقة ثم أنكر الاسم كان مناقضا ، وعد المتكلمون هذا من مناقضات الأشعري، وهذا لعمري أفحش مناقضة فإنه ينفي التكوين ثم يثبته ، ولو لم يكن هذا تناقضا فلا تناقض في عالم الله تعالى، وكل شبهة للأشعرية تبطل بهذا.
Takwin and ijad are what existence pertains to. The existence of the world is connected to the address "Kun" (Be), so it is creating, bringing into existence, and making, and it is other than the thing brought into existence, the existent, the created. However, our companions (the Maturidis) say that His saying "Kun" is an expression of the speed of bringing into existence without difficulty. Al-Ash'ari and his followers among the theologians of the People of Hadith say that it is speech (kalam) and that the world was created by it. So if they admit that the existence and coming-to-be of the world occurred through it, then it would be takwin and making. So whoever affirms the reality then denies the name is contradictory. The theologians count this among the contradictions of al-Ash'ari, and this, by my life, is a worse contradiction: he negates takwin then affirms it. If this is not a contradiction, then there is no contradiction in the entire world of Allah. And every doubt of the Ash'aris is invalidated by this.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage defines takwin and ijad as the attributes by which existence relates to things, specifically the existence of the world through the command "Kun". The author distinguishes between the act of bringing into existence (takwin) and the thing brought into existence (mukawwan). The Maturidi position is that "Kun" is an expression of instantaneous bringing into existence, not a separate speech act. The Ash'aris claim it is speech (kalam) and the world is created by it. The author points out a contradiction: if the Ash'aris admit the world's existence occurs through "Kun", they affirm takwin in reality even while denying the name. This is a contradiction because they deny takwin as an attribute yet affirm it in their explanation. The passage concludes that this invalidates all Ash'ari doubts.

Key Terms

إيجاد
كن
مكون
مناقضة
أشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Ash'aris and Maturidis agree on the nature of takwin, differing only in terminology.
Correction: The passage shows a substantive contradiction: the Ash'ari denial of takwin as an attribute clashes with their own explanation of creation through 'Kun', revealing a logical inconsistency that is more than a terminological difference.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi author, why is the Ash'ari position a contradiction?
A) They claim 'Kun' is created.
B) They deny takwin but their proof affirms it.
C) They say 'Kun' is a metaphor.
D) They reject the verse.

Key Takeaway
Denying an attribute while affirming its effect is a logical contradiction, and this single point strikes at the core of Ash'ari theology on creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The author says this contradiction is so severe that it invalidates all Ash'ari doubts. Is there any area of your faith where you have allowed a logical inconsistency to persist? How will you address it today?

Proof from the Verse 'Kun' for the Eternity of Speech and Takwin
Maturidi author turns Ash'ari proof for eternal speech into proof for eternal takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari proof from the verse 'Kun' for eternal speech also establishes the Maturidi attribute of takwin as eternal.

Core Idea
The same proof that shows speech is eternal also shows takwin is eternal.

This passage presents a clever argument used by both Ash'aris and Maturidis. The Ash'aris use the verse 'Kun' to prove that God's speech is eternal, but the author points out that this very argument also proves an eternal attribute of creating — which is exactly what the Maturidis call takwin. This shows that even the Ash'aris implicitly affirm takwin.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the tight logical structure.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Understand the Ash'ari argument
The Ash'aris argue that if 'Kun' were created, it would need another 'Kun', leading to infinite regress. Therefore, God's speech (including 'Kun') must be uncreated and eternal.
This is a classic proof for the eternity of speech.
3
See the author's twist
The author points out that this same proof shows there must be an eternal attribute by which creation occurs, which is exactly takwin. Thus, the Ash'aris have inadvertently proven takwin.
This is a clever sectarian move — using the opponent's own proof against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نحققه أنه ما من كتاب من كتب الأشعري أو أحد من أصحابه تكلموا فيه على المعتزلة في إثبات أزلية كلام الله تعالى إلا وقد تعلقوا بهذه الآية، وقالوا: إنه تعالى أخبر أن خلق المخلوقات بخطاب "كن" فلو كان خطاب "كن" مخلوقا لاحتاج إلى خطاب آخر، وكذا الثاني إلى الثالث إلى ما لا يتناهى، فدل أن الكلام غير مخلوق، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ثبت أنهم أثبتوا الله تعالى صفة أزلية يتعلق بها حدوث العالم، وهذا هو التكوين والإيجاد والخلق عند القائلين به وهذا ظاهر لا محيص عنه لمن أنصف ولم يكابر.
We verify that there is no book from the books of al-Ash'ari or any of his followers in which they argue against the Mu'tazila for the eternity of Allah's speech except that they have clung to this verse, and they say: He, exalted, informed that the creation of creatures is by the address 'Kun'. So if the address 'Kun' were created, it would need another address, and so the second to a third, ad infinitum. So it indicates that speech is uncreated. And if the matter is so, it is established that they have affirmed for Allah an eternal attribute by which the occurrence of the world is related. And this is exactly takwin, ijad, and khalq according to those who affirm it. And this is clear, with no escape for one who is fair and not obstinate.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage presents a proof accepted by both Ash'aris and Maturidis. The Ash'aris use the verse 'Kun' to prove that God's speech (kalam) is eternal because if it were created, it would require another speech, leading to infinite regress. The author points out that this same proof establishes an eternal attribute by which the world's coming into existence is related, which is precisely what the Maturidis call takwin. Thus, by the Ash'aris' own reasoning, they affirm takwin as an eternal attribute, contradicting their denial.

Misconception: The Ash'ari proof only proves the eternity of speech, not any attribute of creation.
Correction: The author demonstrates that the same logic proves an eternal attribute (takwin) by which the world comes into existence.

Checkpoint

A) That 'Kun' is a metaphor.
B) That the Ash'aris have proven the eternity of takwin.
C) That the Mu'tazila are correct.
D) That the world is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari proof for eternal speech from the verse 'Kun' simultaneously proves the eternity of the attribute of creating (takwin).

The Ruling on Swearing by the Creation of Allah
Al-Nasafi refutes opponent's consensus argument on swearing by 'khalq Allah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why swearing by 'creation of Allah' is not an oath by default, due to customary usage referring to the created thing, and how the Hanafi scholars distinguish between attribute and created in oaths.

Core Idea
The term 'creation' normally refers to the created, not the attribute.

This passage from al-Nasafi refutes an opponent who argued that swearing by 'creation of Allah' should be a valid oath because creation is an attribute of Allah. Al-Nasafi explains that the Hanafi jurists rely on customary usage: just as the term 'knowledge' is understood as the known object, 'creation' is understood as the created being. Only when the swearer explicitly intends the attribute does the oath become valid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the literal translation to get the flow of al-Nasafi's argument.
The passage is dense with legal reasoning.
2
Understand the analogy between 'ilm and khalq
Notice how al-Nasafi uses the example of swearing by 'knowledge of Allah' from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani to establish the principle: if the term is customarily used for the created thing, the oath is not valid unless the attribute is intended.
3
Identify the key distinction
The crucial point is that 'khalq' is normally understood as 'makhluq' (creation) in common usage. This is why swearing by it is not binding by default.
4
Examine the additional consensus arguments
Al-Nasafi addresses two more claims: the use of 'creation' in phrases like 'Creator of creation' and the alleged consensus on takfir. He shows these all rely on the same misunderstanding.
These are secondary points supporting the main argument.
5
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Summarize: The default ruling on oaths depends on customary usage, not the literal divine attribute reference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ذكر الحلف وما استدل به هذا الرجل بإجماع الفقهاء أن من حلف بصفة من صفات ذات الباري انعقدت يمينه وقول قال وخلق الله، لا يكون ذلك يمينا. كان ذلك لجهله بمذاهب خصومه في الفقه، فإن محمدا بن الحسن ذكر في أول صفحة من كتاب الإيمان من المبسوط أنه لو قال: وعلم الله لا يكون يمينا ولا خلاف أن العلم من صفات الذات ذلك لم يجعله يمينا، لما أن المتعارف كان عندهم أن العلم يذكر ويراد به المعلوم حاشية ومن المعلومات ما لا يحصى كثرة ولا ينعقد الحلف بها فلم يجوز له هذا، حتى إنه لو قال: أردت به العلم الذي هو صفة الله تعالى كان يمينا فكذلك إذا قال: وخلق الله، لأن الخلق يذكر ويراد به المخلوق بل المتعارف هذا هو على ما قررنا فلم ينعقد اليمين به لهذا، حتى إنه لو قال عنيت به صفة الله تعالى ينعقد يمينه كذا فسر مشايخنا الله هذه المسائل، فكان التعلق بمثل هذا جهلا محضا. وما استدل به من إجماع الناس أن الله تعالى خالق الخلق، وقولهم : اللهم راحم هذا الخلق فهو على إرادة المخلوقين ولا كلام فيه، فكان هذا الرجل لم يسمع من الناس استعمال الخصم والضيف والزور والعدل على إرادة الفاعل، والتعلق بهذا كله منه خيال لا يجدي به نفعا. وما قال : إن الناس أجمعوا على الكفار من امتنع من القول بأن الخلق غير الله. قلنا : ذلك إجماع من يصرف اسم الخلق إلى المخلوق، فأما من عرف أن الخلق صفة الله فلا نساعدهم على هذا الإكفار.
As for the mention of the oath and what this man adduced by the consensus of the jurists that whoever swears by an attribute of the attributes of the divine essence, his oath is binding, and it is said 'by the creation of Allah' (wa khalq Allah), that is not an oath. That was due to his ignorance of the doctrines of his opponents in fiqh. Indeed, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan mentioned in the first page of the Book of Oaths in al-Mabsut that if one says 'by the knowledge of Allah' (wa 'ilm Allah), it is not an oath, and there is no disagreement that knowledge is among the attributes of the essence; that did not make it an oath, because the customary practice among them was that 'knowledge' is mentioned and the known (al-ma'lum) is intended thereby—except that among the known things are countless things upon which an oath cannot be held, so he did not permit this. So much so that if he said 'I intended by it the knowledge that is an attribute of Allah, Exalted,' it would be an oath. Similarly, if he says 'by the creation of Allah,' because 'creation' (al-khalq) is mentioned and the created (al-makhluq) is intended thereby; rather, the custom is such as we have established, so the oath is not binding for this reason. So much so that if he said 'I intended by it the attribute of Allah, Exalted,' his oath would be binding. Thus did our teachers, may Allah have mercy on them, explain these issues. So adherence to such (objections) is pure ignorance. And what he adduced from the consensus of people that Allah, Exalted, is the Creator of the creation, and their saying 'O Allah, have mercy on this creation' — it is intended as the created beings, and there is no dispute. So this man has not heard from people the use of 'opponent' (khasm), 'guest' (dayf), 'falsehood' (zawr), and 'justice' ('adl) with the intention of the agent (al-fa'il). And adherence to all this from him is a delusion that brings no benefit. And what he said: 'The people have unanimously agreed upon declaring disbelief (takfir) of those who refrain from saying that creation is other than Allah.' We say: That is the consensus of those who apply the term 'creation' to the created being. As for those who know that 'creation' is an attribute of Allah, we do not assist them in this declaration of disbelief.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of an opponent's argument from juristic consensus regarding the validity of swearing by 'creation of Allah'. The author first points out the opponent's ignorance of the actual fiqh positions. Using the example of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, he shows that swearing by 'knowledge of Allah' is not an oath because the term is customarily used to refer to the known object, not the attribute. The same logic applies to 'creation': it is normally understood as the created thing. But if the swearer explicitly intends the attribute, then the oath becomes valid. The author then addresses two more consensus arguments. First, that phrases like 'Creator of creation' or 'have mercy on this creation' clearly refer to the created being, not the attribute. Second, that the alleged consensus on declaring disbelief for denying that creation is other than God only applies when 'creation' is taken as the created being, not as the attribute. Therefore, the opponent's arguments are based on linguistic misunderstanding and ignorance of the actual consensus.

Key Terms
الحلف
صفات الذات
الخلق
المخلوق
العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Swearing by 'creation of Allah' is always a valid oath because creation is an attribute of Allah.
Correction: In Hanafi fiqh, the validity depends on customary usage. Since 'khalq' normally means the created thing, the oath is not binding unless the attribute is explicitly intended.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is swearing by 'khalq Allah' not an oath by default?
A) Because 'khalq' is not an attribute of Allah.
B) Because 'khalq' is customarily used to refer to the created thing.
C) Because the Hanafi school does not allow oaths by any attribute.
D) Because the opponent's argument is based on ignorance.

Key Takeaway
Swearing by 'creation of Allah' is not a valid oath in Hanafi fiqh by default because the term is customarily understood to refer to the created being, not the attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you use the phrase 'creation of Allah' in daily speech, do you usually think of the created beings or the act of creating? How might this unconscious habit affect your understanding of the divine attributes? What will you do to align your speech with the more precise meaning when needed?
?
Have you ever judged someone's belief or practice based on a surface-level understanding of their words, without considering what they actually intended? How does al-Nasafi's careful distinction between custom and intention challenge you to be more charitable in interpreting others' statements about religion?
?
This lesson shows that even words like 'creation' can have multiple valid meanings, and that ignoring context and intention leads to false conclusions. In what area of your own life—whether in learning, dialogue, or worship—are you most prone to assuming a single meaning for a term, and how will you deliberately seek a deeper understanding from now on?

Refuting the Claim that 'Fa''āl' Implies Createdness
Refutes opponent's argument linking 'Fa''āl' to createdness of acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi refutes the claim that God's attribute 'Fa''āl' implies that the act itself is created, using linguistic and logical arguments.

Core Idea
Intensive divine attributes indicate multiplicity of objects, not the attribute itself.

This passage presents a sharp refutation of a theological error. An opponent argued that because God is described as 'Fa''āl' (intensive form of doer), His acts must be created. Imam al-Nasafi dismantles this argument by exposing its logical flaws and providing counterexamples from the Qur'an. You will see how careful attention to Arabic grammar and theological consistency defeats the claim.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponent's claim
Read the opponent's argument: God says 'Fa''āl limā yurīd' (Doer of what He wills), and the intensive form 'Fa''āl' indicates multiplicity, so whatever God wills must be created.
The opponent assumes that intensive forms imply multiplicity in the attribute itself.
2
Examine the counterexample with 'Allām'
Notice how al-Nasafi uses the parallel term 'Allām al-ghuyūb' (All-Knower of the unseen) to create a dilemma: if the opponent says knowledge is created, he joins the Jahmiyyah; if not, his proof collapses.
This shows the inconsistency in the opponent's reasoning.
3
Learn the correct interpretation of intensive forms
Al-Nasafi clarifies that 'Fa''āl' indicates multiplicity of God's effects (maf'ūlāt), not multiplicity of His act (fi'l). Similarly, 'Allām' indicates many known things, not many knowledges.
Intensive forms intensify the object, not the attribute.
4
Analyze the attachment of will
The opponent claimed will is attached to the act. Al-Nasafi responds that will is attached to what God does (the effect), not to His own act. The effect of will is the emergence of the effect, not the existence of the act from God.
5
Follow the dilemmas that expose absurdity
Al-Nasafi presents two further dilemmas: one about God willing not to give a share in the Hereafter, and another about willing not to create the world. In both, the opponent's principle fails.
These dilemmas show the extremes the opponent must accept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما قال: إن الله تعالى قال : فَعَالُ لِمَا يُرِيدُ والفعال للمبالغة والتكثير، ثم علق به الإرادة، وما تناولته الإرادة فهو مخلوق يدل هذا على غاية سخافة الرجل حيث ظن لنفسه في هذا دليلا يعتمد عليه وذلك أنه يقال له: أيش؟ فيكون الفعال للمبالغة والتكثير ما يدل على كون الفعل هو المفعول، أليس أن الله تعالى قال : عَلَّامُ الْغُيُوبِ أكان العلم مخلوقا؟ فإن قال : نعم، ترك مذهبه والتحق بالجهمية، وإن قال : لا ، أبطل دليله. ثم نقول : الفعال يدل على كثرة مفعولاته دون كثرة فعله، كما أن العلام يدل على كثرة معلوماته دون علمه، وكذا قدير للمبالغة وهو يدل على كثرة مقدوراته دون قدرته وقوله : علق به الإرادة قلنا: علق الإرادة بما يفعله لا بفعله إذ أثر الإرادة خروج المفعول على التتابع والتوالي، وكون الفاعل مختارا غير مضطر فيما يفعل لا وجود الفعل. ثم يقال له: أليس أن الله تعالى قال: يُرِيدُ اللهُ أَلَّا يَجْعَلَ لَهُمْ حَظًّا فِي الْآخِرَةِ فلابد من بلى. قيل له: أكان لا يجعل لهم حظا في الآخرة مخلوقا؟ فإن قال: نعم، فقد جعل أن لا يجعل مفعولا وهذا جهل. ثم نقول له: إن شاء الله تعالى لم يجعل العالم في الأزل هل كان أن لو لم يجعل مفعولا؟ فإن قال: نعم، فقد أثبت المخلوق في الأزل وهو كفر، وإن قال: لا، قيل أليس أن الله تعالى علق به الإرادة؟ فلابد أن يقول : بلى. فقيل له، فقد أبطلت إذا حجتك أن ما تعلقت به الإرادة فهو مخلوق، على أنا بينا أن تعلق الإرادة بالمفعول دون الفاعل، والله الموفق.
And he said: Indeed God said: 'Doer of what He wills' and 'Fa''āl' is for intensification and multiplication, then He attached will to it, and whatever the will encompasses is created. This indicates the extreme foolishness of the man, as he thought he had a reliable proof in this. For it is said to him: What? So that 'Fa''āl' for intensification and multiplication indicates that the act is the effect. Is it not that God said: 'All-Knower of the unseen'? Was knowledge created? If he says: Yes, he leaves his school and joins the Jahmiyyah; if he says: No, he invalidates his proof. Then we say: 'Fa''āl' indicates multiplicity of His effects, not multiplicity of His act, just as 'Allām' indicates multiplicity of His known things without His knowledge, and similarly 'Qadīr' for intensification indicates multiplicity of His objects of power without His power. And his statement: He attached will to it—we say: He attached will to what He does, not to His act, for the effect of will is the emergence of the effect successively and consecutively, and that the agent is free and not compelled in what he does, not the existence of the act. Then it is said to him: Did not God say: 'God wills not to give them any share in the Hereafter'? So he must say yes. It is said to him: Was 'not to give them a share in the Hereafter' created? If he says: Yes, then he made 'not to give' an effect, and this is ignorance. Then we say to him: If God willed not to create the world in pre-eternity, would 'if He had not created' be an effect? If he says: Yes, he affirms a created thing in pre-eternity, which is disbelief; if he says: No, it is said: Did not God attach will to it? So he must say yes. So it is said to him: Then you have invalidated your proof that whatever will is attached to is created, whereas we have shown that will is attached to the effect, not to the agent. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage refutes an opponent's argument that the Qur'anic term 'Fa''āl' (intensive form of 'doer') implies that the act itself is the object of God's action, and thus everything God wills is created. The author (Imam al-Nasafi) begins by stating the opponent's claim: God says 'Fa''āl limā yurīd' (Doer of what He wills), and the intensive form indicates multiplicity, so whatever God wills is created. He then exposes the folly of this argument by asking: if 'Fa''āl' implies the act is the object, then consider 'Allām al-ghuyūb' (All-Knower of the unseen). Does that mean knowledge is created? The opponent cannot consistently say yes without adopting Jahmi doctrine, and if he says no, his proof collapses. Next, the author clarifies that intensive forms like 'Fa''āl', 'Allām', and 'Qadīr' indicate multiplicity of the objects (effects, known things, objects of power), not multiplicity of the attribute itself. As for the opponent's point that the will is attached, the author explains: God's will is attached to what He does (the act as a whole), not to His own attribute of acting. The effect of will is the actualization of the effect, not the existence of the act from God. Then the author presents another dilemma: God says 'God wills not to give them a share...' If the opponent says that 'not giving' is created, he absurdly makes a negation an effect; if he says it is not created, then his general principle fails. Finally, the author raises the case of God willing not to create the world in pre-eternity: if the opponent says the non-creation is created, he affirms a created thing in pre-eternity (disbelief); if he says no, then his principle is again broken because will was attached to it. Thus the opponent's argument that whatever will is attached to is created is invalidated. The author concludes that will attaches to the effect, not to the agent.

Key Terms
فعَّال (Fa''āl)
علَّام (Allām)
الإرادة (al-irāda)
المفعول (al-maf'ūl)
الفعل (al-fi'l)
المبالغة (al-mubālagha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The intensive form of a divine attribute implies multiplicity or change in the attribute itself.
Correction: Intensive forms like 'Fa''āl' and 'Allām' indicate multiplicity of the attribute's objects (effects, known things), not multiplicity in the attribute itself.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Nasafi, what does 'Fa''āl' primarily indicate?
A) Multiplicity of God's acts.
B) Multiplicity of God's effects (maf'ūlāt).
C) That God's act is created.
D) That God's will is attached to His essence.

Key Takeaway
Intensive divine attributes denote abundance of their objects, not multiplicity in the attribute itself, so 'Fa''āl' does not imply that God's act is created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that God is 'Fa''āl limā yurīd', do you ever subconsciously imagine His act as something that unfolds in time like human acts? How does this lesson correct that, and what must you do to affirm that His act is eternal and not created?
?
The opponent's mistake was projecting a grammatical intensive form onto God's essence. Have you ever understood a divine attribute in a way that limited God's transcendence? What concrete step will you take today to study the creed of the righteous predecessors to avoid such errors?
?
If someone were to tell you that 'intensive forms imply createdness', how would this lesson equip you to respond? Are you prepared to defend the eternal attributes with the same clarity shown here? Commit to explaining this argument to one person this week.

Nasafi's Dialectical Argument: Fi'l as Speech and Divine Eternity
Nasafi presents a conditional refutation using the grammarians' definition of fi'l.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the grammarians' definition of 'fi'l' as speech to refute the opponent's claim that God's acts are contingent.

Core Idea
If fi’l is speech, then God’s act is eternal—a dialectical trap.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses an opponent who relies on grammatical definitions. He turns the tables by showing that if we accept the grammarians' equation of 'fi'l' with 'kalim' (speech), then God's acts—being speech—would be eternal, contradicting the opponent's own position. This clever argument forces the opponent into a dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the structure of the argument come through.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if...then...'.
2
Identify the grammarians' division
The passage divides speech into two categories: definition (ta'rif) and obligation (taklif). Note the subdivisions: informing (ikhbar) with tenses, and command/prohibition.
This division sets up the premise that fi'l equals speech.
3
Follow the conditional logic
Nasafi applies the premise: if the opponent accepts the grammarians' definition, then God's act (fi'l) is speech, which is eternal, so God's act is eternal. This contradicts the opponent's view.
The second conditional: if the opponent rejects the definition, their own argument fails.
4
Reflect on the dialectical method
Consider why Nasafi is not endorsing the definition but using it as a rhetorical tool to expose inconsistency.
This shows the importance of understanding dialectical arguments in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول له : الفعل عند النحويين هو الكلام، وهو ينقسم إلى قسمين: تعريف وتكليف، ويعني بالتعريف الإخبار، وهو ينقسم انقسام الأزمنة وهي الماضي والقائم والآتي مثل ضرب زيد أمس وهو ضرب للحال، وسيضرب غدا. والتكليف ينقسم إلى إيجاب وهو الأمر، وإلى منع وهو النهي. وهذا كله من أقسام الكلام، ولهذا يقال في أقسام الكلام: إنه خبر واستخبار وأمر ونهي . فإن كنت أخذت بقول أهل اللغة، ففعل الله إذا كلامه وكلامه أزلي بلا خلاف بيننا وبينكم فكان فعل الله أزليا، ولو كان الفعل حادثا عندك لكان الكلام حادثا ، فإن لم تقبل هذا من أهل اللغة بطل إلزامك
Then we say to him: The act/verb (fi'l) according to the grammarians is speech (kalim), and it is divided into two parts: definition (ta'rif) and obligation (taklif). By definition he means informing (ikhbar), and it is divided according to the division of tenses: past, present, and future, like 'Zaid struck yesterday' and 'he is striking now' and 'he will strike tomorrow'. Obligation is divided into command (ijab) which is the imperative (amr), and prohibition (man') which is the forbidding (nahy). All of these are divisions of speech, and therefore it is said of the divisions of speech: it is information (khabar), interrogation (istikhbar), command (amr), and prohibition (nahy). So if you accept the statement of the linguists, then God's act is His speech, and His speech is eternal without dispute between us and you, so God's act would be eternal. And if the act were contingent according to you, then speech would be contingent. But if you do not accept this from the linguists, then your objection is invalid.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage presents a hypothetical argument aimed at the opponent who had appealed to grammatical definitions. Nasafi states that according to grammarians, 'fi'l' (verb/act) is synonymous with 'kalim' (speech). Grammarians divide speech into two categories: definition (ta'rif) and obligation (taklif). Definition includes informing (ikhbar), which is further divided by tense (past, present, future). Obligation includes command and prohibition. Thus, all these are types of speech. Nasafi then applies this: if the opponent accepts the grammarians' definition, then God's 'fi'l' (act) would be His speech (since fi'l = kalim). Since Muslims agree God's speech is eternal, then God's act would be eternal. But the opponent holds that God's acts are contingent (hadith). This would be a contradiction: if God's act is eternal, then the opponent's claim that it is contingent fails. Alternatively, if the opponent rejects the grammarians' definition, then they cannot use that same definition to support their own argument against Nasafi. Either way, the opponent's position is undermined.

كلام
تعريف
تكليف
خبر
أمر
نهي
أزلي
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Nasafi believes that fi'l and kalim are identical in all contexts.
Correction: Nasafi is employing the grammarians' definition as a dialectical tool to refute the opponent, not necessarily endorsing it as his own view.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's argument, what follows if the opponent accepts the grammarians' definition of fi'l as speech?
A) God's act becomes contingent.
B) God's act becomes eternal.
C) The opponent's argument is strengthened.
D) The grammarians are proven wrong.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's argument uses the opponent's own grammatical definitions to force a contradiction, showing that God's act must be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you argue for a theological truth, do you more often seek to win the argument or to arrive at the truth? Nasafi's dialectical method presses the opponent to admit inconsistency. Examine your own heart: would you be willing to surrender a cherished position if it were shown to be self-contradictory? How would you respond if someone used your own definitions against you? Commit today to pursue truth over victory.
?
This passage shows that even language points to the eternity of God's actions. When you speak of God's doing something, do you consciously remember that His actions are not bound by time? Or do you think of Him as acting within your temporal framework? This very moment, reflect on the eternal nature of God's act and let it reshape how you speak about Him in your prayers and conversations.
?
Nasafi's argument forces the opponent to choose: either accept the grammarians' definition and conclude that God's act is eternal, or reject it and lose the basis for their own objection. Are there areas in your life where you cling to definitions or assumptions that, if examined, would force you to change your beliefs? Are you willing to let go of comfortable but inconsistent positions for the sake of consistency with divine truth? Identify one such assumption today and resolve to test it.

The Rational Proof for the Preeternity of التكوين (Part 1)
Nasafi presents the first part of a rational proof for the preeternity of التكوين.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Nasafi's rational argument that the attribute of creative bringing into existence (التكوين) must be preeternal because otherwise creation would be independent of God, leading to the preeternity of the world.

Core Idea
Without an eternal attribute of creation, priority alone cannot make God a Creator.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi begins the rational proof for the preeternity of التكوين. After refuting scriptural and consensus-based objections, he lays down a logical argument: since 'Creator' is a description of Allah, there must be a real meaning by which He is Creator. Denying this meaning forces the conclusion that the world exists by itself and hence is preeternal—a consequence the opponents themselves would reject.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the argument. Then read the translation. Note how Nasafi sets up the shared premise and then exposes the logical consequence of the opponents' view.
Pay attention to the example of Zayd and 'Amr.
2
Identify the agreed premise
All Muslims agree that Allah is the Creator. Nasafi uses this to argue that 'Creator' implies a real attribute (معنى) in Allah.
3
Understand the opponents' position
The Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, and Najjariyya deny any attribute of creation in Allah; they claim the act of creation is identical to the created thing itself.
4
Follow the refutation through analogy
Mere priority in time does not make one a creator. The example of Zayd and 'Amr shows that without a specific act, priority is insufficient.
Similarly, power without connection to action does not make one an agent.
5
Grasp the implication
If the world's existence is by itself (not through an attribute of Allah), then it would be preeternal. Thus the opponents inadvertently affirm the world's preeternity.
This is the key move: denying التكوين leads to the very conclusion the opponents wish to avoid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل العقلي على قدم التكوين وإبطال شبه الخصوم العقلية] وقد فرغنا من إبطال شبههم السمعية والإجماعية واللغوية، فنشتغل بعد هذا ببيان حجتنا العقلية وإبطال شبههم العقلية فنقول: أجمع المسلمون على أن خالق العالم هو الله تعالى ولا شك أن الخالق وصف منا لله تعالى لا بد من وجود معنى يكون به خالقا ثم عند المخالفين لنا من المعتزلة والأشعرية والنجارية لم يكن من الله تعالى إلى العالم معنى يتصف هو بكونه خالقا والعالم بكونه مخلوقا، إذ المعنى لو كان لكان هو الخلق والإيجاد، وذلك هو عين الموجود المخلوق، لا معنى قائم بذات الله تعالى. فإذا كان وجود العالم بالعلم لا بالله تعالى إذ لم يكن منه إليه معنى سوى أنه أقدم من العالم، ووجود شيء ما لا يجعل من هو أقدم منه خالقا له إذا لم يكن منه معنى إليه يكون به خالقا لتكوين زيد بعد عمرو ولا يجعل عمرا خالقا لزيد، وإن كان أقدم منه إذا لم يكن منه إليه صنع، وكذا القدرة لا توجب كون القادر فاعلا إذا لم يتصل بها الفعل، ألا ترى أنه كان في الأزل قادرا ولم يكن خالقا ولم يثبت مخلوق، وكذا العلم لا ألا ترى بالباري بل كان وجوده بنفسه، وما كان وجوده بنفسه لا بغيره فهو قديم، فكان القول بهذا موجبا القول بقدم العالم فكانوا هم القائلين بقدم العالم لا نحن. والثاني: أن وجوده لو كان بنفسه أو بمعنى راجع إلى ذاته لا إلى غيره
The rational proof for the preeternity of creative bringing into existence (التكوين) and the invalidation of the opponents' intellectual doubts. And we have finished invalidating their scriptural, consensus-based, and linguistic doubts, so we engage after this in presenting our rational proof and invalidating their intellectual doubts. We say: The Muslims are agreed that the Creator of the world is Allah Most High, and there is no doubt that 'the Creator' is an attribute of ours for Allah Most High; there must necessarily be a meaning by which He is Creator. Then according to our opponents among the Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, and Najjariyya, there is from Allah Most High to the world no meaning by which He is qualified as Creator and the world as created, for if the meaning existed, it would be the act of creation and bringing into existence, and that is the very same as the created existent, not a meaning subsisting in the essence of Allah Most High. So if the existence of the world is through knowledge, not through Allah Most High, since there is from Him to it no meaning other than that He is prior to the world, and the existence of something does not make one who is prior to it a creator of it if there is from Him no meaning to it by which He is a creator — for the bringing into existence of Zayd after 'Amr does not make 'Amr a creator of Zayd, even if he is prior to him, if there is from him to him no act — and likewise power does not necessitate that the powerful one is an agent if the action is not connected to it. Do you not see that He was powerful in preeternity and was not Creator, and no created thing was established, and likewise knowledge... Do you not see by the Creator? Rather, its existence was by itself, and what exists by itself not by another is preeternal. So saying this necessitates saying the preeternity of the world; thus they are the ones saying the world is preeternal, not we. And the second: that its existence, if it were by itself or by a meaning reverting to its essence not to other than it...
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a rational proof for the preeternity of God's attribute of التكوين (creative bringing into existence). Nasafi first announces that he has already refuted the opponents' doubts from scripture, consensus, and language, and now turns to the rational proof. He begins with a premise agreed upon by all Muslims: that Allah is the Creator of the world. 'Creator' is a description of Allah, so there must be some real meaning (معنى) in Allah by which He is Creator. The opponents (Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, Najjariyya) deny that there is any meaning proceeding from Allah to the world; they claim that if such a meaning existed, it would be identical to the created being itself, not an eternal attribute in Allah. Consequently, they hold that the world's existence is through God's knowledge and His priority, not through an attribute like التكوين. Nasafi argues that mere priority in time does not make one the creator of something else: Zayd's existence after 'Amr does not make 'Amr the creator of Zayd. Similarly, power alone does not make one an agent unless the action is connected; God was powerful in preeternity but not yet creating. He then makes a key point: if the world's existence were by itself (بنفسه) or by an attribute inherent in its essence, then it would be preeternal, because what exists by itself is necessarily preeternal. This would mean the world is preeternal, a conclusion the opponents would have to accept. Thus, the opponents inadvertently become the ones who affirm the world's preeternity, not the Maturidis. The passage ends with the beginning of a second argument (والثاني) but is cut off.

Key Terms
التكوين
خالق
قدم
معنى
العلم
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's priority in time (being prior to the world) is sufficient for Him to be the Creator.
Correction: Nasafi argues that priority alone does not make one a creator; an actual attribute of creation (التكوين) must connect God to the act of creation.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, what conclusion does the opponents' denial of an attribute of creation lead to?
A) God is not the Creator.
B) The world is preeternal.
C) The world is created in time.
D) God's power is limited.

Key Takeaway
The attribute of التكوين is preeternal because without it, creation would be independent of God, leading to the preeternity of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if your very existence is being constantly created by God through His eternal attribute of takwin, or do you feel self-sufficient and independent? What specific change in your daily attitude would result from truly believing that without God's continuous creative act, you would cease to exist?
?
When you face a trial or a need, do you rely solely on the abstract concept that 'God has power', or do you actively seek His creative intervention in your life? How can you personally turn to the attribute of takwin in your du'a and trust that He is actively creating solutions for you?
?
If you were to truly internalize that priority in time does not make one a creator without an actual act, how would that transform your understanding of your own role in your achievements? Are you attributing your successes to your own precedence or effort, or to Allah's continuous act of creation? Commit to one specific way to remind yourself daily that you are being created by Allah at every moment.

The Necessity of Takwin as a Meaning in Allah
Author states the necessity of a creative meaning in Allah and the opponents' denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that there must be a meaning of creation (takwin) in Allah's essence, and how this contrasts with the opponents' view that creation is identical to the created thing.

Core Idea
Allah's attribute of creation is a real meaning in His essence, not the created thing itself.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the rational foundation for believing that takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) is eternal and subsisting in Allah's essence. He begins by noting the universal Muslim consensus that Allah is the Creator, then argues that the description 'Creator' requires a real meaning in Him by which He creates. The opponents—Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, and Najjariyya—deny this meaning, claiming it would be identical to the created thing. Understanding this disagreement is key to grasping the Maturidi position on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Focus on the opening lines where the author states the consensus and the opponents' denial.
2
Identify the key claim
The author asserts there must be a meaning (ma'na) in Allah by which He is Creator. Contrast with opponents who say the act of creation is the same as the created thing.
3
Reflect on the implication
Why does the author insist on a meaning separate from the created thing? What does this preserve about Allah's attributes?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل العقلي على قدم التكوين وإبطال شبه الخصوم العقلية وقد فرغنا من إبطال شبههم السمعية والإجماعية واللغوية، فنشتغل بعد هذا ببيان حجتنا العقلية وإبطال شبههم العقلية فنقول: أجمع المسلمون على أن خالق العالم هو الله تعالى ولا شك أن الخالق وصف منا لله تعالى لا بد من وجود معنى يكون به خالقا ثم عند المخالفين لنا من المعتزلة والأشعرية والنجارية لم يكن من الله تعالى إلى العالم معنى يتصف هو بكونه خالقا والعالم بكونه مخلوقا، إذ المعنى لو كان لكان هو الخلق والإيجاد، وذلك هو عين الموجود المخلوق، لا معنى قائم بذات الله تعالى. فإذا كان وجود العالم بالعلم لا بالله تعالى إذ لم يكن منه إليه معنى سوى أنه أقدم من العالم، ووجود شيء ما لا يجعل من هو أقدم منه خالقا له إذا لم يكن منه إليه صنع، وكذا القدرة لا توجب كون القادر فاعلا إذا لم يتصل بها الفعل، أنه كان في الأزل قادرا ولم يكن خالقا ولم يثبت مخلوق، وكذا العلم لا ألا ترى بالباري بل كان وجوده بنفسه، وما كان وجوده بنفسه لا بغيره فهو قديم، فكان القول بهذا موجبا القول بقدم العالم فكانوا هم القائلين بقدم العالم لا نحن. والثاني: أن وجوده لو كان بنفسه أو بمعنى راجع إلى ذاته لا إلى غيره لكان حادثا لا بغيره، فلم يدل على غير أوجده، فكان القول به قولا بنفي الصانع.
The rational proof for the eternity of takwin and the refutation of the opponents' rational doubts. And we have finished refuting their textual, consensus-based, and linguistic doubts, so after this we engage in presenting our rational proof and refuting their rational doubts, saying: The Muslims are agreed that the Creator of the world is Allah Almighty, and there is no doubt that 'the Creator' is an attribute of ours for Allah Almighty; there must be a meaning by which He is Creator. Then according to our opponents from the Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, and Najjariyya, there is no meaning from Allah Almighty to the world by which He is described as Creator and the world as created, because if there were a meaning, it would be the act of creation and bringing into existence, and that is exactly the existent created thing, not a meaning subsisting in the essence of Allah Almighty. So if the existence of the world is by something other than Allah Almighty, since there is no meaning from Him to it except that He is prior to the world, and the existence of something does not make that which is prior to it its creator if there is no act from it to it, similarly power does not necessitate that the powerful one is an agent if the act is not connected to it. Do you not see that He was powerful in pre-eternity and was not Creator, and no created thing existed; similarly knowledge does not ... rather its existence was by itself, and what exists by itself and not by another is eternal, so saying this entails saying the world is eternal, so they are the ones who say the world is eternal, not we. And the second: if its existence were by itself or by a meaning returning to its essence not to another, it would be originated not by another, so it would not indicate one who brought it into existence, so saying this is a saying negating the Maker.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage presents the rational proof for the eternity of the attribute of creation (takwin) and refutes the rational arguments of opponents. The author begins by stating the consensus that Allah is the Creator, and then argues that there must be a meaning (ma'na) in Allah by which He is Creator. The opponents (Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, Najjariyya) deny this meaning, claiming that if it existed it would be identical to the created thing. The author then draws out two consequences of their denial. First, if the world's existence is not from Allah but from itself, then it would be eternal—thus the opponents inadvertently affirm the eternity of the world. Second, if the world's existence is from itself or from a meaning returning to its essence, it would be originated without an originator, which denies the existence of the Creator. The author emphasizes that mere priority in time does not make something a creator without an act, and power alone does not make one an agent without connection to the act. The proof is structured as a reductio ad absurdum, showing the opponents' position leads to either shirk (eternity of world) or atheism (denial of Creator).

Key Terms
تكوين
خالق
معنى
المخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah's attribute of creation is just the act of creating, which is the same as the created thing.
Correction: The Maturidi view distinguishes the eternal attribute of takwin from the temporal created things; the attribute is a meaning in Allah's essence, not identical to the effect.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the opponents (Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, Najjariyya) claim about the meaning of creation?
A) It is a real meaning subsisting in Allah's essence.
B) If it existed, it would be identical to the created thing.
C) It is the act of creating separate from the creature.
D) It is an eternal attribute of Allah.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi argument begins by insisting that 'Creator' must refer to a real, eternal meaning in Allah's essence, not merely to the created effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's attribute of being Creator is a real, eternal meaning in His essence, or do you unknowingly reduce it to a past event? What must change in your heart so that you feel His creative power present now, not just at the beginning of time? Write down one practical step you will take this week to remind yourself of this.
?
The opponents' argument can feel logical: if the attribute were real, it would be the created thing. Have you ever thought something similar about Allah's attributes—that they are just descriptions of His actions, not realities in His essence? How might this lesson correct that thought in a way that brings you closer to Allah? Commit to memorizing the Arabic phrase that refutes this: 'لا معنى قائم بذات الله تعالى' and reflect on it daily.
?
If the attribute of creation were not real in Allah, then He would become a Creator only at the moment of creation. Does your worship reflect a belief in an eternally perfect and powerful Creator, or one who is only powerful when He acts? How will you align your belief about Allah's attributes with the Maturidi position—explain it to yourself in your own words and share it with one person this week.

The Absurd Consequences of Denying Takwin
Author presents a reductio ad absurdum with two branches proving the necessity of takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two absurd conclusions that follow from denying the attribute of takwin in Allah, and how the author uses these to prove that takwin must be eternal.

Core Idea
Denying takwin leads either to affirming the eternity of the world or denying the existence of the Creator.

Having established the necessity of a creative meaning in Allah, Imam al-Nasafi now exposes the irrational consequences of the opponents' denial. He shows that if the world's existence is not from Allah through a real meaning, then either the world is eternal (because it exists by itself) or it has no originator (if it exists by a meaning returning to itself). Both conclusions are unacceptable to Muslims, thus the opponents' position is self-defeating.

Guided Path
1
Read the reductio argument
Notice how the author presents two scenarios.
2
Analyze each scenario
First, if the world exists by itself, it is eternal. Second, if it exists by a meaning returning to itself, it is originated without an originator.
3
Connect to the conclusion
The author concludes that the opponents themselves would be forced to accept the eternity of the world or atheism, which they reject.

Source Text

?

Which of these two does your mind secretly lean towards when you forget this teaching?
