The Principle of Derived Names in Kalam
Author verifies principle of derived names with examples and notes agreement with Ash'aris.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi principle that derived names apply to the one in whom the meaning (ma'na) subsists, and how this principle is agreed upon between Maturidis and Ash'aris.

Core Idea
Derived names require the meaning to actually exist in the subject.

The author begins by verifying the logical grounding of names like 'Creator' and 'Existent', showing that they are derived from meanings that must be present in the entity described. This principle is foundational for understanding divine attributes and will later be used to critique sectarian views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses examples from everyday language.
2
Identify the derived names and their bases
The passage lists several derived names: 'Creator' from creation, 'eater' from eating, 'striker' from striking, 'existent' from bringing into existence, 'stationary' from stationariness, etc. See how each is linked to a meaning that subsists in the subject.
3
Recognize the agreement with Ash'aris
The passage states that agreement on this principle was reached between 'us' (Maturidis) and the Ash'ariyya. Make a mental note that both schools share this foundational view.
This agreement will be contrasted later with their inconsistent practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه : أن الخالق اسم مشتق من الخلق، كالأكل اسم مشتق من الأكل، والضارب من الضرب، وكذا الموجود من الإيجاد ثم عندنا الاسم المشتق من معنى يكون وصفا لمن قام به المعنى أو لمن له المعنى بأن كان المعنى راجعا إلى الذات، كالساكن اسم لما قام به السكون، وكذا الحركة والسواد والموجود اسم لمن كان وجوده راجعا إلى ذاته. وانعقد الاتفاق على هذه الجملة بيننا وبين الأشعرية. إلى ونسبنا جميعا المعتزلة إلى الجهل حيث زعموا أن المتكلم اسم لموجد الكلام لا للمحل الذي قام به الكلام، والكافر اسم لفاعل الكفر لا لمن قام به الكفر. وادعينا التناقض والخروج عن المعقول حيث ساعدونا على أن المتحرك من قامت به الحركة لا من أوجدها ، وكذا الساكن والأسود والأبيض والحي والميت والصحيح والفاسد والمريض . ثم إن هؤلاء الأشعرية تركت هذا الأصل وزعمت أن الخالق غير من قام به الخلق، والموجد غير من قام به الإيجاد وهذا تناقض ظاهر وترك لأصول أهل الحق بل خروج عن إجماع العقلاء والمعتزلة في هذه المسألة أسعد حالا منهم، فإنهم وقعوا فيما وقعوا لإلجاء أصلهم الفاسد في استحالة قيام معنى بذات الله تعالى إلى هذا، وهذا الإلجاء في حق الأشعرية منعدم فإنهم ساعدونا على وجود القول بقيام الصفات بذات الباري جل وعلا. والثاني: أن المعتزلة جروا على هذا الأصل في بعض المواضع وهو مسألة الكلام حيث جعلوا المتكلم من أوجد الكلام لا من قام به الكلام، وكذا جعلوا الكافر
Its verification: that 'the Creator' is a noun derived from creation, just as 'the eater' is a noun derived from eating, and 'the striker' from striking, and similarly 'the existent' from bringing into existence. Then according to us, the derived noun from a meaning is a description for the one in whom the meaning subsists or for the one to whom the meaning belongs, such that the meaning returns to the essence, like 'the stationary' is a noun for that in which stationariness subsists, and similarly movement and blackness, and 'the existent' is a noun for one whose existence returns to his essence. And agreement was reached on this principle between us and the Ash'ariyya. And we all attributed ignorance to the Mu'tazila where they claimed that 'the speaker' is a noun for the one who brings about speech, not for the locus in which speech subsists, and 'the disbeliever' is a noun for the doer of disbelief, not for the one in whom disbelief subsists. And we claimed contradiction and departure from reason where they agreed with us that 'the moving' is that in which movement subsists, not the one who brings it about, and similarly 'the stationary', 'the black', 'the white', 'the living', 'the dead', 'the healthy', 'the corrupt', and 'the sick'. Then these Ash'ariyya abandoned this principle and claimed that 'the Creator' is other than the one in whom creation subsists, and 'the bringer into existence' is other than the one in whom bringing into existence subsists, and this is a clear contradiction and abandonment of the principles of the people of truth, rather a departure from the consensus of rational people. And the Mu'tazila in this matter are in a better state than them, for they fell into what they fell into due to the constraint of their corrupt principle of the impossibility of a meaning subsisting in the essence of Allah Almighty, but this constraint does not apply to the Ash'ariyya, for they agreed with us on the existence of the statement of the subsistence of attributes in the essence of Allah, Exalted and Majestic. And the second: that the Mu'tazila followed this principle in some places, namely the issue of speech, where they made 'the speaker' the one who brings about speech, not the one in whom speech subsists, and similarly they made 'the disbeliever' ...
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage provides a verification (tahqiq) of the principle of derived names and then uses it to criticize both the Ash'ariyya and the Mu'tazila for inconsistency. The author begins by stating that names like 'Creator', 'existent', etc., are derived from a meaning (ma'na) that must subsist in the subject. They illustrate with examples: 'stationary' applies to that in which stationariness resides, not to one who merely causes stationariness. The author notes that the Ash'ariyya agree with this principle in general, and they all accuse the Mu'tazila of ignorance for reversing it in cases like 'speaker' (they say speaker is one who creates speech, not the locus). But then the author points out a contradiction: the Ash'ariyya themselves abandon this principle when it comes to 'Creator', claiming that the Creator is not the one in whom creation subsists. This is a clear contradiction and a departure from the consensus of rational people. The Ash'ariyya have no excuse, since they already accept that attributes subsist in Allah's essence. The author then begins a second point criticizing the Mu'tazila for applying this principle inconsistently (e.g., in the case of speech they follow it, but they deny it for creation). The passage cuts off mid-sentence, but the argument is that the Mu'tazila also contradict themselves.

Key Terms
مشتق
اسم
خالق
إيجاد
معنى
قيام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the principle for derived names?
A) A derived name applies to the one who brings about the meaning.
B) A derived name applies to the one in whom the meaning subsists or to whom the meaning returns.
C) A derived name applies arbitrarily based on convention.
D) A derived name applies only to objects, not to God.

Key Takeaway
Derived names like 'Creator' must be applied to the one in whom the corresponding attribute actually exists, not merely the one who brings it about.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the name 'Creator' requires that the attribute of creation subsists in Allah eternally, does your heart truly recognize that He is never not creating, that His creative power is inherent to His being? Or do you sometimes think of creation as a one-time act, distant from His essence? How would your awe shift if you meditated on the fact that at every moment, creation flows from an eternal attribute within Him, not just a past event?
?
The passage says 'the existent' is a name for one whose existence returns to his essence. For Allah, existence is His essence. For you, your existence is entirely derived from Him. Do you live with a constant, felt awareness that you are only existing this very moment because He holds you in existence? Or do you walk as if existence is your right? What would change today if you truly owned that you are not self-existent?
?
The Ash'aris agreed on this principle but later failed to apply it consistently to all divine names. Are you consistent in your understanding of Allah's names? Do you affirm, for example, that 'al-Rahim' (the Merciful) requires mercy to be a real, eternal attribute subsisting in Him, or do you think of it as just a description of His actions? How would your reliance on His mercy deepen if you believed that mercy is eternally within Him, not just expressed temporally?

intermediate
7 min
Refuting Inconsistency in Ash'ari and Mu'tazili Views on Derived Names
Author criticizes Mu'tazili and Ash'ari inconsistency in applying derived names principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the principle of derived names to expose contradictions in both Ash'ari and Mu'tazili positions.

Core Idea
Both Ash'aris and Mu'tazilis abandoned their own principles inconsistently.

After establishing the agreed principle, the author turns to criticize the Mu'tazila for reversing it in cases like 'speaker' and 'disbeliever'. Surprisingly, he then finds the Ash'aris equally guilty when they deny that 'Creator' applies to the one in whom creation subsists. This lesson explores this double critique and the asymmetry in their excuses.

Guided Path
1
Review the principle from Lesson 1
Remind yourself of the principle: a derived name applies to the one in whom the meaning subsists. This is essential to follow the critique.
2
Identify the Mu'tazili inconsistency
The author says the Mu'tazila claim 'the speaker' is the one who brings about speech, not the locus of speech. Similarly for 'disbeliever' – they take it as the doer of disbelief, not the one in whom disbelief subsists. This contradicts their own acceptance of the principle for other names like 'stationary'.
The author accuses them of ignorance and contradiction.
3
Identify the Ash'ari inconsistency
Even worse, the Ash'aris who agreed on the principle now abandon it for 'Creator' and 'bringer into existence', claiming these apply to the one who creates, not the one in whom creation subsists. The author calls this a clear contradiction and a departure from consensus.
Note the irony: Ash'aris criticized the Mu'tazila but commit the same error.
4
Understand the asymmetry of excuses
The author argues that the Mu'tazila at least have an excuse: their corrupt principle that no meaning can subsist in Allah. But the Ash'aris accept that attributes subsist in Allah, so they have no excuse for their inconsistency.
This means the Ash'ari position is worse in the author's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه : أن الخالق اسم مشتق من الخلق، كالأكل اسم مشتق من الأكل، والضارب من الضرب، وكذا الموجود من الإيجاد ثم عندنا الاسم المشتق من معنى يكون وصفا لمن قام به المعنى أو لمن له المعنى بأن كان المعنى راجعا إلى الذات، كالساكن اسم لما قام به السكون، وكذا الحركة والسواد والموجود اسم لمن كان وجوده راجعا إلى ذاته. وانعقد الاتفاق على هذه الجملة بيننا وبين الأشعرية. إلى ونسبنا جميعا المعتزلة إلى الجهل حيث زعموا أن المتكلم اسم لموجد الكلام لا للمحل الذي قام به الكلام، والكافر اسم لفاعل الكفر لا لمن قام به الكفر. وادعينا التناقض والخروج عن المعقول حيث ساعدونا على أن المتحرك من قامت به الحركة لا من أوجدها ، وكذا الساكن والأسود والأبيض والحي والميت والصحيح والفاسد والمريض . ثم إن هؤلاء الأشعرية تركت هذا الأصل وزعمت أن الخالق غير من قام به الخلق، والموجد غير من قام به الإيجاد وهذا تناقض ظاهر وترك لأصول أهل الحق بل خروج عن إجماع العقلاء والمعتزلة في هذه المسألة أسعد حالا منهم، فإنهم وقعوا فيما وقعوا لإلجاء أصلهم الفاسد في استحالة قيام معنى بذات الله تعالى إلى هذا، وهذا الإلجاء في حق الأشعرية منعدم فإنهم ساعدونا على وجود القول بقيام الصفات بذات الباري جل وعلا. والثاني: أن المعتزلة جروا على هذا الأصل في بعض المواضع وهو مسألة الكلام حيث جعلوا المتكلم من أوجد الكلام لا من قام به الكلام، وكذا جعلوا الكافر
Its verification: that 'the Creator' is a noun derived from creation, just as 'the eater' is a noun derived from eating, and 'the striker' from striking, and similarly 'the existent' from bringing into existence. Then according to us, the derived noun from a meaning is a description for the one in whom the meaning subsists or for the one to whom the meaning belongs, such that the meaning returns to the essence, like 'the stationary' is a noun for that in which stationariness subsists, and similarly movement and blackness, and 'the existent' is a noun for one whose existence returns to his essence. And agreement was reached on this principle between us and the Ash'ariyya. And we all attributed ignorance to the Mu'tazila where they claimed that 'the speaker' is a noun for the one who brings about speech, not for the locus in which speech subsists, and 'the disbeliever' is a noun for the doer of disbelief, not for the one in whom disbelief subsists. And we claimed contradiction and departure from reason where they agreed with us that 'the moving' is that in which movement subsists, not the one who brings it about, and similarly 'the stationary', 'the black', 'the white', 'the living', 'the dead', 'the healthy', 'the corrupt', and 'the sick'. Then these Ash'ariyya abandoned this principle and claimed that 'the Creator' is other than the one in whom creation subsists, and 'the bringer into existence' is other than the one in whom bringing into existence subsists, and this is a clear contradiction and abandonment of the principles of the people of truth, rather a departure from the consensus of rational people. And the Mu'tazila in this matter are in a better state than them, for they fell into what they fell into due to the constraint of their corrupt principle of the impossibility of a meaning subsisting in the essence of Allah Almighty, but this constraint does not apply to the Ash'ariyya, for they agreed with us on the existence of the statement of the subsistence of attributes in the essence of Allah, Exalted and Majestic. And the second: that the Mu'tazila followed this principle in some places, namely the issue of speech, where they made 'the speaker' the one who brings about speech, not the one in whom speech subsists, and similarly they made 'the disbeliever' ...
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage provides a verification (tahqiq) of the principle of derived names and then uses it to criticize both the Ash'ariyya and the Mu'tazila for inconsistency. The author begins by stating that names like 'Creator', 'existent', etc., are derived from a meaning (ma'na) that must subsist in the subject. They illustrate with examples: 'stationary' applies to that in which stationariness resides, not to one who merely causes stationariness. The author notes that the Ash'ariyya agree with this principle in general, and they all accuse the Mu'tazila of ignorance for reversing it in cases like 'speaker' (they say speaker is one who creates speech, not the locus). But then the author points out a contradiction: the Ash'ariyya themselves abandon this principle when it comes to 'Creator', claiming that the Creator is not the one in whom creation subsists. This is a clear contradiction and a departure from the consensus of rational people. The Ash'ariyya have no excuse, since they already accept that attributes subsist in Allah's essence. The author then begins a second point criticizing the Mu'tazila for applying this principle inconsistently (e.g., in the case of speech they follow it, but they deny it for creation). The passage cuts off mid-sentence, but the argument is that the Mu'tazila also contradict themselves.

Key Terms

اسم
خالق
إيجاد
متكلم
كافر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that only the Mu'tazila are inconsistent in their use of derived names, while the Ash'aris are consistent.
Correction: The author shows that both groups are inconsistent: the Mu'tazila violate the principle for speech and disbelief, and the Ash'aris violate it for creation and existence. In fact, the Ash'aris are worse because they have no doctrinal excuse.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the Mu'tazila are in a 'better state' than the Ash'aris?
A) The Mu'tazila never accepted the principle of derived names.
B) The Mu'tazila have an excuse for their inconsistency (their corrupt principle), but the Ash'aris have no excuse.
C) The Ash'aris are more ignorant than the Mu'tazila.
D) The Mu'tazila followed the principle consistently.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ariyya are more inconsistent than the Mu'tazila because they accepted the principle and the subsistence of attributes, yet they denied it for 'Creator' and 'Existent'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own beliefs about Allah's names and attributes, do you find any area where you apply a different standard than you do for other aspects of your faith? What would it take for you to bring full consistency, even if it means abandoning a comfortable position?
?
The Ash'ariyya had no excuse for their inconsistency because they already accepted the principle and the subsistence of attributes. Is there a truth you already accept in principle but fail to apply in a specific area of your life? Will you commit today to closing that gap?
?
The Mu'tazila were forced into contradiction by a flawed foundation. What foundational belief in your own life might be quietly leading you into inconsistencies? Are you willing to let it go, no matter how long you've held it?

The Absurd Consequences of Identifying Creation with the Created
Nasafi uses the example of blackness to show the Ash'ari view leads to impossible descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari view that creation is identical to the created leads to impossible descriptions of God and why it constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
If creation is the same as the created, either the locus becomes a creator or God becomes a creation.

Imam Nasafi presents a powerful logical refutation of the Ash'ari position on divine attributes. Using the simple example of blackness, he shows that identifying creation with the created forces us into an impossible choice: either we attribute creation to the accident's locus, making it a creator, or we attribute the accident's qualities to God, which is clearly blasphemous. The argument then extends to all accidents, demonstrating the far-reaching absurdity of the view.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the premises
The author assumes for argument that creation is identical to the created, and that a blackness exists in a locus. Note the two descriptions: blackness and creation.
This is a hypothetical to show the internal contradiction.
2
Trace the first contradiction
If blackness subsists in the locus, and creation also subsists in it, then the locus would be the creator. That is absurd because only Allah creates.
3
Trace the second contradiction
If we avoid that by saying Allah creates directly without any attribute subsisting in Him, then Allah would be the one who is black, sweet, bitter, etc. That is worse.
The author calls this an egregious contradiction built on whim.
4
Extend to all accidents
The example is not isolated. Every death, motion, color, taste, smell, etc. would force the same absurdity. Either their loci are creators, or Allah has those qualities.
This shows the view is universally incoherent.
5
Understand the final verdict
Both options are impossible and constitute kufr (disbelief). Thus the Ash'ari view is rejected.
The Maturidi view, which distinguishes creation from the created, avoids this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يحقق ما ذهبنا إليه أن لو وجد في محل وهو سواد بنفسه وهو خلق بنفسه فكان من قام به ما هو السواد قام به ما هو الخلق، ولو كان المحل هو الأسود لقيام ما هو السواد لكان ينبغي أن يكون هو الخالق لقيام ما هو الخلق به، ولو كان الباري هو الخالق لا من قام به لكان هو الأسود به لا من قام به فكان القول برجوع أحد الوصفين إلى الصانع والآخر إلى المحل تناقضا فاحشا وبناء للأمر على التشهي، لا على ما يوجبه الدليل. وكذا كل موت يوجد في الدنيا فهو خلق عندهم، وكذا كل حركة وسكون ولون من سواد وبياض وغيرهما وطعم من حلاوة ومرارة وغيرهما ورائحة واجتماع وافتراق وشر وفساد وزمانه ومرض ونجاسة، فينبغي أن توصف محالها بكونها خالقة لها كما وصفت بكونها متحركة ساكنة متلونة سوادا وبياضا وحلوة ومرة وشريرة ومفسدة وغير ذلك أو يكون الباري جل وعلا هو الساكن المتحرك الميت الأسود الأبيض الحلو المر المنتن المجتمع المفترق الشرير الفاسد أو المفسد النجس قبيح الفعل سيئ العمل، وكلا الأمرين كفر.
What verifies what we have gone to is that if there existed in a locus a blackness in itself and it is creation in itself, then the one in which blackness subsists would have creation subsisting in it. And if the locus were the black due to the subsistence of blackness, then it should be the creator due to the subsistence of creation in it. And if the Creator is the Creator not from what subsists in Him, then He would be the black by it not from what subsists in Him. So the statement of assigning one of the two descriptions to the Maker and the other to the locus would be an egregious contradiction and building the matter on whim, not on what the evidence requires. And similarly, every death that occurs in the world is creation according to them, and every motion, rest, color of blackness and whiteness and others, taste of sweetness and bitterness and others, smell, union, separation, evil, corruption, and its time, sickness, impurity—so their loci should be described as being creators of them just as they are described as being moving, resting, colored black and white, sweet, bitter, evil, corrupt, and so on, or else the Exalted and Majestic Creator would be the moving, resting, dead, black, white, sweet, bitter, stinking, societal, separate, evil, corrupt or corrupting, impure, ugly in deed, bad in action—and both matters are disbelief.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed refutation of the Ash'ari view through an example. The author imagines a blackness (sawad) that exists in a locus (mahall) and is both blackness in itself and creation in itself. If creation subsists in the locus, then the locus would be the creator. Alternatively, if the Creator is the creator without anything subsisting in Him, then He would be directly the blackness. This leads to a contradiction: either the locus is creator or God has the attributes of the accident. The author extends this to all accidents: death, motion, rest, colors, tastes, smells, etc. In each case, either the locus is described as the creator of those accidents, or God is described as having those characteristics. Both options are impossible and constitute disbelief (kufr).

Key Terms
سواد
محل
خلق
مخلوق
صفات الباري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari view only concerns actions, not all accidents.
Correction: The author shows it applies to death, motion, colors, tastes, smells, etc., leading to absurd descriptions of God.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what are the two impossible consequences of the Ash'ari view that creation is identical to the created?
A) Either the locus is the creator or God has the accident's attributes.
B) Either God creates everything or nothing.
C) Either the accident is eternal or it is created.
D) Either the locus is eternal or it is temporal.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari view leads to either attributing creation to created things or attributing imperfect qualities to Allah, both of which are kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you catch yourself attributing to Allah qualities that are suitable only for created beings? What specific thoughts or images about God do you need to repent of after reading this passage?
?
The author says building religion on whim leads to kufr. Where in your own understanding of Islam have you followed your own desire or cultural habit rather than what the evidence from revelation and reason dictates? Will you commit to seeking the truth even when it contradicts your comfort?
?
Both outcomes in this argument are described as kufr. Do you take the boundaries of kufr and iman seriously? Is there any belief or practice you have been casual about that, upon reflection, might lead to such consequences? What will you do about it starting today?

The Blasphemous Consequence: Evil Things as Divine Attributes
The author argues that if creation is an attribute, then evil and impure things become divine attributes, which is absurd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari view that creation is an attribute of God leads to the blasphemous conclusion that evil and impure things are divine attributes.

Core Idea
If creation is an attribute, then Iblis and filth become attributes of God.

The author presents a devastating logical consequence of the Ash'ari/Najjari claim that creation is an attribute of God. If creation and the created are identical, then every created thing—including the most vile—would be a divine attribute. This passage forces us to consider the theological absurdity of such a position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author builds a conditional argument: 'if creation is an attribute, then...'.
The author uses strong language: 'extremely corrupt'.
2
Identify the main claim being refuted
The claim is that creation (al-khalq) is an attribute of God, like knowledge and power. Find the statement that spells this out.
3
List the examples provided
The author lists Iblis, his helpers, filth, stench, dogs, monkeys, pigs, dead bodies, blood, and also disbelief and sins. Why are these shocking?
These are all created things according to the opponents.
4
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that if creation = the created, then all these become attributes of God. Grasp why this is considered extremely corrupt.
The author praises God for protection from such a view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يوجب بطلان قولهم: إن الخالق وصف الله تعالى فيكون الخلق صفة له، كالعالم والعلم والقادر والقدرة، فلو كان الخلق هو المخلوق، لكان إبليس وأعوانه والأقذار والأنتان والكلاب والقردة والخنازير والميتات والدماء عندهم جميعا، والكفر والمعاصي على أصول النجارية والأشعرية كلها صفات الله تعالى والقول به في غاية الفساد، والحمد لله على العصمة. ثم الكفر لما كان خلقا وكفرا، فإما أن يكون الكافر به من هو الخالق له، وإما أن يكون الخالق له من هو الكافر به، فإن قالت النجارية والأشعرية بالأول، فقد زعموا أن الله تعالى هو الكافر بخلقه الكفر في الكافر، وكفر من يقول به لا يخفى. وإن قالوا بالثاني فقد جعلوا العبد خالقا لكفره، وهذا منهم ترك لمذهبهم في خلق أفعال العباد.
What necessitates the invalidity of their statement is that the Creator is an attribute of God the Exalted, so creation would be an attribute of Him, like the Knower and knowledge, the Powerful and power. So if creation were the created, then Iblis and his helpers, filth, stench, dogs, monkeys, pigs, dead bodies, and blood would all be, according to them, attributes of God the Exalted, and similarly disbelief and acts of disobedience according to the principles of the Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya would all be attributes of God the Exalted, and saying that is extremely corrupt, and praise be to God for protection. Then disbelief, since it is creation and disbelief, either the one who disbelieves by it is the one who creates it, or the one who creates it is the one who disbelieves by it. If the Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya say the first, then they have claimed that God the Exalted is the disbeliever by creating disbelief in the disbeliever, and the disbelief of one who says this is not hidden. And if they say the second, then they have made the slave the creator of his own disbelief, and this from them is an abandonment of their madhhab on the creation of the actions of servants.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage presents two further arguments against the Ash'ari/Najjari view. First, if creation is an attribute of God (like knowledge and power), then since they say creation is identical to the created, all created things would be attributes of God. This would include evil entities like Iblis, pigs, and dead bodies, as well as disbelief and sins—all would be divine attributes. This is clearly blasphemous. Second, regarding disbelief (kufr) specifically: since disbelief is creation and disbelief, either the one who disbelieves (the kafir) is the creator of it, or the creator of it is the one who disbelieves by it. If the Ash'aris say God is the creator, then God would be the disbeliever, which is clear kufr. If they say the slave creates it, then they abandon their own doctrine that actions are created by God. Thus the Ash'ari view is self-defeating.

Key Terms
صفات الله
إبليس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That saying creation is an attribute of God is harmless and consistent with divine sovereignty.
Correction: The author shows it leads to attributing evil entities like Iblis and filth to God, which is blasphemous.

Checkpoint
What does the author say would be a consequence of saying creation is an attribute of God and identical to the created?
A) Only good things are divine attributes.
B) Evil things like Iblis and pigs become attributes of God.
C) God is beyond all attributes.
D) The slave creates his own attributes.

Key Takeaway
Attributing creation to God in the sense of identity between creation and the created leads to the blasphemous conclusion that evil things are divine attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a theological view without fully considering its consequences, even if it led to attributing evil to God? What does that reveal about your reverence for His perfection?
?
When you hear arguments that try to safeguard God's sovereignty but end up making Him the source of evil, do you pause to examine the logical steps, or do you accept them out of loyalty to a school?
?
If the author's warning applies to those who would unintentionally assign filth and disbelief to God, what safeguards have you put in place to ensure your own beliefs about Allah's attributes remain pure and free from such corruption?

The Dilemma of Disbelief: Who is the Creator of Kufr?
The author presents a dilemma for the Ash'ari/Najjari view on kufr: either God is the disbeliever or the slave creates disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dilemma the Ash'ari/Najjari view faces regarding disbelief: either God becomes the disbeliever or the slave creates his own disbelief, both of which are problematic.

Core Idea
If God creates disbelief, He is the disbeliever; if the slave creates it, Ash'ari doctrine collapses.

The author now focuses on the specific case of disbelief (kufr). Since disbelief is both a creation and an act of disbelief, a dilemma arises: either the creator of disbelief is also the one who disbelieves by it, or the creator is distinct from the disbeliever. The author shows that both options lead to unacceptable conclusions for the Ash'ari and Najjari positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the dilemma
The passage presents a dilemma: 'either the one who disbelieves is the creator, or the creator is the one who disbelieves.' Find these two options.
The author uses 'إما أن يكون... وإما أن يكون'.
2
Analyze the first horn
If the Ash'aris say the disbeliever is the creator (i.e., God creates disbelief but the slave disbelieves?), wait: The text says 'either the one who disbelieves by it is the one who creates it' or vice versa. Actually, the first option: the kāfir (disbeliever) is the creator of his own disbelief. That would mean the slave creates, which contradicts their doctrine.
The author says if they take the first, they abandon their madhhab.
3
Analyze the second horn
If they say God is the creator of disbelief, then God becomes the one who disbelieves by it (since creator and disbeliever are the same). This is clear kufr.
The author says 'كفر من يقول به لا يخفى'.
4
Understand the overall refutation
The dilemma shows that the Ash'ari/Najjari position is self-defeating: it either leads to attributing disbelief to God or to denying God's creation of actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يوجب بطلان قولهم: إن الخالق وصف الله تعالى فيكون الخلق صفة له، كالعالم والعلم والقادر والقدرة، فلو كان الخلق هو المخلوق، لكان إبليس وأعوانه والأقذار والأنتان والكلاب والقردة والخنازير والميتات والدماء عندهم جميعا، والكفر والمعاصي على أصول النجارية والأشعرية كلها صفات الله تعالى والقول به في غاية الفساد، والحمد لله على العصمة. ثم الكفر لما كان خلقا وكفرا، فإما أن يكون الكافر به من هو الخالق له، وإما أن يكون الخالق له من هو الكافر به، فإن قالت النجارية والأشعرية بالأول، فقد زعموا أن الله تعالى هو الكافر بخلقه الكفر في الكافر، وكفر من يقول به لا يخفى. وإن قالوا بالثاني فقد جعلوا العبد خالقا لكفره، وهذا منهم ترك لمذهبهم في خلق أفعال العباد.
What necessitates the invalidity of their statement is that the Creator is an attribute of God the Exalted, so creation would be an attribute of Him, like the Knower and knowledge, the Powerful and power. So if creation were the created, then Iblis and his helpers, filth, stench, dogs, monkeys, pigs, dead bodies, and blood would all be, according to them, attributes of God the Exalted, and similarly disbelief and acts of disobedience according to the principles of the Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya would all be attributes of God the Exalted, and saying that is extremely corrupt, and praise be to God for protection. Then disbelief, since it is creation and disbelief, either the one who disbelieves by it is the one who creates it, or the one who creates it is the one who disbelieves by it. If the Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya say the first, then they have claimed that God the Exalted is the disbeliever by creating disbelief in the disbeliever, and the disbelief of one who says this is not hidden. And if they say the second, then they have made the slave the creator of his own disbelief, and this from them is an abandonment of their madhhab on the creation of the actions of servants.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage presents two further arguments against the Ash'ari/Najjari view. First, if creation is an attribute of God (like knowledge and power), then since they say creation is identical to the created, all created things would be attributes of God. This would include evil entities like Iblis, pigs, and dead bodies, as well as disbelief and sins—all would be divine attributes. This is clearly blasphemous. Second, regarding disbelief (kufr) specifically: since disbelief is creation and disbelief, either the one who disbelieves (the kafir) is the creator of it, or the creator of it is the one who disbelieves by it. If the Ash'aris say God is the creator, then God would be the disbeliever, which is clear kufr. If they say the slave creates it, then they abandon their own doctrine that actions are created by God. Thus the Ash'ari view is self-defeating.

Key Terms
كفر
أفعال العباد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God creating disbelief does not imply He is a disbeliever.
Correction: If creation and the created are identical, and disbelief is created by God, then God would be the one who disbelieves by it, which is absurd.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what dilemma does the Ash'ari view on kufr lead to?
A) Either God creates disbelief or the slave does.
B) Either God is the disbeliever or the slave creates disbelief.
C) Either kufr is not created or God is unjust.
D) Either the slave is free or God is not all-powerful.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari/Najjari view on disbelief leads to a self-defeating dilemma: either God becomes a disbeliever or the slave creates his own disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself indirectly blaming God for your own disbelief or shortcomings, as if He created your failure? How does this dilemma force you to take full ownership of your faith and actions without shifting responsibility to your Creator?
?
This lesson shows that claiming God creates disbelief leads to the absurdity of calling God a disbeliever. In your heart, do you truly believe that your sins are entirely your own doing, or do you still harbor the thought that God willed them for you? What would change if you accepted full accountability without reservation?
?
If you honestly examine your life, are there areas where you have used divine predestination as an excuse to avoid repentance or change? How can you reconcile God's absolute sovereignty with your personal responsibility for disbelief and disobedience, starting today?

The Absurdity of Creation as an Attribute
Sanusi presents a reductio ad absurdum against the view that creation is an attribute of Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why identifying creation (khalq) as an attribute of Allah leads to the absurd conclusion that all created things, including evil and filth, are divine attributes.

Core Idea
If creation is an attribute, then everything created becomes an attribute of Allah.

Sanusi argues against the Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya who consider 'creation' (khalq) to be an attribute of Allah, analogous to knowledge or power. He shows that if khalq is an attribute and is identical with the created thing (makhluq), then every created object—even the most repulsive—would be a divine attribute, which is manifestly absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source once, then the literal translation. Note the logical structure: if...then.
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on 'khalq' (creation) and 'makhluq' (created thing). The argument hinges on equating them.
Also note 'sifa' (attribute) and 'wasf' (description).
3
Understand the reductio
Sanusi lists offensive created things (Iblis, filth, dogs, etc.) to show that if creation is an attribute, these would be attributes of Allah.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that such a view is extremely corrupt. Why is this a strong theological objection?
It violates divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يوجب بطلان قولهم: إن الخالق وصف الله تعالى فيكون الخلق صفة له، كالعالم والعلم والقادر والقدرة، فلو كان الخلق هو المخلوق، لكان إبليس وأعوانه والأقذار والأنتان والكلاب والقردة والخنازير والميتات والدماء عندهم جميعا، والكفر والمعاصي على أصول النجارية والأشعرية كلها صفات الله تعالى والقول به في غاية الفساد، والحمد لله على العصمة. ثم الكفر لما كان خلقا وكفرا ، فإما أن يكون الكافر به من هو الخالق له، وإما أن يكون الخالق له من هو الكافر به، فإن قالت النجارية والأشعرية بالأول، فقد زعموا أن الله تعالى هو الكافر بخلقه الكفر في الكافر، وكفر من يقول به لا يخفى. وإن قالوا بالثاني فقد جعلوا العبد خالقا لكفره، وهذا منهم ترك لمذهبهم في خلق أفعال العباد.
And that which necessitates the invalidity of their statement: that the Creator is an attribute of Allah, so creation (khalq) would be an attribute of Him, like the Knower and knowledge, the Powerful and power. So if creation (khalq) were the created thing (makhluq), then Iblis and his helpers, filth, stench, dogs, monkeys, pigs, dead things, and blood would all, according to them, and kufr and sins, upon the principles of the Najjariyya and the Ash'ariyya, be attributes of Allah Almighty. To say this is extremely corrupt, and praise be to Allah for protection. Then, since kufr is creation (khalq) and disbelief (kufr), either the one who disbelieves is the one who creates it, or the one who creates it is the one who disbelieves by it. If the Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya say the first, they claim that Allah is the disbeliever by His creation of kufr in the disbeliever, and the disbelief of the one who says this is not hidden. If they say the second, they have made the slave a creator of his own kufr, and this is a departure from their doctrine of the creation of acts of servants.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage contains two arguments. First, the author argues that if khalq is an attribute of Allah (like knowledge and power are attributes), and if khalq is identical to makhluq, then everything created would be an attribute of Allah, including filthy and evil things, which is absurd. Second, he presents a dilemma regarding kufr (disbelief). Kufr is both a creation (khalq) and an act of disbelief (kufr). If the one who creates kufr is the one who disbelieves, then Allah would be the disbeliever, which is blasphemy. If the one who disbelieves is the creator of his own kufr, then the slave is a creator, which contradicts the Ash'ari doctrine that all acts are created by Allah. Thus, the Ash'ari position is internally inconsistent.

Key Terms
الخلق (al-khalq)
المخلوق (al-makhluq)
صفة (sifa)
وصف (wasf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that calling 'creation' an attribute of Allah is harmless because it only refers to His act of creating.
Correction: Sanusi shows that if 'creation' (khalq) is an attribute, it must be identical to the created thing (makhluq), making every created object a divine attribute, which is clearly false.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi list as examples to show the absurdity of equating creation with created things?
A) Angels, prophets, and paradise
B) Iblis, filth, dogs, monkeys, pigs, dead things, blood, kufr, and sins
C) Knowledge, power, and will
D) The heavens and the earth

Key Takeaway
If creation (khalq) is an attribute of Allah, then every created thing, including evil and filth, becomes a divine attribute—a manifest absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi lists repulsive things like filth, dogs, and pigs as potential 'attributes' of Allah if the opponents' view were true. When you reflect on your own understanding of Allah's attributes, do you ever unconsciously ascribe to Allah qualities that are unworthy of Him? What would it mean for your relationship with Allah if you held such a view? Commit to checking your own beliefs against the Quran and Sunna today.
?
The argument here protects tawhid by preventing any confusion between Creator and creation. In your daily life, do you ever blur the line between what belongs to Allah and what belongs to His creation—for example, by fearing people's opinions more than Allah's judgment, or by attributing ultimate control to yourself or others? Write down one area where you need to realign your heart's attribution of power and control, and ask Allah to purify it.
?
Sanusi thanks Allah for 'protection' (العصمة) from such corrupt beliefs. When you learn correct aqeedah, do you feel genuine gratitude for being guided away from falsehood, or do you take it for granted? Take a moment to thank Allah specifically for protecting you from the beliefs that the Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya fell into, and ask Him to keep you firm on the truth.

The Dilemma of Kufr as Creation and Disbelief
Sanusi presents a dilemma against the Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya regarding the nature of disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma facing those who hold that disbelief (kufr) is both a creation of Allah and an act of the disbeliever.

Core Idea
If kufr is created by Allah, either Allah disbelieves or the servant creates—both are untenable.

Sanusi continues his refutation by focusing on a specific problem: disbelief (kufr) is both a creation (khalq) and an act of disbelief (kufr). He presents a dilemma: either the one who creates kufr is the one who disbelieves, or the one who disbelieves creates his own kufr. Either option contradicts the opponent's own principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Start from 'ثم الكفر...' Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: 'either...or'.
2
Understand the dilemma
Kufr is both a creation (khalq) and an act of disbelief (kufr). The dilemma asks: who creates and who disbelieves?
3
Explore the first horn
If the creator of kufr is the disbeliever, then Allah creates kufr and disbelieves—blasphemy.
Sanusi says the disbelief of one who says this is obvious.
4
Explore the second horn
If the disbeliever creates his own kufr, then the servant is a creator, contradicting the Ash'ari doctrine that Allah creates all acts.
5
Reflect on the inconsistency
The Najjariyya and Ash'ariyya cannot consistently hold their position without falling into one of these absurdities.

Source Text

The Distinction Between Creation and the Created
Imam al-Nasafi argues against identifying creation with the created, using analogy and direct proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of creation (khalq) is distinct from the created thing (makhluq), and why it is impossible for Allah to re-create what already exists.

Core Idea
Creation is an act, not a substance; the created is its product.

Imam al-Nasafi presents two arguments to demonstrate that creation (khalq) is not identical to the created (makhluq). He first draws an analogy from speech and truth, then provides a direct proof based on the impossibility of bringing into existence what already exists. This distinction is crucial for understanding Allah’s attributes and the nature of causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the two-part structure: an analogy followed by a direct proof.
The text cuts off at the end, but the main argument is complete up to the discussion of will.
2
Understand the analogy
Reflect on the analogy: just as the one who speaks is the same as the one who is truthful, the concept of creation and the created are two aspects of the same relationship, not identical.
This analogy shows that if two attributes are necessarily connected, the subject is the same, but here the author uses it to argue that khalq and makhluq are different.
3
Examine the direct proof
If creation were identical to the created, then creating heaven would mean heaven itself, which is absurd. Also, creation only occurs at the first moment of existence; after that, re-creation is impossible.
The author rejects the view of al-Nazzam that Allah continuously creates.
4
Apply to attributes like power and will
The same logic applies to other attributes: power (qudra) attaches only at the moment of coming into existence, and will (irada) likewise. This refutes the claim that Allah continually creates the same thing.
The text cuts off illustrating will, but the argument is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يحقق هذا: أن من كان موصوفا بأحد معنى صفة، كان هو الموصوف بالمعنى الآخر. فإن الكلام لما كان كلاما وصدقا كان الموصوف بكونه متكلما هو الموصوف بكونه صادقا، ولو ادعى إنسان أن المتكلم به غير من هو صادق به نسب إلي الجهل، فكذا ها هنا والذي يدل على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه أن الخلق لو كان هو المخلوق، لكان خلق السماء هو السماء، وخلق الأرض هو الأرض وكذا هذا في جميع أجسام العالم. ثم الله تعالى إنما كان خالقا لها في ابتداء أحوال وجوها لوجود هذا الذات الذي هو خلقه، وهذا الذات بعينه في الزمان الثاني والثالث فصاعدا موجودا فيكون خلقا فيكون الله تعالى خالقا لها في كل حال، فيوصف بأنه يخلق السماوات والأرضين والجبال للحال، ويوجدها كما هو مذهب النظام، والقول بإيجاد الموجود وخلق المخلوق محال، إذ ليس يشك أن ما صار مثبت الكينونة حاصلا في الوجود والآنية، فهو ما دام في تلك الحال فمن المحال أن يوجد ثانيا ولا يلزمنا هذا، وإن كان الإيجاد الذي هو صفة الله تعالى موجودا للحال لأن المخلوق كان مخلوقا لتعلق تلك الصفة به، وهي تعلقت به عند خروجه من العدم إلى الوجود، فأما بعد ذلك فلا تعلق به لاستحالة إيجاد الموجود ، هذا كما قلنا جميعا إن الموجود في أول أحوال وجوده مقدور الوجود لتعلق القدرة به في تلك الحال، وفي حالة البقاء لم يبق مقدورا لوجود لأنه لا تعلق له بعد ذلك بها لاستحالة تعلق الوجود بالموجد، وكذا الإرادة مع المراد على هذا خلاف ما ذهبوا إليه، فإن ما هو خلق هذا الجسم
And that which verifies this is that whoever is described by one of two meanings of an attribute, he is described by the other meaning. For when speech is speech and truth, the one described as speaking is the one described as truthful. If someone claims that the speaker is other than the one who is truthful, he would be attributed to ignorance. So here as well. And that which indicates the soundness of what we have gone to is that if creation (khalq) were the created (makhluq), then the creation of heaven would be heaven itself, and the creation of the earth would be earth itself, and likewise with all bodies of the world. Then Allah is only Creator of them at the beginning of states, for the existence of this essence which is His creation, and this same essence in the second and third time onward exists, so it would be creation, so Allah would be Creator of them in every state, and thus He would be described as creating the heavens, earths, and mountains at the present moment, and bringing them into existence, as is the doctrine of al-Nazzam. But the statement of bringing into existence what exists and creating what is created is impossible, since there is no doubt that what has become established in being, present in existence and present time, for as long as it is in that state, it is impossible to bring it into existence a second time. And this does not necessitate us, even if the bringing into existence (ijad) which is an attribute of Allah exists for the present moment, because the created thing was created due to the attachment of that attribute to it, and it was attached to it when it came from non-existence into existence. As for after that, there is no attachment to it due to the impossibility of bringing into existence what exists. This is as we all said: that the existent in the first of its states of existence is potential of existence due to the attachment of power to it in that state, and in the state of remaining it does not remain potential for existence because there is no attachment for it after that to it, due to the impossibility of attachment of existence to that which exists. And likewise the will with the object of will, contrary to what they have gone to. For that which is the creation of this body...
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage contains two main arguments. First, an analogy: if speech is speech and truth, the one described as speaking is the same as the one described as truthful. Similarly, if creation and created are two aspects, the one who creates must be the one who is created? Actually, the analogy is meant to show that if two attributes are necessarily connected, the subject must be the same. But the author's point is that if khalq and makhluq were identical, then the subject would be the same. Second, a direct proof: if khalq were identical to makhluq, then the creation of heaven would be heaven itself, which is absurd because the creation is an act, not a substance. Then the author addresses the issue of temporality: Allah creates things only at the moment they come into existence. After that, they are not re-created because that would be creating what already exists, which is impossible. The attribute of creation (ijad) is only attached at the initial moment. The same applies to power (qudra) and will (irada). This refutes the position of al-Nazzam who claimed that Allah continuously creates. The text cuts off during a discussion about the will.

Key Terms
خلق (khalq)
مخلوق (makhluq)
إيجاد (ijad)
موجود (mawjud)
قدرة (qudra)
إرادة (irada)
مراد (murad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that creation (khalq) and the created (makhluq) are the same thing, and that Allah continuously creates everything at every moment.
Correction: Creation is an act distinct from the created thing. It occurs only at the initial moment of existence; after that, the thing exists and cannot be re-created. This is based on the impossibility of bringing into existence what already exists.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can't Allah create something that already exists?
A) Because Allah is not powerful enough
B) Because creation only occurs at the first moment of existence
C) Because the created thing is eternal
D) Because the argument is only an analogy

Key Takeaway
Creation (khalq) is an act distinct from the created (makhluq), and it occurs only at the initial moment of existence; bringing into existence what already exists is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own existence, do you see yourself as a product of a single creative act or as being continuously sustained? How does the distinction between creation and continuous existence change how you recognize God's role in your life right now?
?
Are there areas in your life where you behave as if God is creating something that already exists? For example, do you ask God to 'give you faith' when He has already granted it? How can you align your supplications with the reality that God creates at the initial moment?
?
The passage emphasizes that bringing into existence what already exists is impossible. How does this affect your confidence in God's promises regarding resurrection? Do you truly believe God can create a new creation from nothing again, or do doubts linger?

Refutation of the Identity of Act and Object
Refutes identity of act and object with linguistic and analogical proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi theologians argue that the act (fi’l) and its object (maf’ul) cannot be identical, using linguistic proof and distinguishing act from knowledge based on effect.

Core Idea
Act affects its object; knowledge does not — that's why identity is possible for knowledge but not for act.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla tackles a controversial claim attributed to an-Naẓẓām that the divine act and its object are one and the same. Al-Nasafi refutes this by appealing to linguistic intuition and the fundamental distinction between power and knowledge. Let's follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim being refuted
The passage opens by stating the view that act and object are identical and shows its absurd consequence: 'bringing into existence the existent.' This sets the stage for the refutation.
Notice that the author quickly exposes the logical problem before presenting his own proof.
2
Examine the linguistic proof from the ‘alāqa (relation)
The author quotes the people of language: the act is a relation between agent and object. The agent is agent only by the act subsisting in him; the object is object only by the act occurring upon it. This is intuitively known in the witnessed world.
This linguistic argument is foundational for the analogy to the unseen.
3
Consider the objection from the identity of knowledge and the known
An opponent argues: if knowledge can be identical to its object (as when God knows His knowledge), why can't act be identical to its object? This is a serious challenge that must be answered.
The objection is based on a different attribute — knowledge — which seems to allow identity.
4
Grasp the key distinction: act has an effect, knowledge does not
The author responds by distinguishing power/act from knowledge. In the witnessed, a person knows his own knowledge by that same knowledge, but power is never empowered for its possessor. The act affects its object (mu'aththir), while knowledge does not change the known. Hence identity is impossible for act and object but possible for knowledge and the known.
The decisive factor is that the act has an effect (athar) on its object, requiring distinctness between effector and affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي كان الله تعالى لأجله خالقا له موجودا إذ هو كان خالقا له لهذا لا لتعلق الخلق به ترفع ذلك بعد ذلك بل لعين هذا الخلق وهو قائم فإن ساعدوا النظام تركوا مذهبهم ووقعوا فيما هو محال وهو القول بإيجاد الموجود، وإن خالفوه ناقضوا، وبالله العصمة عن كل ضلال والذي يدل على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه أن القول باتحاد الفعل والمفعول قول باتحاد الضرب والمضروب والأكل والمأكول والقتل والمقتول، وجميع الأفعال مع مفعولاتها، والقول بذلك مما يعرف فساده بالبديهة، وهذا لأن أهل اللغة قالوا: إن الفعل علاقة بين الفاعل والمفعول لا يكون الفاعل فاعلا إلا باعتبار قيامه به، كما لا يكون المفعول مفعولا إلا بوقوعه عليه كما في الضرب والمضروب، وغير ذلك من النظائر . وإذا ثبت هذا في الشاهد، ثبت في الغائب، لاستوائهما في المعنى لما مر من اقتضاء الفعل فاعلا يقوم به، ومفعولا يتعلق به، فيقع عليه، فيكون الفاعل فاعلا لقيام الفعل به والمفعول مفعولا لوقوع الفعل عليه، كما في القادر والمقدور فإن القادر في الشاهد لما كان قادرا باعتبار قيام القدرة به والمقدور كان مقدورا لتعلق القدرة به لم يجز قادر لم تقم القدرة به ولا مقدور لا تتعلق به القدرة بل هو غير المقدور فكذا هذا.
فإن قالوا: أليس أن اتحاد العلم والمعلوم جائز فإن الله تعالى يعلم علمه بعلمه، فكان العلم علما معلوما، فكذا الفعل يجوز أن يكون فعلا ومفعولا، وإن كان لا يجوز ذلك في القدرة والمقدور، فلم كان اعتبار الفعل بالقدرة أولى من اعتباره بالعلم.
قلنا: نحن نعتبر الغائب بالشاهد، وفي الشاهد جاز أن يكون العلم معلوما لمن هو عالم به فإن الإنسان يعلم علمه بنفس ذلك العلم ، لا بعلم آخر سواه خلافا لما يقوله أبو العباس القلانسي، إذ لو كان يعلمه بعلم هو غيره لجاز انعدام ذلك العلم الثاني مع وجود هذا العلم لأجل المغايرة، فيصير الإنسان عالما بشيء ولا يعلم أنه يعلمه وهذا محال، ولما جاز هذا في الشاهد في العلم جوزنا ذلك في الغائب بالإجماع، ولما لم يجز في القدرة في الشاهد، فإن القدرة قط لا تكون مقدورة للقادر بها في الشاهد، وإن كانت مقدورة لغيره وهو الله تعالى لم نجوز في الغائب أن تكون القدرة والمقدور واحدا، والذيل[؟] في الشاهد نظير القدرة، فإن في الشاهد لم يكن الفاعل فاعلا إلا بفعل قام به، فلم يكن المفعول مفعولا إلا لوقوع فعله عليه، ولم يكن فعله قط مفعولا له وإن كان مفعولا لغيره، فلم نجوز القول باتحاد الفعل والمفعول في الغائب استدلالا بالشاهد على الغائب. وحقيقة هذا: أن القدرة لها أثر في المقدور والشيء يؤثر في غيره، إذ المؤثر غير المتأثر ، فلم تكن القدرة مقدورة لمن هي قدرة له، وكذلك الفعل يؤثر في المفعول فلم يكن بد من القول بتغايرهما، وكان القول باتحادهما محالا كما في القدرة والمقدور، فأما في العلم فلا تأثير له في المعلوم لأنه لا يغير المعلوم عما هو عليه، فلم يكن اتحادهما محالا، وبالله التوفيق.
That for which God Almighty was creating is existent, since He was creating it for this, not because of the attachment of creation to it, that being removed after that, but for the very act of creation which is subsisting. So if they agree with an-Naẓẓām, they abandon their doctrine and fall into what is impossible, which is the statement of bringing into existence the existent; and if they oppose him, they contradict themselves. And with God is protection from all misguidance. And what indicates the correctness of what we hold is that the statement that the act and the object are identical is a statement that the hitting and the hit, the eating and the eaten, the killing and the killed, and all acts with their objects are identical, and the statement of that is known to be false by intuition. This is because the people of language said: the act is a relation between the agent and the object; the agent is not an agent except by virtue of its subsistence in him, just as the object is not an object except by its occurring upon it, as in hitting and the hit, and other similar cases. And if this is established in the witnessed, it is established in the unseen, because they are equal in meaning due to what has passed of the act requiring an agent in whom it subsists, and an object to which it is attached, upon which it occurs. So the agent is an agent because of the subsistence of the act in him, and the object is an object because of the occurrence of the act upon it, as in the case of the powerful and the empowered: for the powerful in the witnessed, since he is powerful by virtue of the subsistence of power in him, and the empowered is empowered by virtue of the attachment of power to him, it is not permissible that there be a powerful without power subsisting in him, nor an empowered without power attaching to him; rather he is other than the empowered. So likewise this. Then they said: Is it not that the identity of knowledge and the known is permissible, for God knows His knowledge by His knowledge, so knowledge is a known knowledge; so likewise the act may be an act and an object, even though that is not permissible in the case of power and the empowered. So why is the consideration of the act by power more appropriate than consideration by knowledge? We replied: We consider the unseen by the witnessed, and in the witnessed it is permissible for knowledge to be known for the one who knows it; for a person knows his knowledge by that very knowledge, not by another knowledge besides it, contrary to what Abu al-'Abbās al-Qalānisī says. For if he knew it by a knowledge other than it, it would be possible for that second knowledge to cease while this knowledge exists due to the difference, and then the person would be knowledgeable of something but not know that he knows it, which is impossible. And since this is permissible in the witnessed regarding knowledge, we permitted it in the unseen by consensus. And since it is not permissible for power in the witnessed — for power is never empowered for the powerful by it in the witnessed, even if it is empowered for another, namely God — we did not permit in the unseen that power and the empowered be one. And the evidence[?] in the witnessed is analogous to power: for in the witnessed, the agent is an agent only by an act subsisting in him, and the object is an object only by the occurrence of his act upon it, and his act is never an object for him, even if it is an object for another. So we did not permit the statement of the identity of act and object in the unseen, drawing an analogy from the witnessed to the unseen. And the reality of this is that power has an effect on the empowered, and a thing affects other than itself; for the effecting is other than the affected. So power is not empowered for the one for whom it is power. Likewise, the act affects the object, so it is necessary to state their distinctness, and the statement of their identity is impossible, as in the case of power and the empowered. As for knowledge, it has no effect on the known because it does not change the known from what it is, so their identity is not impossible. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that the act (fi'l) and its object (maf'ul) are identical, a view attributed to an-Naẓẓām. The author argues that such identity would lead to impossible consequences, like 'bringing into existence the existent' (ījād al-mawjūd). He then provides a linguistic proof: language scholars define the act as a 'relation' ('alāqa) between the agent and the object, such that the agent is an agent only by the act subsisting in him, and the object is an object only by the act occurring upon it. This is intuitively known (badīha) to be false in the witnessed world (shāhid), and by analogy (qiyās) it holds in the unseen (ghā'ib) as well. The author draws a parallel to the distinction between the powerful (qādir) and the empowered (maqdūr): power subsists in the agent and attaches to the object; they cannot be identical. An objection is then raised: if knowledge ('ilm) can be identical to the known (ma'lūm) — as when God knows His knowledge by itself — then why cannot the act be identical to its object? The answer distinguishes between power and knowledge: in the shāhid, a person knows his own knowledge by that same knowledge, without a second knowledge; this is permissible. But power never has the power over itself in the shāhid; it is never empowered for the one who possesses it. The act (fi'l) is like power: it has an effect (athar) on its object, changing it, while knowledge does not change its object. Therefore, identity is impossible for act and object but not impossible for knowledge and the known. The author concludes by emphasizing that power and act are effecting (mu'aththir) while the object is affected (muta'aththir); effecting and affected are necessarily distinct. Hence the identity of act and object is impossible, just as the identity of power and the empowered is impossible.

Key Terms
اتحاد الفعل والمفعول
الشاهد والغائب
علاقة الفعل
القدرة
العلم
المؤثر والمتأثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since knowledge can be identical to its object, act can also be identical.
Correction: Act has an effect on its object, changing it, while knowledge does not change the known. Therefore, identity is possible for knowledge but impossible for act.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that act and object cannot be identical, even though knowledge and the known can be identical?
A) Because act and object are both created, while knowledge is uncreated.
B) Because act has an effect on its object, while knowledge does not change its object.
C) Because act is a relation but knowledge is not.
D) Because the object of an act is always prior to the act.

Key Takeaway
Act and object are distinct because act has an effect on the object, unlike knowledge which does not change the known.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own actions, do you ever find yourself thinking that the action and its outcome are one and the same? How does the lesson’s insistence on the distinction between act and object in the divine realm demand that you re-evaluate your understanding of your deeds as being distinct from their results before Allah?
?
The passage argues that knowledge can be identical to its object because it does not change the known. In your own life, when you 'know' something about God, does that knowledge change you, or is it merely an intellectual assent? If knowledge must be distinct from its object only when it has an effect, then what does your knowledge of God's attributes actually produce in your heart and actions?
?
If act and effect are necessarily distinct, then every action you take has a real impact on something other than yourself. On the Day of Judgment, will your acts stand as separate entities with their own weight? Are you living as though your deeds are not just momentary motions but lasting realities that bear witness to your faith?

Why Act and Object Are One in Knowledge but Not in Power
Nasafi argues that act and object cannot be one in power but can be one in knowledge using the witness analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Nasafi, act and object cannot be identical in the case of divine power (qudra) but can be identical in the case of divine knowledge ('ilm).

Core Idea
Power affects its object; knowledge does not—so identity is impossible for power but possible for knowledge.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses a key distinction in divine attributes: why can knowledge and its object be one, but not power and its object? He uses the kalam method of reasoning from the witnessed world (al-shāhid) to the unseen (al-ghā'ib), and clarifies that the difference lies in causal influence. This lesson walks through his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once to get the overall argument.
Notice the question at the beginning.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on the terms qudra (power), maqdūr (object of power), 'ilm (knowledge), and ma'lūm (known). Understand how they relate.
3
Trace the shahid-gha'ib analogy
Follow how Nasafi uses the witnessed world to argue about the unseen. He gives examples from human knowledge and power.
The example about knowing one's own knowledge is crucial.
4
Understand the difference: effect vs. no effect
The core reason is that power has an effect (ta'thir) on its object, while knowledge does not change the known. This makes identity impossible for power but not for knowledge.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters for understanding divine attributes. It shows that God's power and His acts are distinct, but His knowledge and the objects of His knowledge can be conceptually united.
This lesson prepares you for further discussions on divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجوز ذلك في القدرة والمقدور، فلم كان اعتبار الفعل بالقدرة أولى من اعتباره بالعلم. قلنا: نحن نعتبر الغائب بالشاهد، وفي الشاهد جاز أن يكون العلم معلوما لمن هو عالم به فإن الإنسان يعلم علمه بنفس ذلك العلم، لا بعلم آخر سواه خلافا لما يقوله أبو العباس القلانسي، إذ لو كان يعلمه بعلم هو غيره لجاز انعدام ذلك العلم الثاني مع وجود هذا العلم لأجل المغايرة، فيصير الإنسان عالما بشيء ولا يعلم أنه يعلمه وهذا محال، ولما جاز هذا في الشاهد في العلم جوزنا ذلك في الغائب بالإجماع، ولما لم يجز في القدرة في الشاهد، فإن القدرة قط لا تكون مقدورة للقادر بها في الشاهد، وإن كانت مقدورة لغيره وهو الله تعالى لم نجوز في الغائب أن تكون القدرة والمقدور واحدا، والذيل في الشاهد نظير القدرة، فإن في الشاهد لم يكن الفاعل فاعلا إلا بفعل قام به، فلم يكن المفعول مفعولا إلا لوقوع فعله عليه، ولم يكن فعله قط مفعولا له وإن كان مفعولا لغيره، فلم نجوز القول باتحاد الفعل والمفعول في الغائب استدلالا بالشاهد على الغائب. وحقيقة هذا: أن القدرة لها أثر في المقدور والشيء يؤثر في غيره، إذ المؤثر غير المتأثر، فلم تكن القدرة مقدورة لمن هي قدرة له، وكذلك الفعل يؤثر في المفعول فلم يكن بد من القول بتغايرهما، وكان القول باتحادهما محالا كما في القدرة والمقدور، فأما في العلم فلا تأثير له في المعلوم لأنه لا يغير المعلوم عما هو عليه، فلم يكن اتحادهما محالا، وبالله التوفيق.
That is not permissible in power and the object of power. So why is the consideration of the act by power more appropriate than its consideration by knowledge? We say: We consider the unseen by the witnessed. And in the witnessed, it is possible for knowledge to be known to the one who knows it, for man knows his knowledge by that very knowledge itself, not by another knowledge besides it, contrary to what Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi says. For if he knew it by a knowledge other than it, it would be possible for that second knowledge to cease to exist while this knowledge exists due to the difference, and thus a person would know something without knowing that he knows it, and this is impossible. And since this is possible in the witnessed concerning knowledge, we allowed that in the unseen by consensus. And since it is not possible in power in the witnessed—for power is never an object of power for the one who has the power thereby in the witnessed, even if it is an object of power for another, namely God—we do not allow in the unseen that power and its object are one. And the tail in the witnessed is analogous to power, for in the witnessed the agent is not an agent except by an act subsisting in him, so the act is not an object of action except by the occurrence of his act upon it, and his act is never an object of action for him, even if it is an object of action for another. So we did not allow the claim of the union of act and object in the unseen by inferring the witnessed upon the unseen. The reality of this is that power has an effect on the object of power, and a thing affects other than it, since the effector is other than the affected. So power is not an object of power for the one to whom it belongs as power. Similarly, the act affects the object of action, so one must necessarily say they are distinct, and the claim of their union is impossible, as in the case of power and its object. As for knowledge, it has no effect on the known, because it does not change the known from what it is, so their union is not impossible. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a proof that act and object cannot be identical in the case of power, but can be identical in the case of knowledge. The author begins by stating the initial question: why should the act be considered through power rather than through knowledge? He answers by invoking the method of analogical reasoning from the witnessed to the unseen (shahid to ghā'ib). In the observed world, a person knows his own knowledge by that very knowledge itself, not by a separate second knowledge. This is against al-Qalanisi, who posited a separate knowledge for knowing one's knowledge. If that were the case, the second knowledge could vanish while the first remains, leading to the absurdity of someone knowing something without knowing that he knows it. Since this is possible and not absurd in the witnessed, we extend it to the unseen by consensus. However, for power, even in the witnessed, a power is never an object of power for its possessor (e.g., my power to lift is not itself an object of my power); it can only be an object of power for another, like God. Therefore, we do not allow identity between power and its object in the unseen. Similarly, the 'tail' (dhayl) in the witnessed is analogous to power: an agent acts through an act subsisting in him, so the act and the object acted upon are distinct. Thus, we conclude that power and its object must be distinct, as must act and object. The reason is that power has an effect on its object, and the effector is distinct from the affected. Knowledge, by contrast, has no effect on the known—it does not change it—so identity is not impossible. The passage ends with a prayer for divine assistance.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra)
المقدور (al-maqdūr)
الفعل (al-fi‘l)
المفعول (al-maf‘ūl)
العلم (al-‘ilm)
المعلوم (al-ma‘lūm)
الشاهد (al-shāhid)
الغائب (al-ghā’ib)
التأثير (al-ta’thīr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the union of act and object is impossible in all cases, regardless of the attribute.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that it depends on whether the attribute has causal influence. For power, which affects its object, identity is impossible. For knowledge, which does not affect the known, identity is not impossible.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that knowledge can be identical with its object, while power cannot?
A) Because knowledge is not a created attribute
B) Because power has an effect on its object, but knowledge does not
C) Because knowledge is a necessary attribute of God
D) Because the witnessed and unseen differ in knowledge

Key Takeaway
Power has causal influence on its object, making identity impossible; knowledge has no such influence, so identity is not necessarily impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you realise that your knowledge of God does not change Him, but your acting upon that knowledge does affect your own soul, how will you change the way you prioritise learning over action?
?
If God's power has effect and is always active upon you, are you living in awareness that every moment you are the object of His power? What would change if you truly felt that?
?
The passage shows that knowledge without effect can be identical with its object. Does this free you from the fear that your ignorance or limited understanding diminishes God? Or does it humble you that your knowledge, though real, has no power over Him? What is your heart’s response?
