Refutation of the Shubha About Transitivity of Divine Action
Imam al-Nasafi presents and refutes the doubt about transitivity of divine action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi response refutes the objection that an eternal divine action requires an eternal object.

Core Idea
Eternal action does not necessitate an eternal effect; transitivity implies otherness, not coexistence.

The opponents of the Maturidi position argued that if God's attribute of takwīn (making) is eternal, then its effect—the created world—must also be eternal. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents their doubt and offers a two-part refutation. He first points out that the opponents' own logic proves action and object are distinct, and then illustrates with the example of the divine command.

Guided Path
1
Read the doubt carefully
Read the first part of the Arabic passage where the opponent's argument is presented. Note the logical dilemma they propose: if God's act is eternal, its object must either be eternal or non-existent—both problematic.
The opponent tries to force a contradiction between divine eternity and temporal creation.
2
Analyze the first response
In the author's first response, notice how he turns the opponent's own statement against them. The opponent admits that action is transitive to an object, which implies action and object are different. Therefore, coexistence is not required.
This is a clever refutation by accepting the premise and showing it leads to the opposite conclusion.
3
Understand the second response
Read the analogy of the divine command (amr). Just as God's command 'Be' existed eternally without the world existing eternally, so too takwīn can be eternal without its effect being eternal. This clarifies that transitivity does not require simultaneity in all circumstances.
The analogy shows that the 'condition' of transitivity is not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت بما بينا من الدلائل المغيرة بين التكوين والمكون، فيجب علينا أن نصرف العناية إلى حل ما أوردوا من الشبهات فنقول: قولهم: إن الفعل يتعدى إلى المفعول، وإذا ثبت أنه لا بد أن يتعدى إلى مفعول فلو وجد الفعل في الأزل لكان لا يخلو إما أن كان ما يتعدى إليه موجودا في الأزل أو كان معدما، فإن كان موجودا فهو القول بقدم العالم، وإن كان معدوما ينبغي أن يكون المعدوم مفعولا. الجواب عنه أن نقول: عين هذا الكلام اعتراف منه أن الفعل غير المفعول لأنه زعم أن الفعل يتعدى إلى المفعول، والشيء يتعدى إلى غيره لا نفسه، فإن تعدي الشيء إلى نفسه محال، فإذا هذا الكلام حجة عليه. ثم نقول: الفعل يتعدى إلى المفعول في الجملة، فأما أن يتعدى إليه في الأحوال أجمع فهذا ليس بشرطه، ألا ترى أن الأمر متعد يقال: أمرته فأتمر ثم كان أمر الله تعالى للعالم بالوجود، وهو خطاب كن موجودا في الأزل وكان أمره الذي هو أمر إيجاب موجودا في الأزل ولا مأمور ولا وجوب، فكذا هذا لأنه ما كان أمرا بالوجود ليوجد في القدم بل ليوجد كل موجود في وقت وجوده وما كان أمرا ليجب على المعدوم في القدم بل ليجب على المكلفين وقت وجودهم وبلوغهم مبلغ
And when it is proven by what we have explained of the distinguishing proofs between making (takwīn) and the thing made (mukawwan), it is incumbent upon us to turn our attention to solving the doubts they have raised. So we say: Their statement: 'Action (fiʿl) is transitive to the object of action (mafʿūl). And when it is established that it must be transitive to an object, then if the action existed in eternity, it would be either that what it is transitive to existed in eternity, or it was non-existent. If it existed, that is the statement of the pre-eternity of the world; and if it was non-existent, then the non-existent should be an object of action.' The answer is that we say: This very statement is an admission from him that the action is other than the object of action, because he claims that the action is transitive to the object of action, and a thing is transitive to something other than itself, not to itself; for the transitiveness of a thing to itself is impossible. So this statement is evidence against him. Then we say: Action is transitive to the object of action in general, but that it be transitive to it in all circumstances is not a condition. Do you not see that the command (amr) is transitive: one says 'I commanded him, and he complied.' Then God's command to the world for existence was a speech 'Be, existing in eternity' and His command, which is a command of obligation, existed in eternity, while there was no commanded thing and no obligation. So likewise this, because it was not a command for existence to come into existence in pre-eternity, but rather for every existent to come into existence at the time of its existence, and it was not a command to obligate the non-existent in pre-eternity, but rather to obligate the legally responsible at the time of their existence and their reaching the age of
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage presents a doubt (shubha) from the opponents and the author's answer. The opponents argue: Action (fiʿl) is transitive to its object (mafʿūl). If God's act of making (takwīn) is eternal, then its object must either be eternal (leading to the pre-eternity of the world) or non-existent (which would require the non-existent to be an object of action, which is absurd). The author's answer has two parts. First, the opponent's very statement admits that action is distinct from its object, because one thing cannot be transitive to itself. So the opponent's claim that the object must coexist with the action is false; transitivity implies otherness, not simultaneity. Second, action is transitive in general, but not in every state. The example of divine command (amr) illustrates this: God's command 'Be' existed eternally, yet the command itself is transitive to the commanded thing, but the commanded thing (the world) did not exist in eternity. Similarly, a command of obligation existed eternally without any obligated person. Thus, the transitive nature of divine action does not require the object to be co-eternal. The passage ends abruptly but the core refutation is given.

مفعول
تعدي
تكوين
أمر
أزل

Checkpoint

A) Action is not transitive at all.
B) The opponent's own admission that action is transitive to something other than itself proves that the action and object are distinct, so coexistence is not required.
C) The object can be non-existent because non-existence is a thing.
D) God's action is unlike human action.

Key Takeaway
An eternal divine action does not require an eternal effect; the transitive nature of action only requires that action and object are distinct, not simultaneous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's command 'Be', does your heart tremble at the fact that His word is eternal, yet you—the commanded—are a temporal creature? How does this change the way you approach His commands in the Qur'an?
?
The opponent's doubt stemmed from limiting God's action to human analogies. Where in your own life have you subconsciously imposed human limitations on God's power or attributes, and what will you do today to correct that?
?
If God's action does not require a co-eternal effect, then His will is utterly sovereign over time. Are there areas in your life where you still act as if God is bound by your timeline or expectations? What step can you take today to submit to His timing?

The First Objection to Takwin and Its Refutation
Nasafi refutes the objection that takwin requires a pre-eternal effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the claim that God's eternal act of bringing into existence (takwin) necessarily implies a pre-eternal created world.

Core Idea
God's eternal attributes do not demand eternal effects; they act at the appointed time.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a key objection raised by those who argue that if God's act of bringing into existence (takwin) is eternal, then its effect must also be eternal, leading to the pre-eternity of the world. He refutes this by clarifying the nature of divine acts and drawing analogies with God's command and power.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Identify the claim that an act necessarily extends to its object and that if the act is eternal, the object must be eternal or the non-existent would be an object.
2
Analyze the initial counter-argument
Notice how Nasafi turns the opponent's own words against them: the act is other than the object, so extension does not require identity.
This shows the opponent's presumption is self-defeating.
3
Examine the analogy with God's command
Understand how God's eternal command 'Be' does not require a pre-eternal thing commanded, just as takwin does not require a pre-eternal mukawwan.
4
Understand the argument from divine power
Follow how the same logic applies to God's eternal power, which relates to temporal objects without being temporal itself.
This reinforces that eternal attributes relate to temporal effects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: إن الفعل يتعدى إلى المفعول، وإذا ثبت أنه لا بد أن يتعدى إلى مفعول فلو وجد الفعل في الأزل لكان لا يخلو إما أن كان ما يتعدى إليه موجودا في الأزل أو كان معدما ، فإن كان موجودا فهو القول بقدم العالم، وإن كان معدوما ينبغي أن يكون المعدوم مفعولا. الجواب عنه أن نقول : عين هذا الكلام اعتراف منه أن الفعل غير المفعول لأنه زعم أن الفعل يتعدى إلى المفعول، والشيء يتعدى إلى غيره لا نفسه، فإن تعدي الشيء إلى نفسه محال، فإذا هذا الكلام حجة عليه. ثم نقول: الفعل يتعدى إلى المفعول في الجملة، فأما أن يتعدى إليه في الأحوال أجمع فهذا ليس بشرطه، ألا ترى أن الأمر متعد يقال : أمرته فأتمر ثم كان أمر الله تعالى للعالم بالوجود، وهو خطاب كن موجودا في الأزل وكان أمره الذي هو أمر إيجاب موجودا في الأزل ولا مأمور ولا وجوب، فكذا هذا لأنه ما كان أمرا بالوجود ليوجد في القدم بل ليوجد كل موجود في وقت وجوده وما كان أمرا ليجب على المعدوم في القدم بل ليجب على المكلفين وقت وجودهم وبلوغهم مبلغ توجه الخطاب، وكذا التكوين في الأزل ما كان ليكون المكون في الأزل بل ليكون وقت وجوده وكذا ما كانت إرادته ليكون مراده في الأزل بل ليكون كل مراد له وقت وجوده ثم يقال لهم: الله تعالى هل كان قادرا على العالم حال عدمه؟ فلابد من نعم فيكون معدوما مقدور الوجود، قلنا: وبعد وجوده هل هو قادر على عدمه ؟ فلابد من نعم قلنا: وهو يقدر على ذلك بقدرة حادثة أم بقدرة أزلية؟ فلابد من القول بقدرة أزلية، قلنا: تلك القدرة كانت في الأزل قدرة على عدم العالم؟ فإن قالوا نعم. فقد جعلوا قدرة على عدم المعدوم وهو محال وإن قالوا: هو قدرة على عدم الموجود. قلنا : وهل كان العالم في الأزل موجودا؟ فإن قالوا: نعم فقد وقعوا فيما نسبوا خصومهم إليه، وإن قالوا: لا. قلنا وكيف يكون في الأزل قدرة على عدم الموجود ولا موجود؟ فلابد من أن يقولوا كانت القدرة في الأزل قدرة على عدم الموجود وقت وجوده ، فكذا هذا لنا في الفعل.
They said: Verily, the act (al-fi‘l) extends to the object (al-maf‘ūl). And if it is established that it must extend to an object, then if the act existed in pre-eternity (al-azal), it would not be free either from that to which it extends being existent in pre-eternity or being non-existent (ma‘dūm). If it is existent, then that is the statement of the pre-eternity of the world. If it is non-existent, then the non-existent should be an object (maf‘ūl). The answer to it is that we say: This very statement is an admission from him that the act is other than the object, because he claimed that the act extends to the object, and a thing extends to other than itself, not to itself. For the extension of a thing to itself is impossible. So this statement is an argument against him. Then we say: The act extends to the object in general (fī al-jumla), but as for it extending to it in all states (fī al-aḥwāl ajma‘), that is not a condition of it. Do you not see that the command (al-amr) is transitive? It is said: 'I commanded him and he obeyed.' Then the command of Allah to the world for existence—which is the address 'Be, existing in pre-eternity'—and His command, which is a command of obligation, existed in pre-eternity while there was no commanded one (ma’mūr) nor obligation (wujūb). So likewise this [act] is like that, because it was not a command for existence in order that [the world] exist in pre-eternity, but rather that every existent exist at the time of its existence. And it was not a command in order that obligation be upon the non-existent in pre-eternity, but rather that obligation be upon the obligated persons (al-mukallafīn) at the time of their existence and their reaching the stage of being addressed (taklīf). And likewise, the bringing into existence (al-takwīn) in pre-eternity was not in order for the brought-into-existence (al-mukawwan) to be in pre-eternity, but rather to be at the time of its existence. And similarly, His will (irāda) was not that His object of will (murād) be in pre-eternity, but rather that everything willed by Him be at the time of its existence. Then it is said to them: Was Allah, exalted, powerful over the world in the state of its non-existence? They must answer 'yes.' So it is non-existent capable of being brought into existence (maqdūr al-wujūd). We say: And after its existence, is He powerful over its non-existence? They must answer 'yes.' We say: And does He have power over that by an originated power (qudra ḥāditha) or by an eternal power (qudra azaliyya)? They must answer by an eternal power. We say: Was that power in pre-eternity a power over the non-existence of the world? If they say 'yes,' then they have made it a power over the non-existence of the non-existent, which is impossible. And if they say: it is a power over the non-existence of the existent, we say: Was the world existent in pre-eternity? If they say 'yes,' they have fallen into what they attributed to their opponents. And if they say 'no,' we say: How can there be in pre-eternity a power over the non-existence of the existent when there is no existent? They must then say: The power in pre-eternity was a power over the non-existence of the existent at the time of its existence. So likewise for us regarding the act (al-fi‘l).
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair (shubha wa radd) regarding the relationship between God's eternal act of bringing into existence (takwin) and the temporal existence of created things. The objection argues: if the act (fi‘l) of bringing into existence existed in pre-eternity (al-azal), then its object (maf‘ūl) must also be pre-eternal, because an act necessarily extends to an object. If the object is pre-eternal, that entails the pre-eternity of the world (qidam al-‘ālam). If it is non-existent (ma‘dūm), then the non-existent would be an object, which is absurd. The answer begins by turning the objection back on the opponent: the very statement that 'the act extends to the object' implies that the act is other than the object, so the opponent admits that the act and object are distinct. Extension requires distinction; an act cannot extend to itself. Then the answer refines the notion of extension: acts extend to objects in a general way, but not necessarily in every state (ḥāl). Analogy is drawn to God's command (amr): God's eternal command 'Be' (kun) did not require a pre-eternal thing commanded (ma’mūr) or a pre-eternal obligation (wujūb), because the command's effect is realized at the time of its intended occurrence. Similarly, takwin (bringing into existence) in pre-eternity does not require the mukawwan (brought-into-existence) to be pre-eternal; rather, it is an eternal attribute that brings each thing into existence at its appointed time. The same applies to God's will (irāda). The answer then presents an independent argument using God's power (qudra). If God is powerful over the world when it is non-existent, and after its existence He is powerful over its non-existence, and this power is eternal, then the opponent must explain the relation of eternal power to temporal objects. If they say the power in pre-eternity is a power over non-existence of the world, that is power over the non-existent which is impossible. If they say it is power over non-existence of the existent, then the world must have been existent in pre-eternity, which is absurd. The only consistent position is that the power is a power over non-existence of the existent at the time of its existence. Thus, just as eternal power relates to temporal effects, so does eternal takwin relate to temporal created things without requiring pre-eternity of the effect.

المكون (al-mukawwan)
الفعل (al-fi‘l)
المفعول (al-maf‘ūl)
الأمر (al-amr)
القدرة (al-qudra)
الأزل (al-azal)
المعدوم (al-ma‘dūm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's eternal attributes (like takwin) require eternal effects.
Correction: The passage shows that divine attributes are eternal while their effects are temporal; the attribute relates to the effect at the time of its occurrence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the opponent's own statement about the act extending to the object imply?
A) The act and object are identical
B) The act is other than the object
C) The object must be pre-eternal
D) The non-existent cannot be an object

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute of God that brings each thing into existence at its proper time, not requiring the effect to be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray for something and do not see it happen immediately, do you truly believe that God's act of bringing it into existence is at the perfect time, even if that time is not your own? How will you cultivate patience rooted in this truth starting today?
?
Have you ever felt that God's power is somehow limited because the thing you desire does not yet exist? This lesson teaches that God's power relates to your situation at the appointed time. Are you willing to trust His timing even when it feels like nothing is happening?
?
The objection suggests that if God's act is eternal, then the world must be eternal. Reflect on your own life: do you sometimes think that if God has willed something, it must happen immediately? How does the analogy of the command 'Be' existing in pre-eternity without an immediate effect challenge your assumptions about God's action?

The Objection of Redundant Creation Answered
Nasafi refutes the claim that creation implies multiple powers and redundancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi response defends the distinction between divine power and creation against the charge of redundancy.

Core Idea
Creation is not redundant; it is the act of bringing existence, while power is potential.

Imam Nasafi now presents a second objection: if creation is a distinct attribute, does it not imply two powers or redundancy? The answer is sharp and rhetorical, but it points to a deeper distinction. Read carefully to see how the Maturidi position avoids the objection's trap.

Guided Path
1
Read the Objection
Read the first part of the passage carefully. Identify the two problems the objector raises: (1) equating creation with power leads to two powers, and (2) if power is all-encompassing, creation becomes superfluous.
The objector assumes creation must mean power, but the Maturidi position distinguishes them.
2
Identify the Core Charge
Note that the objection claims affirming a separate attribute of creation with no benefit is impermissible. This is a key theological principle: every attribute must have a function.
3
Read the Answer
Read the answer: the opponent is told his argument backfires. Think about how the objection, if applied consistently, could also undermine the opponent's own position.
The answer is terse but implies the objection conflates terms.
4
Reflect on the Distinction
Consider the Maturidi distinction: power is ability, creation is the act of bringing into existence. Why is that distinction necessary? How does it avoid redundancy?
Power alone does not entail actualization; creation is the actualizing attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما قال إن عند هؤلاء القوم أن المخلوق واقع بالخلق، فيلزمهم أن يكون الخلق بمعنى القدرة، فيلزم أن يكون له قدرتان، ولأن قدرة الباري إذا كانت شاملة لجميع المقدورات استغنى عن الخلق والإيجاد، ولا يجوز إثبات صفة الله تعالى لا فائدة فيها. يقال في جوابه: إنك رجل تهذي أبدا بما يعود ضرره عليك دون خصمك
And what he said: 'According to these people, the created thing (al-makhlūq) occurs through creation (al-khalq), so they must [hold] that creation (al-khalq) has the meaning of power (al-qudra), and thus they must [affirm] two powers for Him (qudratān). And because the power of the Creator (al-Bārī) if it encompasses all possible things (al-maqdūrāt), then creation (al-khalq) and bringing into existence (al-ījād) become superfluous, and it is not permissible to affirm an attribute of Allah, exalted, that has no benefit in it.' It is said in its answer: 'You are a man who always babbles with what brings harm back to you, not to your opponent.'
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage presents a second objection and its answer. The objection claims that if the Maturidi position holds that created things occur through an attribute called 'creation' (khalq) distinct from power (qudra), then this leads to two problems: (1) They must then say creation is the same as power, resulting in two powers (qudratān) for God. (2) Since God's power already encompasses all possible things, creation would be redundant (istighnā’); affirming an attribute without benefit is not permissible. The answer is brief and somewhat rhetorical: the opponent is accused of babbling in a way that harms himself, not his adversary. The full answer may continue in later text, but as presented here, it dismisses the objection as self-defeating. The core point is that the objection mistakenly equates creation with power, whereas the Maturidi position distinguishes them: creation is the attribute by which God brings things into existence, while power is the attribute of being able to do so. The objection's claim of redundancy is based on a conflation; if creation is a distinct attribute, its benefit is precisely to effect existence, which power alone might not imply (since power is about ability, not actualization). The answer implies the opponent's reasoning backfires.

Key Terms
الخلق (al-khalq)
القدرة (al-qudra)
المخلوق (al-makhlūq)
المقدور (al-maqdūr)
الإيجاد (al-ījād)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if God's power is all-encompassing, a separate attribute of creation is redundant and thus cannot exist.
Correction: The Maturidi position maintains that power is potential while creation is actualizing; they are distinct. An all-encompassing power does not make creation superfluous because power alone does not entail existence; creation is the attribute that brings existence about.

Checkpoint
What accusation does the objection make against the Maturidi position on creation?
A) It leads to belief in two gods
B) It makes creation identical to will
C) It implies two powers and makes creation redundant
D) It denies God's power altogether

Key Takeaway
The objection that creation is redundant fails because it conflates power (ability) with creation (act), a distinction the Maturidi position maintains.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that the opponent's objection was dismissed as babbling that harms the speaker, not the opponent. Think of a time you argued about religious matters more to win than to seek truth. Did your words bring benefit or harm to your own faith? Will you now commit to examining your motives before debating?
?
The passage distinguishes between power (potential) and creation (actual action). In your own life, where do you confuse intending to do good with actually doing it? What one good deed have you been postponing under the excuse of 'I have the ability'? Will you set a time today to turn that intention into action?

The Eternal Power of God and Its Relation to Creation
Dialectical argument proving eternal power relates to creation at time of existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dialectical argument demonstrates that God's eternal power is a power to create and annihilate at the time of existence, not in eternity.

Core Idea
Eternal power does not require an eternal creation.

This passage presents a sophisticated dialectical argument (jadal) defending the Sunni position that God's eternal attributes are not identical with their temporal effects. Through a series of leading questions, the author forces the opponent to admit that God's eternal power relates to creation at the time of existence, not in eternity. This resolves the apparent tension between an eternal Creator and a temporal world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the full translation. Notice the dialectical style of questions and answers.
The passage is a back-and-forth with an imaginary opponent.
2
Analyze the initial analogy
The author begins with an analogy: divine speech and takwin (bringing into existence) relate to their objects at the time of existence, not in eternity. Identify this point.
This sets the pattern for the discussion of power.
3
Follow the dialectical exchange on power
Track each question about God's power over the world: before existence, after existence, temporal vs eternal, and the implications. Note how the opponent is forced into a corner.
Pay attention to the logical moves and the absurdities avoided.
4
Grasp the final conclusion
The opponent must admit that eternal power was a power to annihilate the world at the time of its existence. By analogy, eternal power is a power to create at the time of creation, not in eternity.
This preserves both God's eternity and the world's temporality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توجه الخطاب، وكذا التكوين في الأزل ما كان ليكون المكون في الأزل بل ليكون وقت وجوده، وكذا ما كانت إرادته ليكون مراده في الأزل بل ليكون وقت وجوده. كل مراد له وقت وجوده. ثم يقال لهم: الله تعالى هل كان قادرا على العالم حال عدمه؟ فلابد من نعم، فيكون معدوما مقدور الوجود. قلنا: وبعد وجوده هل هو قادر على عدمه؟ فلابد من نعم. قلنا: وهو يقدر على ذلك بقدرة حادثة أم بقدرة أزلية؟ فلابد من القول بقدرة أزلية. قلنا: تلك القدرة كانت في الأزل قدرة على عدم العالم؟ فإن قالوا نعم فقد جعلوا قدرة على عدم المعدوم وهو محال. وإن قالوا: هو قدرة على عدم الموجود. قلنا: وهل كان العالم في الأزل موجودا؟ فإن قالوا نعم فقد وقعوا فيما نسبوا خصومهم إليه، وإن قالوا: لا. قلنا وكيف يكون في الأزل قدرة على عدم الموجود ولا موجود؟ فلابد من أن يقولوا كانت القدرة في الأزل قدرة على عدم الموجود وقت وجوده، فكذا هذا لنا في الفعل.
The addressing of discourse, and likewise [the attribute of] bringing into existence (al-takwin) in eternity, was not such that the brought-into-existence would be in eternity, but rather at the time of its existence. And likewise, His will was not such that its object would be in eternity, but rather at the time of its existence. Every object of His will has a time of its existence. Then it is said to them: Was God, exalted, powerful over the world at the time of its non-existence? They must answer yes, so it would be non-existent but possible of existence. We said: And after its existence, is He powerful over its non-existence? They must answer yes. We said: Does He have power over that by a temporal power or by an eternal power? They must affirm an eternal power. We said: Was that power in eternity a power over the non-existence of the world? If they say yes, then they have made it a power over the non-existence of the non-existent, which is impossible. And if they say: It is a power over the non-existence of the existent. We said: Was the world existent in eternity? If they say yes, then they have fallen into what they attributed to their opponents; and if they say no. We said: How could there be in eternity a power over the non-existence of the existent when there is no existent? So they must say that the power in eternity was a power over the non-existence of the existent at the time of its existence. Likewise this applies for us regarding the act.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument (jadal) defending the Ash'ari/Maturidi position that God's eternal attributes (such as power, will, and takwin) are not the same as the temporal act of creation. The author begins by stating that divine speech (al-khitab) and takwin (bringing into existence) in eternity were not such that the object of creation would be eternal; rather, they are related to the object at the time of its existence. Similarly, God's will is not such that its object is eternal, but rather at the time of existence. Each object of will has its specific time of existence. The author then engages in a series of questions with an imaginary opponent (likely the Mu'tazila) about God's power (qudra) over the world. He asks: Was God powerful over the world when it was non-existent? The opponent must say yes, making it a possible non-existent. After creation, is God powerful over its annihilation? Again yes. Is this power temporal or eternal? The opponent must admit it is eternal since no temporal power can arise in God. Then the author asks: Was this eternal power in eternity a power to annihilate the world? If yes, then it would be power to annihilate something non-existent, which is absurd. If they say it is power to annihilate the existent, then the author asks: Was the world existent in eternity? If yes, they fall into holding the eternity of the world (which they reject). If no, then how can there be power to annihilate an existent that does not exist? The opponent is forced to say: The eternal power was a power to annihilate the world at the time of its existence. Similarly, the author concludes, the eternal power is a power to create the world at the time of its existence, not in eternity. This establishes that God's eternal power does not necessitate an eternal creation; it is a power to create when God wills.

Key Terms
القدرة
الأزل
التكوين
الخلق
الإيجاد
المعدوم
المقدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's eternal power necessitates an eternal world.
Correction: The argument shows that eternal power can be directed at temporal effects, not requiring eternal effects.

Checkpoint
What conclusion does the author force the opponent to accept regarding God's eternal power over the non-existence of the world?
A) That the power was in eternity a power to annihilate the world at the time of its existence
B) That the power was in eternity a power to annihilate a non-existent thing
C) That the power was in eternity a power to annihilate an eternally existent world
D) That the power is temporal and not eternal

Key Takeaway
God's eternal power is a power to create and annihilate at the time of existence, not in eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's power is eternal but relates to you at every moment of your existence, do you truly live with the awareness that He is actively sustaining you right now? What one change would you make today to live in that reality?
?
The passage forces you to acknowledge that God's power is over your non-existence as well as your existence. Are you more afraid of losing something God has given you, or of failing to acknowledge His absolute control over your very being? How should that reshape your attachment to worldly things?
?
This lesson shows that God's will and power are not bound by time. When you delay repentance or obedience, are you assuming that God's power and will are somehow constrained by your timeline? What would it mean for you to act as if God's power is fully present and ready to respond to you at every moment?

Why Creation Needs Distinct Attributes: Refuting the Two Powers Objection
Refutation of the objection that creation implies two powers or redundancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari position affirms creation (khalq) as a distinct attribute from power, and how the refutation defends the necessity of multiple attributes in bringing the world into existence.

Core Idea
Power alone cannot create; distinct attributes explain divine freedom, order, and bringing existence from non-existence.

The author addresses a second objection from opponents who claim that if creation is by a separate attribute of khalq, then khalq would be identical to power, implying two powers, or that an all-encompassing power makes creation redundant. This lesson unpacks the layered refutation, showing how the author distinguishes between power, causing-to-occur, and bringing-into-existence, and why the act of creation is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objection claims that if the created thing occurs by khalq, then khalq must be power, leading to two powers; also, if power covers all possibles, creation is useless.
Notice the opponent's assumption that khalq and power are identical.
2
Examine the first refutation
The author argues that occurrence is not by power alone but by causing-to-occur (iqa') and bringing-into-existence (ijad). Power serves to make the agent free, will ensures order, knowledge ensures perfection.
3
Understand the second refutation
The non-existent does not come into existence merely by power over creation; it requires the specific act of ijad at the time God wills.
The author uses the example of the world: it was possible but non-existent until God brought it into being.
4
See the turning of the tables
The author points out that if occurrence were solely by power, the world would be eternal (since power is eternal), which is exactly what the opponents criticize.
This shows the absurdity of the opponent's position.
5
Reflect on the final argument
The author invokes the Qur'anic command 'Be' (kun) to show that even the opponents affirm a distinct creative act, so they cannot deny the need for khalq and ijad.
This ties the refutation back to Islamic scripture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه ثانية للخصوم
وما قال إن عند هؤلاء القوم أن المخلوق واقع بالخلق، فيلزمهم أن يكون الخلق بمعنى القدرة، فيلزم أن يكون له قدرتان، ولأن قدرة الباري إذا كانت شاملة لجميع المقدورات استغنى عن الخلق والإيجاد، ولا يجوز إثبات صفة لله تعالى لا فائدة فيها.
الرد عليها
يقال في جوابه: إنك رجل تهذي أبدا بما يعود ضرره عليك دون خصمك، ولا تدري بذلك لجهلك بالحقائق. أما قولك: إن المخلوق لو كان واقعا بالخلق فيكون الخلق قدرة. قلنا والوقوع متى يكون بالقدرة، الوقوع يكون بالإيقاع والوجود بالإيجاد والقدرة ليكون الفاعل في فعله مختارا غير مضطر، والإرادة ليخرج المفعول على التوالي والنظام، والعلم ليخرج على الإحكام. ثم إن هذا الكلام هو سخنة عينك، والمخيب لك في جميع سعيك، فإن وقوع العالم لو كان بالقدرة، والقدرة أزلية، ينبغي على زعمك أن يكون العالم أزليا، ليكون ما يتعلق وقوعه به أزليا فتقع في جميع ما عبت به خصمك. وكلامك الثاني: أن قدرة الباري جل وعلا إذا كانت شاملة لجميع المقدورات استغنى عن الخلق والإيجاد، ولا يجوز إثبات صفة لا فائدة فيها وباطل أيضا، لأن المعدوم لا يوجد بالقدرة على الإيجاد بدون الإيجاد، فإن العالم في حال عدمه كان مقدور الإيجاد ولا وجود له لأن الإيجاد لم يكن ليوجد للحال بل ليوجد عندما علم الله تعالى وجوده وأراد وجوده، فلم يقع بها الغنية عن الإيجاد والخلق، ثم هذا عليك، فإن الوقوع لما كان بالقدرة وقعت الغنية عن الخلق والإيجاد، فلماذا تجعله خالقا موجدا، وتجعل العالم مخلوقا موجدا؟ وأي فائدة في ذلك؟ وأي معنى تحت لفظة الخلق والإيجاد والمخلوق والموجد؟ وفيه أيضا ما مر من وجوب قدم الموجودات لما كان وجودها متعلقا بالقدرة، قدم ما يتعلق به وجود العالم يوجب قدم العالم. ثم نقول له: لما كان الوجود متعلقا بالقدرة لا غير، فأي فائدة في خطاب كن؟ ولأي معنى قال صاحبكم الأشعري بل جميع أصحابكم إن الله تعالى خلق جميع المخلوقات بخطاب كن؟ فأي عذر لك في ذلك، فهو عذري في الخلق والإيجاد.
A second objection of the opponents: And what he said: According to these people, the created thing occurs by the act of creation (al-khalq). So it would necessitate that al-khalq means power (al-qudra), and thus it would necessitate that He has two powers. And because if the power of the Creator encompasses all possibles, He would be independent of creation (al-khalq) and bringing into existence (al-ijad). And it is not permissible to affirm an attribute of God that has no benefit.
The refutation of it: It is said in response: You are a man who always babbles with what harms you, not your opponent, and you do not realize that due to your ignorance of realities. As for your saying: If the created thing occurs by al-khalq, then al-khalq would be power. We say: When does occurrence occur by power? Occurrence occurs by causing-to-occur (al-iqa') and existence by bringing-into-existence (al-ijad), and power is so that the agent in his act is free and not compelled, and will is so that the effect emerges sequentially and systematically, and knowledge is so that it emerges with perfection. Then indeed this speech is the heat of your eye and the disappointor in all your efforts, for if the occurrence of the world were by power, and power is eternal, then according to your claim the world should be eternal, so that what its occurrence is connected to would be eternal, and you would fall into all that you criticized your opponent for. And your second statement: That the power of the Creator, majestic and exalted, if it encompasses all possibles, He would be independent of creation and bringing-into-existence, and it is not permissible to affirm an attribute with no benefit, is also false, because the non-existent does not come into existence by power over bringing-into-existence without the act of bringing-into-existence. For the world in the state of its non-existence was possible of being brought into existence, and it had no existence because bringing-into-existence was not to bring it into existence at the present moment, but rather to bring it into existence when God knew its existence and willed its existence. So independence from bringing-into-existence and creation does not occur by it. Then this militates against you, for if occurrence were by power, then independence from creation and bringing-into-existence would occur. So why do you make Him a creator and bringer-into-existence, and make the world created and brought-into-existence? And what benefit is in that? And what meaning under the words creation, bringing-into-existence, created, and brought-into-existence? And in it also is what has passed: the necessity of the eternity of existents because their existence is connected to power; the eternity of what the existence of the world is connected to would necessitate the eternity of the world. Then we say to him: Since existence is connected to power alone, what benefit is in the command 'Be' (kun)? And for what meaning did your master al-Ash'ari—rather all your companions—say that God created all creations by the command 'Be'? So what excuse do you have in that? That is my excuse in [affirming] creation and bringing-into-existence.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a second objection raised by opponents (likely Mu'tazila or others) against the Ash'ari view that the created thing occurs by the attribute of creation (khalq). The author first presents the objection: if creation is by khalq, then khalq would be equated with power (qudra), implying two powers (one for power itself and one for creation). Moreover, if God's power encompasses all possibles, then there is no need for a separate act of creation and bringing-into-existence (ijad); affirming a useless attribute is invalid. The author then refutes this point by point. He begins with a rhetorical rebuke, accusing the objector of ignorance. Then he addresses the claim that occurrence is by power. He distinguishes: occurrence (wudu') occurs by causing-to-occur (iqa') and existence by bringing-into-existence (ijad). Power serves to make the agent free and not compelled; will ensures sequential order; knowledge ensures perfection. Thus power is not identical to the act of creation. The author then turns the objection back: if occurrence were solely by power, and power is eternal, then the world would be eternal (since what is related to an eternal cause would be eternal), which is the very view the opponents criticize. Next, he tackles the second part: the claim that if power is all-encompassing, then there is no need for creation. He argues that the non-existent (ma'dum) does not come into existence merely by power over creation without the act of creation; the world was possible but non-existent until God knew and willed its existence at a specific time. Thus power does not suffice without the act. He further points out that if occurrence were by power alone, then the act of creation would be redundant, and the terms 'creator' and 'created' would be meaningless. Finally, he raises an internal inconsistency: if existence is connected only to power, then the Qur'anic command 'Be' (kun) would be pointless, yet the opponents (Ash'aris) affirm that God creates by 'Be'. The author concludes that his own affirmation of separate attributes of creation and bringing-into-existence is justified.

Key Terms
الخلق
القدرة
الإيجاد
الإيقاع
كن
المعدوم
المقدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming separate attributes of creation and power implies multiple gods.
Correction: Each attribute has a distinct function: power ensures freedom, will ensures order, knowledge ensures perfection, creation brings into existence.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, why is power alone insufficient for bringing about the existence of the world?
A) Because power is temporal and cannot act on non-existence
B) Because the non-existent requires the act of bringing-into-existence (ijad) in addition to power
C) Because power is only for making the agent free, not for causing existence
D) Because the world is eternal and does not need creation

Key Takeaway
The creation of the world requires distinct divine attributes—power, will, knowledge, and the act of bringing-into-existence—because power alone cannot bring the non-existent into being without a specific act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever reduce God's actions to a single attribute, forgetting His wisdom and will? How does this lesson challenge you to see God's creative act as more than just power?
?
If you believed that God's power alone is enough, how would that affect your understanding of the Qur'anic command 'Be'? Do you take the words of the Qur'an seriously as real acts of God?
?
This passage shows that the opponent's view leads to the absurdity that the world is eternal. Have you ever held a view about God that, if followed logically, would lead to a contradiction with what you know from revelation? How can you guard against such reasoning?

Refuting the Identification of Creation with Power
Nasafi refutes the identification of creation with power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that creation (khalq) is distinct from power (qudra), and why identifying them leads to the absurd conclusion of the world's eternity.

Core Idea
Creation is not power — it requires bringing-into-existence, will, and knowledge.

In this passage, Nasafi responds to an opponent who claims that if a created thing occurs by creation, then creation must be power itself. Nasafi first clarifies the roles of power, will, and knowledge in bringing about existence, then turns the argument back on the opponent: if the world occurred by power alone, and power is eternal, the world would be eternal — a position the opponent himself rejects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Nasafi structures his refutation: he first quotes the opponent's claim, then responds, and finally gives a reductio ad absurdum.
The opponent's claim is in the first part: 'if the created were to occur by creation, then creation would be power.'
2
Identify the components of occurrence
Find where Nasafi lists what is needed for occurrence (wuqū'). He mentions bringing-about, existence, power, will, and knowledge. Note the specific Arabic terms: الإيقاع, الوجود, الإيجاد, القدرة, الإرادة, العلم.
Each component has a distinct function: power ensures volition, will ensures order, knowledge ensures precision.
3
Understand the reductio argument
Follow the logical consequence if occurrence were only by power: since power is eternal, the world would be eternal. This is exactly what the opponent criticizes in others, so his own position is self-refuting.
4
Reflect on the refutation
Think about why Nasafi emphasizes the distinct roles of attributes. This reinforces the Maturidi principle that divine attributes are not identical to each other or to the essence.
This lesson connects to broader discussions of divine attributes and causality in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما قولك : إن المخلوق لو كان واقعا بالخلق فيكون الخلق قدرة. قلنا والوقوع متى يكون بالقدرة، الوقوع يكون بالإيقاع والوجود ،بالإيجاد والقدرة ليكون الفاعل في فعله مختارا غير مضطر، والإرادة ليخرج المفعول على التوالي والنظام، والعلم ليخرج على الإحكام . ثم إن هذا الكلام هو سخنة عينك، والمخيب لك في جميع سعيك، فإن وقوع العالم لو كان بالقدرة، والقدرة أزلية، ينبغي على زعمك أن يكون العالم أزليا، ليكون ما يتعلق وقوعه به أزليا فتقع في جميع ما عبت به خصمك .
As for your statement: If the created were to occur by creation, then creation would be power. We say: Occurrence is when it is by power? Occurrence is by bringing-about and existence, by bringing-into-existence, and power so that the agent in his action is voluntary, not compelled; and will so that the effect comes out in succession and order; and knowledge so that it comes out with precision. Then this statement is the heat of your eye and the frustrater of all your effort, for if the occurrence of the world were by power, and power is eternal, then according to your claim the world should be eternal, so that what its occurrence is related to would be eternal, and thus you would fall into all that you criticized in your opponent.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage refutes a specific objection. The opponent claims that if the created occurs by creation (khalq), then creation is identical with power (qudra). Nasafi first distinguishes the concepts: occurrence (wuqu') is by bringing-about (īqā') and existence (wujūd) through bringing-into-existence (ījād), not by power alone. Power is to make the agent voluntary; will is to produce the effect in order; knowledge is for precision. Then he turns the argument: if the world's occurrence were by power, and power is eternal, the world would be eternal, which is absurd. Thus the opponent's position leads to the very error (claiming the world's eternity) that he criticizes in others.

Key Terms
الخلق (al-khalq)
القدرة (al-qudra)
الإيجاد (al-ījād)
الوقوع (al-wuqū')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that power (qudra) alone suffices for creation.
Correction: Nasafi insists that a distinct act of bringing-into-existence (ījād) is necessary, along with will and knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi in this passage, what is the consequence if the world's occurrence were by power alone?
A) The world would be temporal.
B) The world would be eternal.
C) Power would be temporal.
D) Creation would be unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
To avoid absurdity, creation must be understood as a distinct act of bringing-into-existence, not identical to power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever thought that God's power alone explains everything that happens, ignoring His will and knowledge? How does that simplification affect your trust in His perfect wisdom?
?
Nasafi says the opponent's claim is 'the heat of your eye and frustrater of all your effort.' Where in your own understanding of God might you be holding a view that, if pressed to its logical end, would contradict what you affirm?
?
If you truly believe that God's bringing-into-existence (ījād) is distinct from His power, how should that change the way you seek help from Him — do you ask only for His ability, or also for His will and wisdom to act in your life?

Why God’s Power Requires the Act of Creation
Nasafi refutes the claim that God's power eliminates need for creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that God's all-encompassing power does not eliminate the need for a distinct act of bringing-into-existence (ījād).

Core Idea
Power alone cannot turn non-existence into existence.

The opponent claims that an all-powerful God has no need for a separate act of creation. Nasafi responds by pointing out a crucial distinction: power is the ability to bring about an effect, but it does not automatically produce that effect without the specific act. In this passage, he explains why the non-existent remains non-existent until the divine act of ījād occurs at the time God wills.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Let the argument flow naturally.
Pay attention to the opponent's claim and Nasafi's refutation.
2
Identify the opponent’s argument
Find the sentence where the opponent states that God's power suffices without creation. Understand its logic: why would an all-encompassing power need a separate act?
3
Understand Nasafi’s refutation
Nasafi gives two reasons: (1) the non-existent does not come to exist by power alone without the act; (2) the world's existence was tied to a specific time when God knew and willed it. Work through each.
Notice that Nasafi uses the example of the world's non-existence.
4
See how Nasafi turns the argument
Nasafi then turns the opponent's logic against them: if power alone sufficed, then there would be no need for creation, yet they still call God 'Creator'. Ask why this is a problem for them.
5
Reflect on the additional implication
Consider the final point: if existence were related to power alone, it would entail the pre-eternity of the world—a conclusion the opponent would reject.
This connects to earlier discussions in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكلامك الثاني: أن قدرة الباري جل وعلا إذا كانت شاملة لجميع المقدورات استغنى عن الخلق والإيجاد، ولا يجوز إثبات صفة لا فائدة فيها وباطل أيضا، لأن المعدوم لا يوجد بالقدرة على الإيجاد بدون الإيجاد، فإن العالم في حال عدمه كان مقدور الإيجاد ولا وجود لما أن الإيجاد لم يكن ليوجد للحال بل ليوجد عندما علم الله تعالى وجوده وأراد وجوده، فلم يقع بها الغنية عن الإيجاد والخلق، ثم هذا عليك، فإن الوقوع لما كان بالقدرة وقعت الغنية عن الخلق والإيجاد، فلماذا تجعله خالقا ،موجدا، وتجعل العالم مخلوقا موجدا؟ و أي فائدة في ذلك؟ وأي معنى تحت لفظة الخلق والإيجاد والمخلوق والموجد؟ وفيه أيضا ما مر من وجوب قدم الموجودات لما كان وجودها متعلقا بالقدرة، قدم ما يتعلق به وجود العالم يوجب قدم العالم.
And your second statement: That the power of the Creator, exalted and majestic, if it encompasses all possibilities, would be free of need for creation and bringing-into-existence, and it is not permissible to affirm an attribute that has no benefit in it, and it is also false, because the non-existent does not come into existence by power over bringing-into-existence without the bringing-into-existence; for the world in its state of non-existence was possible of being brought into existence, and there was no existence because the bringing-into-existence was not to bring it into existence immediately, but to bring it into existence when Allah knew its existence and willed its existence; thus freedom from need for bringing-into-existence and creation does not occur through it. Then this [argument] is against you: for if occurrence were by power, freedom from need for creation and bringing-into-existence would occur; so why do you make Him a creator, a bringer-into-existence, and make the world created, brought into existence? And what benefit is there in that? And what meaning is there under the word creation and bringing-into-existence and the created and the brought-into-existence? And in it also is what has passed of the necessity of the pre-eternity of existents, since their existence is related to power—the pre-eternity of that to which the existence of the world is related necessitates the pre-eternity of the world.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage refutes the second objection: The opponent claims that since God's power (qudra) encompasses all possible things, there is no need for a separate attribute of creation (khalq) or bringing-into-existence (ījād); affirming such an attribute would be useless. Nasafi counters: The non-existent (ma'dūm) does not come into existence by power alone without the act of bringing-into-existence. The world, when non-existent, was possible of being brought into existence, but existence only occurred when God knew and willed it at a specific time. Thus power does not eliminate the need for ījād. He then turns the argument against the opponent: If occurrence were by power alone, then indeed there would be no need for creation, so why do they still affirm that God is a creator? He also notes the earlier point: if existence were related to power alone, it would entail the pre-eternity of the world, which is false.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra)
الإيجاد (al-ījād)
الخلق (al-khalq)
المعدوم (al-ma'dūm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An all-powerful God does not need to perform a distinct act of creation; power alone should be sufficient to bring things into existence.
Correction: Nasafi argues that power is the ability to bring about an effect, but it does not automatically produce existence without the specific act of bringing-into-existence (ījād), which occurs at the time God wills.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does God's power not suffice without bringing-into-existence (ījād)?
A) Because power is temporal.
B) Because the non-existent does not come into existence by power alone without the act.
C) Because bringing-into-existence is identical with power.
D) Because God's power is limited.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi teaches that God's power, though all-encompassing, does not eliminate the need for the divine act of bringing-into-existence, which occurs at the time of His willing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that because Allah is all-powerful, He will automatically give you what you need without you actively seeking Him? This passage reminds us that power alone does not bring about existence—there must be an act of creation and will. How does this challenge your passive reliance on God?
?
The opponent thought God's power made creation unnecessary. In your life, do you ever think that God's power makes your own efforts irrelevant? Reflect on how this passage emphasizes that God's power is exercised through active will and specific acts. How will you respond by increasing your own active seeking of Him?
?
The world only came to be when Allah knew and willed its existence. When you consider your own existence, do you appreciate that each moment you exist is because Allah actively wills it? How does this affect your gratitude and your sense of purpose?

The Redundancy of the Command 'Be'
Nasafi refutes the concept of khitāb kun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that the concept of a divine command 'Be' is either redundant or leads to an absurd multiplicity of powers.

Core Idea
If power suffices for creation, 'Be' adds nothing.

In this passage, Nasafi challenges the Ash'ari notion that Allah creates all things by uttering the command 'Be'. He demonstrates that if existence is solely related to divine power, then the command has no function; if it does have function, it implies an additional power, which is theologically problematic. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation to get a sense of Nasafi's rhetorical style and logical flow.
Notice the repeated rhetorical questions.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
Nasafi quotes the Ash'ari position that Allah created all creatures by the command 'Be'. Identify this claim in the text.
The opponent is al-Ash'ari and his followers.
3
Follow the first consequence
Nasafi argues that if existence is only related to power, the command 'Be' is useless. Ask yourself: why would the command be unnecessary?
4
Follow the second consequence
Nasafi then shows that if the command is effective, it must itself be a power, leading to two powers in God. Trace this reasoning.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
5
Reflect on the argument's significance
Consider how this argument preserves divine unity and simplicity. Why does it matter that God has only one power?
This connects to the core Islamic belief in tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول له: لما كان الوجود متعلقا بالقدرة لا غير، فأي فائدة في خطاب كن؟ ولأي معنى قال صاحبكم الأشعري بل جميع أصحابكم إن الله تعالى خلق جميع المخلوقات بخطاب كن؟ فأي عذر لك في ذلك، فهو عذري في الخلق والإيجاد، ثم ينبغي على قود كلامك أن يكون خطاب كن قدرة فيكون له تعالى قدرتان.
Then we say to him: Since existence is related to power alone, what benefit is there in the address 'Be'? And for what meaning did your master al-Ash'ari, rather all your companions, say that Allah created all creatures by the address 'Be'? So what excuse do you have in that? That is my excuse regarding creation and bringing-into-existence. Then, according to the consequence of your statement, the address 'Be' would be a power, and thus He would have two powers.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage presents a further argument against the opponent. Nasafi asks: If existence is related only to power (qudra), what purpose does the divine command 'Be' (kun) serve? The opponent (Ash'ari) and his followers claim that Allah creates by the command 'Be'. But if the opponent holds that occurrence is solely by power, then 'Be' is superfluous. Conversely, if they insist that 'Be' is effective, then it must be another power, implying two powers in God, which is problematic. Thus the opponent's position is self-contradictory.

Key Terms
خطاب كن (khitāb kun)
القدرة (al-qudra)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The command 'Be' is a separate act of creation distinct from God's power.
Correction: Nasafi shows that if 'Be' is effective, it must itself be a power, leading to multiple powers in God, which is absurd. Therefore 'Be' cannot be a separate act.

Checkpoint
What consequence does Nasafi draw from the opponent's view that the command 'Be' is used in creation?
A) The command 'Be' is identical with power.
B) The command 'Be' would be a second power, implying two powers in God.
C) The command 'Be' is unnecessary because power suffices.
D) The command 'Be' shows that creation is temporal.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi demonstrates that the theological concept of a command 'Be' is either superfluous or implies two powers, thus undermining divine unity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make du'a, do you sometimes feel that your words or rituals are the 'Be' that makes Allah act? What would it mean to trust that His power alone is enough, without any intermediary of your own making?
?
Is there a 'Be' in your understanding of how Allah provides, guides, or forgives—a step you add mentally that this lesson reveals as either redundant or a subtle form of shirk? What will you strip away starting today?
?
If you truly believed that nothing—no formula, no intermediary, no special phrase—adds to Allah's power, how would your worship change? What would you stop relying on that you have been treating as necessary?

The Opponent's Division and the Invention Objection
Nasafi presents and critiques the opponent's division and invention argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponent's division of possibilities for creation and why Nasafi dismisses the claim that invention through creation equates to power.

Core Idea
Creation and invention are synonyms; the opponent's claim about power is nonsense.

In this dense refutation, Nasafi first lays out the opponent's attempted division of what creation could be if it were distinct from the created. He then exposes a critical flaw: the opponent's claim that 'invention occurs through creation' is meaningless because creation and invention are the same reality. This lesson walks through that initial exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the division and initial response
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the opponent's trichotomy (in a locus, not in a locus, in God's essence) and the subdivision of the last option into originated or eternal.
The opponent excludes the impossible options to leave only one possibility.
2
Focus on the invention argument
Identify the opponent's claim that if invention occurs through creation, it is like power. Nasafi calls this 'obvious nonsense' because invention is identical to creation.
Nasafi lists synonyms: creation, invention, bringing-into-existence, bringing-about.
3
Understand the correction
Nasafi says the opponent should have said 'if existence occurs through it' instead of 'invention', but that was already refuted because existence comes from bringing-into-existence, not power.
This shows Nasafi's precise theological vocabulary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما قال : إن الخلق لو كان غير المخلوق إما أن يكون قائما بمحل أو لا في محل أو بذات الباري، ولو كان قائما بذات الباري، لا يخلو إما أن يكون محدثا أو أزليا . والأقسام كلها باطلة عندنا على ما نبين إلا ما قال إنه قائم بذات الباري وإنه أزلي، فما قال في إبطاله أن الاختراع إن حصل به فهو في معنى القدرة. هذيان ظاهر، كيف يقال يحصل الاختراع بالخلق القائم بذات الله تعالى والاختراع هو الخلق على ما بينا أن الخلق والاختراع والإيجاد والتكوين نظائر، وهي من الأسامي المترادفة، بل كان ينبغي أن يقول : إن حصل به الوجود فهو في معنى القدرة. وقد بينا أن هذا فاسد ، لأن الوجود يكون بالإيجاد لا بالقدرة. وما قال بعد فراغه عن إفساد هذه الأقسام بزعمه أن ببطلان هذه الأقسام ظهر أن الخلق ليس معنى زائدا على المخلوق. قلنا: وما انقسم إلى أقسام وظهر بطلان الأقسام سوى واحد منها، إنما يتعين ذلك أن لو كان في حد الإمكان، فأما إذا كان هو ساوى غيره في الامتناع فلم قلت إنه يتعين ؟ وأي فرق بينك وبين غيرك من الخصوم أن لو قال: لما ظهر بطلان الأقسام كلها تعين أن التكوين معنى وراء المكون وهو قائم لا في مكان كما قاله جماعة منكم، أو قال: هو حادث قائم بذات الباري كان قالت الكرامية؟ وذلك كله باطل. فكذا قولك باطل ودلائل امتناع كون التكوين راجعا إلى المكون قد مرت على الاستقصاء.
And what he said: That if creation were other than the created, it would either be subsisting in a locus, or not in a locus, or in the essence of the Creator; and if it were subsisting in the essence of the Creator, it would not be free from being either originated or eternal. All the divisions are false according to us, as we will explain, except what he said that it is subsisting in the essence of the Creator and that it is eternal. So what he said in invalidating it is that if invention occurs through it, it is in the meaning of power. Obvious nonsense! How can it be said that invention occurs by the creation that subsists in the essence of Allah, while invention is creation, as we have explained that creation, invention, bringing-into-existence, and bringing-about are synonyms, and they are among synonymous names. Rather he should have said: If existence occurs through it, it is in the meaning of power. And we have already explained that this is corrupt, because existence occurs by bringing-into-existence, not by power. And what he said after finishing invalidating these divisions, claiming that by the invalidity of these divisions it became clear that creation is not an additional meaning to the created. We say: What was divided into divisions and the invalidity of divisions became apparent except one of them, that would be determined only if it were within the bounds of possibility. But if it equals others in impossibility, why do you say it is determined? And what difference is there between you and other opponents if someone said: When the invalidity of all divisions became apparent, it is determined that bringing-about is a meaning behind the brought-about, and it is subsisting not in a place, as said by a group of you, or said: it is originated subsisting in the essence of the Creator, as the Karramiyya said? All that is false. So too your statement is false, and the proofs of the impossibility of bringing-about being reducible to the brought-about have already passed in detail.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage refutes the opponent's argument that creation (khalq) is not a distinct attribute from the created (makhluq). The opponent divides possibilities: if creation is other than the created, it must either subsist in a locus, not in a locus, or in God's essence; if in God's essence, it is either originated or eternal. He claims that all divisions are false except the one he chooses (creation subsisting in God's essence and eternal). Then he says that if invention (ikhtirā') occurs through it, it is like power. Nasafi dismisses this as nonsense: invention is creation, and these terms are synonymous. He points out that the opponent should have said 'if existence occurs through it, it is like power', but that was already refuted because existence is by ījād, not power. Then the opponent concludes that since all but one division are false, creation is not an additional meaning. Nasafi counters: if the remaining division is as impossible as the others, it is not determined. He gives analogies: others might claim that bringing-about (takwīn) is a distinct meaning subsisting not in a place (as some Ash'aris say) or originated in God's essence (as Karramiyya say), but those are also false. Thus the opponent's argument is invalid, and the proofs that takwīn is not reducible to the mukawwan have already been fully given.

Key Terms
الخلق
المخلوق
الاختراع
الإيجاد
التكوين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that invention and creation are distinct, and that creation can be a means of invention.
Correction: Nasafi insists that creation, invention, ījād, and takwīn are synonymous; there is no distinction.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does he say invention is?
A) A synonym for power
B) A synonym for creation
C) A distinct attribute
D) An act of the created

Key Takeaway
The opponent's claim that invention through creation equates to power is invalid because invention and creation are identical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The opponent assumed invention through creation is like power, but Nasafi called it nonsense. Have you ever held a belief about Allah that, upon closer examination, turned out to be based on a faulty analogy? What was it, and what will you do to ensure your 'aqeedah is sound?
?
Nasafi emphasizes that creation and invention are synonyms. When you say 'Allah creates,' do you truly mean that He brings into existence from nothing, or do you unconsciously mix in human ideas of making? How can you train your heart to purify your understanding of Allah's attributes?
?
This passage is a reminder that even learned scholars can err in their reasoning about Allah. In your own learning, do you humbly accept correction when your understanding is shown to be flawed? Or do you cling to familiar but incorrect ideas? Commit to one specific change in how you seek knowledge.

Refuting the Conclusion that Creation is Not Additional
Nasafi refutes the opponent's final deduction by showing the remaining possibility is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi rejects the opponent's conclusion that creation is not an additional meaning, using the argument that the remaining division is impossible like the others.

Core Idea
Just because one division remains doesn't make it true; it may be impossible too.

After dismantling the opponent's arguments about invention, Nasafi turns to the opponent's final deduction: since all but one division are false, creation cannot be an additional meaning. Nasafi counters with a powerful logical move: the remaining division might be as impossible as the others, so no conclusion follows. He draws parallels to other theological positions to highlight the absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's conclusion
The opponent claims that after invalidating all but one division, it is proven that creation is not an additional meaning. Read carefully.
Note the opponent's logic: elimination of alternatives leads to truth of the remainder.
2
Nasafi's counter-argument
Nasafi says that the remaining division must be possible to be determined. If it is as impossible as the others, it cannot be chosen.
This is a key epistemological point about the method of division.
3
Analogy with other sects
Nasafi gives examples: others might claim takwīn is a distinct meaning subsisting not in a place (Ash'aris) or originated in God's essence (Karramiyya). Both are false, so the opponent's claim is similarly unfounded.
The point is that multiple contradictory conclusions can be drawn from the same refutation of divisions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما قال : إن الخلق لو كان غير المخلوق إما أن يكون قائما بمحل أو لا في محل أو بذات الباري، ولو كان قائما بذات الباري، لا يخلو إما أن يكون محدثا أو أزليا . والأقسام كلها باطلة عندنا على ما نبين إلا ما قال إنه قائم بذات الباري وإنه أزلي، فما قال في إبطاله أن الاختراع إن حصل به فهو في معنى القدرة. هذيان ظاهر، كيف يقال يحصل الاختراع بالخلق القائم بذات الله تعالى والاختراع هو الخلق على ما بينا أن الخلق والاختراع والإيجاد والتكوين نظائر، وهي من الأسامي المترادفة، بل كان ينبغي أن يقول : إن حصل به الوجود فهو في معنى القدرة. وقد بينا أن هذا فاسد ، لأن الوجود يكون بالإيجاد لا بالقدرة. وما قال بعد فراغه عن إفساد هذه الأقسام بزعمه أن ببطلان هذه الأقسام ظهر أن الخلق ليس معنى زائدا على المخلوق. قلنا: وما انقسم إلى أقسام وظهر بطلان الأقسام سوى واحد منها، إنما يتعين ذلك أن لو كان في حد الإمكان، فأما إذا كان هو ساوى غيره في الامتناع فلم قلت إنه يتعين ؟ وأي فرق بينك وبين غيرك من الخصوم أن لو قال: لما ظهر بطلان الأقسام كلها تعين أن التكوين معنى وراء المكون وهو قائم لا في مكان كما قاله جماعة منكم، أو قال: هو حادث قائم بذات الباري كان قالت الكرامية؟ وذلك كله باطل. فكذا قولك باطل ودلائل امتناع كون التكوين راجعا إلى المكون قد مرت على الاستقصاء.
And what he said: That if creation were other than the created, it would either be subsisting in a locus, or not in a locus, or in the essence of the Creator; and if it were subsisting in the essence of the Creator, it would not be free from being either originated or eternal. All the divisions are false according to us, as we will explain, except what he said that it is subsisting in the essence of the Creator and that it is eternal. So what he said in invalidating it is that if invention occurs through it, it is in the meaning of power. Obvious nonsense! How can it be said that invention occurs by the creation that subsists in the essence of Allah, while invention is creation, as we have explained that creation, invention, bringing-into-existence, and bringing-about are synonyms, and they are among synonymous names. Rather he should have said: If existence occurs through it, it is in the meaning of power. And we have already explained that this is corrupt, because existence occurs by bringing-into-existence, not by power. And what he said after finishing invalidating these divisions, claiming that by the invalidity of these divisions it became clear that creation is not an additional meaning to the created. We say: What was divided into divisions and the invalidity of divisions became apparent except one of them, that would be determined only if it were within the bounds of possibility. But if it equals others in impossibility, why do you say it is determined? And what difference is there between you and other opponents if someone said: When the invalidity of all divisions became apparent, it is determined that bringing-about is a meaning behind the brought-about, and it is subsisting not in a place, as said by a group of you, or said: it is originated subsisting in the essence of the Creator, as the Karramiyya said? All that is false. So too your statement is false, and the proofs of the impossibility of bringing-about being reducible to the brought-about have already passed in detail.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage refutes the opponent's argument that creation (khalq) is not a distinct attribute from the created (makhluq). The opponent divides possibilities: if creation is other than the created, it must either subsist in a locus, not in a locus, or in God's essence; if in God's essence, it is either originated or eternal. He claims that all divisions are false except the one he chooses (creation subsisting in God's essence and eternal). Then he says that if invention (ikhtirā') occurs through it, it is like power. Nasafi dismisses this as nonsense: invention is creation, and these terms are synonymous. He points out that the opponent should have said 'if existence occurs through it, it is like power', but that was already refuted because existence is by ījād, not power. Then the opponent concludes that since all but one division are false, creation is not an additional meaning. Nasafi counters: if the remaining division is as impossible as the others, it is not determined. He gives analogies: others might claim that bringing-about (takwīn) is a distinct meaning subsisting not in a place (as some Ash'aris say) or originated in God's essence (as Karramiyya say), but those are also false. Thus the opponent's argument is invalid, and the proofs that takwīn is not reducible to the mukawwan have already been fully given.

Key Terms
التكوين
المكون
الكرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if all but one logical division are eliminated, the remaining must be true.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the remaining division may be impossible as well, so no true conclusion follows.

Checkpoint
What condition does Nasafi say is necessary for the remaining division to be determined?
A) That it is equal to the others in impossibility
B) That it is within the bounds of possibility
C) That it is supported by revelation
D) That it is chosen by majority

Key Takeaway
The opponent's conclusion is invalid because the remaining possibility is as impossible as the others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there any beliefs you hold about God's attributes simply because all other options seem false, without honestly checking whether your chosen belief is truly possible? What would it take to examine that belief with both reason and revelation today?
?
Nasafi showed that a clever method (division) can lead to false conclusions if the remaining option is impossible. In your own spiritual life, is there a 'remaining option' you cling to—like assuming God will forgive you because other outcomes are unbearable—that may not be realistically possible? How can you align your hope with truth, even if uncomfortable?
?
The opponent used his reasoning to defend a false claim about creation. Have you ever used a seemingly logical argument to justify a position that contradicts clear scripture or sound reason? What safeguard can you establish to prevent your own reasoning from leading you astray, and what step will you take today to implement it?
